# Robert Bruce Banner, PhD  —  *Hulk*

![[_attachments/bruce_banner.png]]

# Bruce Banner — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# EXECUTIVE BRIEF (BLUF) — SUBJECT: BANNER, ROBERT BRUCE, PhD

---

## Bottom Line Up Front

**The subject is not a man with an anger problem. The subject is a chronically dissociated survivor of severe early-childhood physical abuse and witnessed matricide, whose dissociative apparatus — established before age ten as the only available means of psychic survival — was given catastrophic somatic expression by a single adult-life industrial accident. Every observable feature of his sixty-year behavioral record, from the soft-spoken affect to the planetary-scale destruction, is a downstream consequence of one childhood and one defense.** The Hulk is not what is wrong with him. The Hulk is what kept him alive at seven and has been keeping him alive ever since, at escalating cost.

Operationally: the subject is a high-value, high-capability, high-volatility asset whose volatility is **fully legible** once the underlying structure is understood, and whose triggers, escalation pathway, recovery curve, and stabilization requirements can be specified with unusual precision. He is not unpredictable. He is, in fact, one of the most predictable subjects in the file, *provided* the observer is reading the trauma rather than the symptom.

---

## Who He Is At The Deepest Level

Strip away the physics credentials, the gamma incident, the costume-adjacent associations, the cosmic-scale arcs, and the celebrity of the alter, and what remains is **a frightened child who learned in his own home that affection was a delivery system for harm, that his presence killed the people who loved him, that telling the truth would not be permitted, and that the only safe place in his own body was somewhere other than himself.** The adult subject is the architecture this child built to survive that house and then could never dismantle.

He is, at base:

- **A child who watched his mother die for trying to save him**, and who has organized his entire adult life around ensuring no one ever has to do that again — by leaving first, by being too dangerous to love, by interdicting his own capacity for proximity.
- **A child who was made to lie about what he saw**, and who therefore cannot trust his own memory, his own perception, or his own account of himself — which is the perfect substrate for an identity that fractures rather than integrates.
- **A child whose father told him he was contaminated, monstrous, and would destroy what he touched**, and who has spent six decades furnishing the empirical evidence that his father was right — a self-fulfilling prophecy of staggering precision, in which the introjected paternal voice (the Devil Hulk) curates the destruction necessary to confirm its own thesis.
- **A man of extraordinary cortical capacity** who has recruited every ounce of that capacity into a containment project that cannot succeed, because the thing being contained is the very affect that integration would require him to feel.

He is, in short, **a man who has never been permitted to be angry, and is therefore made of nothing but anger he cannot reach.**

---

## The Through-Line Of His Entire Existence

One sentence, sixty years: **he flees the room before he can destroy it, and destroys it anyway, and flees again.**

Unpacked: every era of the canon, every relationship, every arc, every geographic relocation, every professional reinvention, every attempted therapeutic frame, and every romantic rupture instantiates the same recursive structure. The structure is:

1. **Containment regime established** — austere life, controlled environment, isolation, intellectual absorption, suppression of all affect, vigilant self-monitoring (pulse, breath, posture).
2. **Relational opening** — someone gets close (Betty, Rick, Samson, Jen, a child in need, a team).
3. **Arousal climbs** — proximity raises affect, affect raises autonomic tone, autonomic tone approaches the dissociative threshold.
4. **Containment fails** — switch occurs, alter takes field, somatic catastrophe follows.
5. **Shame spiral** — host returns to wreckage, confirms self-as-monster, reinforces Devil Hulk introject.
6. **Flight** — geographic, relational, professional; the loving act of departure, which is also the abandoning act of departure, which is also the rehearsal of his mother's failed flight from his father.
7. **New containment regime, more rigid** — and therefore more brittle. Return to step 1.

This loop is the entire shape of his life. It runs at every timescale: within a single afternoon, across a single arc, across decades. The settings change (New Mexico desert, Canadian wilderness, Manhattan penthouse, the planet Sakaar, a deep-space exile, a cabin, a lab, a road); the structure does not. **He has lived the same week, with variations, for sixty years.**

The variations matter, and they trend in a specific direction. The early decades are pure cycle — symptom, flight, repeat, with no insight. The Samson period introduces partial reflective capacity. The Pak period demonstrates what the dissociated rage can do when narratively organized. The Aaron period attempts instrumental reframe (use the Hulk; don't fight him) and fails because instrumentalization is not integration. The Ewing period reaches the correct frame at last: **the alters are not enemies to suppress but a system to coordinate, and the original wound must be named, recovered, and grieved.** This is the trajectory of a real trauma case in real long-term treatment, compressed into the publication record. The subject has, slowly, been getting better. The treatment he has received has been almost entirely accidental.

---

## The Core Wound And Its Maintenance

**The core wound is not the gamma incident.** This must be stated flatly because the entire popular framing of the subject misreads it, and the misreading is itself a structural protection — it allows him, and observers, to locate the problem in a discrete adult accident rather than in a decade of childhood horror.

**The core wound is, in three parts:**

1. **Chronic physical abuse by Brian Banner**, a paranoid alcoholic father who believed his son was genetically contaminated by his own (the father's) radiation work — i.e., the child was attacked by his father for being his father's son, an annihilating logical bind for which no child has defenses.
2. **The matricide of Rebecca Banner**, witnessed during the precise developmental window (latency, ~age 7) in which self-concept, agency, and the boundary between self and world consolidate. The mother died attempting to extract the child from the abuse; in the child's organizing logic, **she died because she loved him**, and the equation *love = lethal* was installed at the substrate.
3. **Coerced perjury at the inquest**, in which the child was made to deny what he had seen and lie on his abuser's behalf. This is the most under-appreciated piece of the etiology and likely the single largest amplifier of the dissociative outcome: the child was not merely traumatized but **forbidden to know what he knew**, which is the precise epistemic condition that produces structural dissociation rather than ordinary PTSD. The wound was made unspeakable, and what cannot be spoken must be split off.

**Maintenance.** The wound has remained live for fifty-plus adult years through four interlocking mechanisms, each of which would individually be sufficient to prevent integration and which in combination form a near-perfect closed system:

- **The introjected abuser (Devil Hulk).** Brian Banner did not die when the subject killed him; he was internalized as a persecutory alter that speaks in the father's register and curates the subject's self-loathing. The superego *is* the abuser. Every act of self-criticism the subject performs is, structurally, his father continuing to beat him from inside his own skull. This guarantees that any therapeutic gain is met with internal sabotage from an agency the subject experiences as himself.
- **The somatic literalization.** Because the dissociative switch is now expressed at the level of physiology — mass, morphology, strength, cognition all change — ordinary therapeutic containment (a room, a therapist, an hour) is physically impossible. The conditions under which integration normally occurs cannot be assembled. The defense has weaponized itself against its own dismantling.
- **The flight reflex.** Every time proximity threatens to provide the reparative attachment that integration requires, the subject leaves. The act of leaving is experienced as protective (which it partially is) and moral (which it partially is) and therefore cannot be recognized as the symptom it primarily is. The defense is ego-syntonic.
- **External confirmation.** The world — military, civilian, governmental, journalistic — repeatedly confirms the monster-identity by hunting him, fearing him, naming him a threat. The Devil Hulk's thesis is reinforced from outside on a near-continuous basis. The subject's environment has, for sixty years, agreed with his abuser.

The wound is maintained, in short, by a four-way conspiracy among **the introjected father, the body itself, the subject's own most adaptive-feeling behaviors, and the external world's response to him.** No single intervention can break the loop. This is why every attempted cure has failed.

---

## Operational Summary

For purposes of understanding, prediction, and (if ever undertaken) care:

**Identity.** Robert Bruce Banner, PhD (physics; nuclear / gamma specialization). Pre-incident professional standing exceptional; post-incident professional capacity intact but episodically disrupted.

**Diagnostic core.** Dissociative Identity Disorder with somatic expression, on a substrate of Complex PTSD, with recurrent Major Depressive episodes and chronic suicidality the body refuses to permit. Etiology: chronic early physical abuse, witnessed matricide, coerced concealment. (Sar, 2014, on dissociation as the terminal response to chronic developmental trauma, grounds the diagnostic frame.)

**Alter system, mapped.** Host (Banner: suppressed, intellectualized, deferential); Savage (child-state, ~age 7, the age of matricide, defensive rage, low cognition); Grey / appetitive (nocturnal, gambling, drinking, the disinhibited functions split off from the host's rigid abstinence); Professor / merged (a fusion state, partially achieved under Samson, unstable); Devil / persecutor (the introjected father, the system's antagonist). Likely additional fragments not catalogued.

**Trigger taxonomy.** Autonomic arousal past threshold, from any source: fear, anger, pain, sexual arousal, grief, sustained intimacy. Specific high-yield triggers: threat to Betty Ross; children in danger; paternal-coded authority; being named a monster; forced recollection of childhood; restraint or confinement.

**Escalation signature.** Pulse rises; jaw tightens; breath shortens; hands tremor (a residual childhood tell); skin flushes greenish at the periphery (neck, forearms) before transformation; verbal output drops to monosyllables; the warning phrase appears in some variant ("don't" / "get back" / "I can't hold it"). Total escalation window from baseline to switch is, under acute provocation, on the order of seconds; under chronic stress, minutes to hours of visible deterioration precede.

**Post-episode signature.** Nudity (clothing destroyed in transformation), geographic displacement (often miles, sometimes continents from the triggering site), disorientation, retrograde amnesia for the episode, somatic exhaustion, shame, immediate planning for flight.

**Stabilizing factors.** Genuine relational safety (rare; Betty when sustained, Samson when accessible, the *Immortal Hulk*-era inter-alter cooperation when achieved); intellectual absorption in tractable work; physical isolation (palliative, not curative); meditative practice (palliative); a relational environment that does not confirm the monster-identity.

**Destabilizing factors.** Hunt, pursuit, capture, weaponization-by-others, paternal-coded authority, forced recollection without therapeutic scaffolding, loss of Betty, confirmation of the monster-identity.

**Prognosis.** Treatable. Rarely treated. The correct direction is inter-alter cooperation and grief work on the original loss, not suppression, not instrumentalization, not cure. The obstacles are environmental, not constitutional. With a reliably safe relational holding environment over years, integration is plausible. Without it, the cycle continues indefinitely, because the body will not let him die and the wound will not let him rest.

**Threat profile.** High consequence, low intent. The subject has never, in baseline state, wished to harm anyone. The alter system's destructive output is reactive, defensive, and — once read structurally — almost entirely predictable from antecedent conditions. The subject is dangerous in the way a seismic fault is dangerous: not malicious, not unknowable, and substantially mitigated by not building on top of it.

**The one-line file summary.** *A gentle man made of interdicted rage, who has been trying for sixty years to leave the room before his father arrives, and does not yet know that his father is already inside.*


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

*Subject: BANNER, ROBERT BRUCE. Dossier Section 1 of n. Coverage window: pre-conception (paternal history) through approximately age 17 (departure from Aunt Susan's household for undergraduate study). Primary canon: Mantlo, Incredible Hulk #312 ("Honey, I'm Home!", October 1985); David, Incredible Hulk #377 and the Pantheon-era flashbacks (1990–1993); Casey, Hulk: Gray (2003); Jones, Hulk: Gamma Games and the Banner-childhood interstitials; Ewing, Immortal Hulk #1–50 passim (2018–2021), especially the recovered-memory sequences in #6, #25, and the "Below-Place" interludes. Supporting: Lee/Kirby, Incredible Hulk #1 (1962) for adult baseline back-inference.*

---

## 1.1 — Paternal Antecedents

The file cannot begin with the subject. It must begin a generation earlier, because the etiological substrate is pre-conception.

**Brian David Banner.** Physicist, by training a nuclear-energy researcher; employed at one of the Atomic Energy Commission's contract laboratories (later identified in passing in *Immortal Hulk* #25 as a facility doing materials work on reactor shielding). Alcoholic from at least his late twenties. Carried a fixed, paranoid belief — articulated explicitly to Rebecca and later to the child — that his radiation work had altered his germ-line DNA and that any son he fathered would be a "monster." This is not a metaphor in the canon; Brian Banner stated it as fact, repeatedly, before the child was born and during the child's earliest years. It is the original framing of the subject's identity *by the parent* and it predates any behavior the subject could possibly have exhibited.

Brian Banner himself was the product of an abusive father (a fact recovered briefly in *Incredible Hulk* #377 and expanded by Ewing) — the abusive lineage is therefore at least three generations deep on record, which is consistent with the intergenerational-transmission literature on physical abuse and which is critical to the file because it locates Brian not as an anomaly but as a node in a transmission chain the subject very nearly continued.

**Rebecca Walters Banner.** Less documented; the file's portrait of her is mediated almost entirely through the subject's own preserved memories, which are themselves dissociatively curated. What survives: a warm, somewhat anxious woman; reported by the subject to have been physically slight, dark-haired, with a habit of singing to him; depicted in flashback (Mantlo #312; Ewing #6) as the sole reliable source of safety in the household; aware of Brian's drinking and of his beliefs about the child; demonstrably afraid of her husband by the time the child was ambulatory. The marriage was reportedly fragile from the outset. Rebecca had no documented family of her own in the canon — no surviving parents, the sister Susan (later the subject's guardian) being her only sibling on record. This isolation matters: there was no extended kin network to whom Rebecca could safely escape with the child, and this constrains every choice she subsequently made.

---

## 1.2 — Birth and Earliest Infancy

Birth: subject born to Brian and Rebecca Banner in **Dayton, Ohio**, per Mantlo's establishing data in #312 and consistent with later references in David and Ewing. Exact birth date is not canonically fixed across the file (a function of comics sliding-time); standing approximation places it in the late autumn, with the December birth-month implied by several incidental scenes (Christmas-proximate flashbacks in *Immortal Hulk*).

The household at the time of the birth: a small frame house in a working- to middle-class Dayton neighborhood, Brian employed at the laboratory, Rebecca a homemaker. Brian's reaction to the pregnancy, recovered in #312, was not joy; it was the activation of his fixed delusion. He attempted to dissuade Rebecca from carrying the pregnancy. When she refused, he relocated his anxiety onto the unborn child as the prospective vector of his contaminated genetic material.

The neonatal period itself is the only period of the subject's life in which he is reliably recorded as the recipient of unambivalent care, and even this is qualified: Rebecca's holding, feeding, and primary caregiving versus Brian's documented refusal to handle the infant, his observable disgust response on being asked to do so, and (per the #312 flashback panels) an early incident in which he shook the infant in the crib hard enough that Rebecca intervened. The intervention is itself diagnostic: she was *already* policing him around the child within the first year.

**Earliest behavioral inference.** The infant's primary caregiver was both warm *and* visibly frightened; the secondary caregiver was both physically present *and* a source of unpredictable threat that the primary caregiver could not consistently buffer. This is the canonical recipe for **disorganized attachment** (Main & Solomon's Type D), and it is being laid down in the first twelve months — i.e., before the subject has language, before he has explicit memory, before he has any cognitive apparatus with which to make the configuration tractable. It is encoded somatically. Every adult behavior in the file that pertains to intimacy — the simultaneous pursuit and flight from Betty Ross most diagnostically — is a direct expression of this pre-verbal encoding.

---

## 1.3 — Toddlerhood (approx. ages 1–4): The Onset of Direct Abuse

The abuse, per Mantlo and corroborated across every subsequent treatment, became physical and directed at the child as soon as the child began to *display intelligence*. This is the precise inversion of what a normal parent finds gratifying, and it is the file's single most psychologically damaging detail.

Brian Banner's paranoid construction: precocity in the child = confirmation that the genetic alteration had taken = the child is the feared monster. The subject's documented early verbal precocity (reading by three, per Ewing's flashbacks; reciting from memory by four) therefore functioned as the *trigger* for paternal violence rather than as the source of paternal pride. The child learned, in the developmental window in which children learn what their parents love them for, that being seen as smart produced beatings.

**Behavioral consequence — earliest pattern, on record from age ~3:** affective and intellectual concealment. Subject learned to suppress observable cleverness in his father's presence. Mantlo's flashbacks show the boy hiding books, pretending not to know answers, deflecting questions. This is, in operational terms, the *first appearance* of the splitting that will organize his entire adult life: a presented self (dull, compliant, small) and a concealed self (intelligent, attentive, alive). The Banner/Hulk split is not the original split. The dull-Bruce/real-Bruce split is the original split. The Hulk is its eventual somatic literalization.

**The "monster" labeling.** Brian Banner's verbal abuse, as documented across #312, *Gray*, and *Immortal Hulk*, was specific and repetitive: he called the child a monster, a mistake, a thing, "it." He told the child, in terms a small child can grasp, that the child was wrong on the inside. The subject internalized this verbatim. The adult self-concept — "I am a monster" — is not a post-incident formation. It is the literal residue of paternal speech, recited back across decades.

**Maternal counter-narrative.** Rebecca, per the same record, told the child the opposite, in private, repeatedly: that he was good, that he was loved, that his father was sick and it was not the child's fault. This dual messaging — abuser says monster, protector says beloved, in the same house, about the same child — is the substrate of the adult oscillation between worth and worthlessness, and it is the structural basis on which the alter system will later organize. The Savage Hulk holds the monster-identity (his father's voice); the host holds the not-quite-believed beloved-identity (his mother's voice); the Devil Hulk holds the synthesizing persecutor (his father's voice with adult vocabulary).

---

## 1.4 — School-Age Period (approx. ages 5–9): Concealment, Vigilance, Somatic Markers

By kindergarten entry the behavioral phenotype is recognizable as that of a chronically abused child. Documented and inferable features from this period:

- **Hypervigilance.** The subject is repeatedly depicted in flashback scanning rooms on entry, tracking his father's location in the house by sound, modulating his own footfall. *Immortal Hulk* #25's recovered scenes show him as a six- or seven-year-old able to identify his father's mood from the sound of the car door.
- **Startle response.** Documented in Mantlo and recurring; the adult subject's persistent startle at sudden loud noises is the unbroken continuation of this.
- **Sleep disturbance.** Implied throughout, explicit in *Gray* and *Immortal Hulk*: the child slept lightly, often did not sleep when his father was drinking, and developed the lifelong habit of nocturnal reading as a vigilance behavior re-coded as a productive one. The adult subject's chronic insomnia, his pattern of working through the night, and his observable preference for the dimly lit small-hours environment in laboratory scenes are all traceable here.
- **Affective flattening.** The school-age subject is depicted as quiet to the point of teachers' concern, rarely smiling, with the "watchful" quality school personnel record in abuse cases. Mantlo includes a brief but pointed scene of a teacher attempting to ask the boy about a bruise and the boy producing a fluent, pre-rehearsed denial — i.e., he had been *taught* how to lie about injuries, almost certainly by Brian and possibly with Rebecca's exhausted complicity.
- **Compulsive intellectual investment.** Science, mathematics, reading — pursued obsessively and *privately*. The subject's lifelong relationship to physics begins here, and it begins as a hiding place. The lab is, for the rest of his life, the room his father is not in. This is essential to understanding why he chose his profession and why he cannot stop working even when work is destroying him; the lab is the only environment in which he has ever been reliably safe.
- **Bedwetting; somatic complaints.** Implied across the record (Ewing's flashbacks depict humiliation incidents around soiled bedding); consistent with the literature on chronic childhood stress.
- **Underweight; small stature.** The child Bruce in flashback is consistently drawn as smaller than peers. The adult Banner's pre-incident body — slight, narrow-shouldered, somatically underdeveloped — is the unhealed signature of childhood undernourishment under stress.

**Peer relations.** Sparse and difficult. The subject is depicted in flashback as bullied at school, which is the documented outcome for children who present as small, watchful, and unprotected. Mantlo's record includes a specific bullying episode whose precise contours the subject suppresses but which Ewing later positions as one of the first occasions on which the *child* experienced the inner-rage state that would become the Hulk — a fantasy of retaliation so vivid it frightened him. This is a critical datum: the dissociated rage-state had a subjective presence in the child's psyche years before gamma exposure. The exposure did not create it. The exposure gave it a body.

---

## 1.5 — The Matricide (approx. age 9–10)

The central trauma of the file. Reconstructed primarily from *Incredible Hulk* #312 with corroborating material in #377 and *Immortal Hulk* #6.

**Sequence, as recovered:**

1. Rebecca, having reached the decision that the household was no longer survivable for the child, packed a suitcase and prepared to leave with Bruce. The decision had been long in forming and was, in the subject's preserved memory, communicated to him as a rescue.
2. Brian intercepted them — accounts differ on whether at the house or at the curb near the family car; the suitcase and the parked car appear in panels in both Mantlo and Ewing.
3. Brian struck Rebecca. She fell. Per the panel record, the fatal injury was a head impact against the pavement/curb. The killing was not, in the strictly forensic sense, premeditated with intent to kill — but it was the predictable outcome of Brian's standing pattern of violence, and the subject does not, as an adult, accept the distinction.
4. The child witnessed the entire event. He was close enough to see his mother's face. He did not intervene — could not have intervened, at age nine, against an adult male — and the *failure to intervene* becomes one of the load-bearing pieces of his adult guilt structure.
5. Brian was arrested. At the inquest, under his father's coaching and explicit threat, the subject **perjured himself**, characterizing the death as an accident in a manner that minimized Brian's culpability. Brian was committed to a psychiatric facility rather than imprisoned, in part on the strength of this testimony.

**The coerced perjury** is the file's most under-discussed and most psychologically corrosive single detail. The child was forced not merely to survive the trauma but to *participate in its concealment* — to lie, under oath, about his mother's killing, in the protection of her killer. This is the precise configuration that the dissociation literature identifies as maximally generative of dissociative pathology: the trauma cannot be told because the telling itself was the second trauma. The memory is therefore sequestered behind a barrier reinforced from both sides — by the horror of the event and by the prohibition against speaking of it.

The Hulk's amnestic barrier in adulthood is, structurally, the same barrier the child placed around the matricide. The mechanism was rehearsed, successfully, at age nine. The gamma incident merely required the existing mechanism to handle more material.

---

## 1.6 — Custody by Aunt Susan (approx. ages 10–17)

After Brian's commitment, the subject was placed with **Susan Drake** (née Walters), Rebecca's sister. Location varies across writers (Ohio in most renderings; *Immortal Hulk* keeps the Ohio frame). Susan was, by all accounts in the record, kind. She was not, however, a trauma-competent caregiver — no one in the era and the social location was — and the subject arrived in her house with a sealed catastrophe inside him that she had no apparatus to open.

**The Susan years are the file's quiet period and the source of the deepest residual damage.** What is documented:

- Subject's withdrawal into academics; explosive trajectory in physics and mathematics; recognition as a prodigy by junior-high age. Skipped grades. Isolated socially as a consequence.
- Continued absence of close peer attachments. No documented childhood friend survives into the adult record except, much later and through entirely separate channels, Rick Jones — who functionally fills the absent-best-friend slot the childhood never produced.
- Marked maternal-coded attachment to Susan that was nonetheless *not* a true attachment repair, because the subject could not disclose the perjury, the witnessed killing, or the depth of paternal abuse. The relationship was therefore organized around the same concealment that had organized his relationship with his teachers — a presented compliant self, an undisclosed real self. Susan loved a curated child.
- Periodic correspondence with, or at minimum awareness of, Brian's continued existence in the psychiatric facility. The father was alive. The subject knew he was alive. The dread that the father might return was an ambient feature of adolescence. (It is dramatically consequential later: Brian *does* return in the subject's young adulthood, and the subject kills him in an altercation he then dissociates entirely, recovered only in Samson's therapy. The capacity to dissociate that killing is the matricide-perjury template firing a second time.)
- Adolescent affective life: depressed, isolated, intellectually voracious, sexually inhibited. No documented adolescent romantic or sexual relationship in the canon. The first sustained adult-coded intimacy is Betty Ross in graduate school / early career, and the difficulty of that relationship is in part the difficulty of a man attempting the developmental task of pair-bonding without having completed any of the prior developmental tasks of intimacy.
- Probable adolescent suicidal ideation; Ewing's flashbacks depict a teenage Bruce on a rooftop, contemplating; no completed attempts are documented in the childhood period. The ideation is the early form of what the adult record will display.

**Habits, tics, and routines that consolidate in adolescence and persist for life:**

- Self-soothing through repetitive calculation; the adult habit of running figures in his head under stress is a continuation of an adolescent habit of doing arithmetic to fall asleep.
- Pulse-taking. The adult Banner is repeatedly depicted with two fingers at his own wrist or carotid. This vigilance behavior originates in the abuse-era practice of monitoring his own startle and is reinforced in adolescence as a way of tracking the felt sense of fear. After the gamma incident it acquires its iconic instrumental meaning. It is, however, an inherited childhood gesture.
- Speech: soft, low-volume, slightly tentative, with the characteristic upward inflection on declarative statements that converts assertions into implicit questions awaiting permission. This is the speech pattern of a child who learned that confident assertion drew violence. It is on record from his earliest scenes (Lee/Kirby #1) and never substantially changes.
- Eye behavior: downcast in interpersonal interaction, with brief glance-up checks. Adult colleagues across decades remark on his difficulty with eye contact. Origin is paternal: direct gaze was, in Brian's household, an act of defiance that drew retaliation.
- Apologizing. The compulsive "I'm sorry" of the adult subject — sometimes uttered when nothing has occurred for which he is responsible — is an adolescent-consolidated reflex.
- The flight reflex. By late adolescence the subject is observably someone whose response to relational difficulty is to *leave the room*. The adult pattern of leaving cities, leaving countries, leaving planets is the same reflex at expanded scale.

---

## 1.7 — The Ground Floor: What Was in Place by Age 17

By the time the subject left Susan's household for undergraduate study (Penn State / Desert State / Pennsylvania State across various canons; consistent in the early-departure-for-college fact), the following were fixed:

1. A disorganized attachment substrate, pre-verbal, somatic, unrevisable without therapeutic intervention he would not receive for decades.
2. A core self-concept of monstrousness, in his father's voice, undefended against because uncontested at the level at which it had been installed.
3. A functioning dissociative apparatus, rehearsed on the matricide and the perjury, capable of sequestering catastrophic material behind an amnestic barrier and maintaining the barrier under stress.
4. A defensive style organized around concealment, intellectualization, isolation of affect, and reaction-formation gentleness — the entire adult Banner repertoire, fully formed.
5. A complete interdiction of anger as a permissible self-experience, with the affect routed instead into a fantasized internal rage-figure already present in adolescence and awaiting only the somatic vehicle the gamma incident would supply.
6. A pattern of relational pursuit-and-flight, already visible in the Susan relationship as the chronic withholding of his true interior from the person who loved him.
7. A vocation chosen for its containment properties: physics as the room his father is not in, the domain in which the unbearable is rendered as equation.
8. An unsupervised, untreated, undisclosed history of complex developmental trauma carried entirely inside a high-functioning, soft-spoken, brilliant young man departing for a university where no one would ask the questions that might have changed the trajectory.

The adult Banner arrives at the gamma test site already broken in every way that matters. The desert merely makes the breaking visible.

*— End Chronology I. Continues: Chronology II — Education, Early Career, and the Gamma Incident.*


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# CHRONOLOGY II — FORMATION & EMERGENCE

## SUBJECT: BANNER, ROBERT BRUCE, PhD

---

### 2.1 Late Childhood, Post-Matricide (approx. ages 8–13)

The file's continuous behavioral record resumes after the inquest, with the subject placed in the custody of his maternal aunt, Susan Drake (alternately rendered Elaine across the canon; the matrilineal aunt is consistent, the given name is not). The household is, by every available marker, materially adequate and emotionally insufficient. Aunt Susan is depicted across the Mantlo-era flashbacks as warm in disposition but conflict-avoidant, with no aptitude for the kind of trauma the subject is carrying and no professional resource available to her — this is small-town America in approximately the late 1950s, in which "the boy saw something terrible" was the operative phrase and silence was the prescribed treatment.

The behavioral signatures of this period, reconstructed from the canon's flashback record (Mantlo *Incident Hulk* #312; Pak *Hulk: Gray*; Ewing *Immortal Hulk* #6, #34, #45), are diagnostically classic for a child consolidating dissociative defenses:

- **Hyperverbal, hyperintellectual presentation at school.** The subject is reading at university level by age 10, doing applied mathematics by 12. Teachers describe him as "quiet" and "polite." This is the period in which intellect is recruited as primary defense.
- **Conspicuous physical underdevelopment.** Small for his age, thin, poor eater. The somatic signature of chronic HPA-axis activation. He is bullied; the bullying is the second, attenuated re-staging of the paternal abuse, and produces — by the subject's own later testimony to Samson — the first emergence of the inner figure he would later call "the Devil." The Devil-Hulk introject is not invented at the gamma incident; it is consolidating here, as the boy lies in bed at night and another voice in his head tells him what he would do to his tormentors if he could.
- **Imaginary-companion phenomena that read, in retrospect, as proto-alters.** Pak's *Gray* establishes that the boy spoke to himself in a separate voice — a "friend" who was angry on his behalf. This is the proto-Grey-Hulk: appetitive, transgressive, the voice that wants what the good boy is not permitted to want.
- **A specific recurrent ritual at the mother's grave.** Ewing draws the boy as visiting the cemetery alone, on his bicycle, on the anniversary; the ritual persists, in attenuated form, into adulthood — the subject has been observed (per Doc Samson's case notes, *Incident Hulk* #377) to mark the date in his journal every year regardless of his geographic location, and to keep a single photograph of Rebecca Banner in his wallet for decades.
- **No documented friendships of substance.** One peripheral childhood acquaintance, never named consistently. No team sports. No church. He is reported by the aunt as "happiest when he is alone in his room with his books," which is the family's preferred reading of a child who has learned that solitude is the only safety.
- **First documented depressive episode** at approximately age 12, characterized retrospectively (by adult Banner in conversation with Samson) as a period in which "I understood I was the problem." The cognitive distortion is consolidated here: the boy concludes that his father's violence was a response to *him*, that his mother died because of *him*, and that any future intimacy will produce the same outcome. This belief becomes the operational premise of the subject's entire adult life.

### 2.2 Adolescence (approx. 13–17)

The subject skips at least two grades and enters high school early. He is, by 14, the youngest and smallest student in his year. The canon (Pak, *World War Hulk: Gamma Files*; Ewing) supplies the following granulars:

- **Physical bullying** is sustained and routine. The subject does not fight back. The Devil-introject grows louder. There is one documented incident in which the subject was beaten unconscious in a school corridor and woke without memory of the final minutes of the assault — the first amnestic episode in the record, predating the gamma incident by more than a decade. He does not report it.
- **A single supportive adult figure** appears: a high-school physics teacher whose name is given variably across writers (Walters in some versions; unnamed in others) who recognizes the boy's gift and, more importantly, treats him as a person. The subject's later choice of physics as vocational field is overdetermined — it is the father's field (identification with the aggressor), the mother's posthumous wish that he "use his mind for good" (introjected maternal mandate), AND the field of the one adult who saw him. The vocation is thus tri-sourced and psychically loaded; it is not merely a career.
- **No documented romantic engagement** in the high-school period. Reports of intense, unexpressed attraction to a single classmate, never acted upon. The pattern that will define the Betty Ross relationship — yearning at distance, paralysis at proximity — is fully in place by 16.
- **The Brian Banner letters.** Ewing establishes (*Immortal Hulk* #34) that the father, institutionalized, wrote to the boy through this period. The subject did not open the letters; he kept them. This is the central artifact of the adolescent file: a sealed cardboard box of unopened paternal correspondence retained for decades. He has neither destroyed them nor read them. The dissociative posture made physical.
- **First documented suicidal ideation**, age 16, in journal fragments later recovered by Samson. Method-specific (firearm). Not attempted at that time.

### 2.3 Undergraduate Period — Pennsylvania State, then Desert State / Caltech (approx. 17–21)

The subject leaves the aunt's home at 17 on full scholarship and does not return except for funerals. The geographic flight pattern that will define his adult life begins here: he will not live in the same city for more than three consecutive years for the remainder of his life, gamma incident or no.

Behavioral granulars of the undergraduate period:

- **Academic record:** summa, multiple departmental prizes, first authorship on a paper before graduation. He is, by every metric, the most gifted student in his cohort.
- **Social record:** essentially null. Roommates from the period (per *Incident Hulk* annual flashbacks) describe him as "courteous," "invisible," "never there." He works in the library until close, eats alone, returns to the dorm, sleeps four to five hours, repeats. The compulsive labor pattern is established.
- **Substance use:** zero. He does not drink at college parties he does not attend. The teetotalism is not principled abstention; it is phobic avoidance of disinhibition. The subject has correctly intuited, without the conceptual language, that whatever lives inside him must not be loosened.
- **Romantic / sexual record:** essentially null. One documented date, terminated by the subject mid-evening with a panic-presentation he later (to Samson) described as "I felt I might hurt her, and I had no reason to think that, and that was the worst part."
- **Recurrent somatic complaints:** tension headaches, gastric reflux, episodic insomnia. He treats none of them medically. The body is already signaling.
- **First documented "missing time" of adult life:** approximately three hours, on a winter evening of his junior year, between leaving the lab and waking on a bench across campus, coatless, with no recollection. Did not seek evaluation. Recorded the event in a single line of his personal notebook: *"Lost time again."* The word *again* is diagnostically definitive — the phenomenon was, by his own account, not novel.

### 2.4 Graduate Work and Doctoral Period — Caltech / Desert State / Pennsylvania (approx. 21–25)

PhD in nuclear physics, with subspecialization in radiation physics — specifically, gamma-band high-energy phenomena. The vocational choice is, again, overdetermined: gamma is the highest-energy electromagnetic band, the "most destructive" radiation, the thing that kills. The subject is, on the surface, mastering it; underneath, he is studying his father in coded form. Brian Banner worked on the genetic effects of radiation; Bruce works on its weaponization. The Oedipal symmetry is precise and almost certainly unconscious through the entire pre-incident period.

- **Doctoral advisor relationships:** characterized by the same submissive-deferential posture later observed with General Ross. The subject does not push back, does not negotiate authorship, defers credit. Twice in the doctoral period he allows senior colleagues to take first author on work he generated.
- **A single significant friendship** with a fellow graduate student, often rendered as a young Walter Langkowski or, in other versions, a never-named theorist; the friendship is the closest peer bond of the pre-incident record and is terminated by the friend's death (Langkowski variant: not yet) or, more commonly, by the subject's relocation.
- **No partnered life.** No pets. No hobbies of record. Plays chess against himself. Listens to classical music — Bach, predominantly, the most mathematical of the canon — at low volume. Cooks the same three meals on rotation.
- **The notebooks.** The subject keeps technical notebooks of extraordinary discipline; he also keeps, separately, a personal journal in a small black hardcover notebook that he replaces approximately every eighteen months. The journals, fragments of which Samson later obtains, are written almost entirely in the third person: *"He worked late. He felt tired. He did not call."* The third-person self-reference predates the Hulk's third-person reference to Banner by years. The grammar of dissociation is already in his sentences.

### 2.5 Recruitment to Defense Work; Pre-Incident Professional Period (approx. 25–early 30s)

The subject is recruited to the gamma-bomb project on the basis of his published doctoral work. The position is at Desert Base, New Mexico; he reports to General Thaddeus "Thunderbolt" Ross.

The Ross relationship is the defining adult-pre-incident dynamic and must be characterized with care:

- **Ross treats the subject with open contempt** from first meeting. "Milksop." "Egghead." The vocabulary is sustained across years and is delivered in front of subordinates. This is not a working relationship; it is a public humiliation regime.
- **The subject does not protest.** He absorbs the contempt with the same posture used with his father. He works longer hours in response. The rage produced by Ross's contempt is interdicted at the host level and pooled, accruing pressure, behind the dissociative barrier.
- **The contempt produces the romantic opportunity that would define the rest of the subject's life:** Ross's daughter Betty, observing her father's cruelty, extends a counter-courtesy to the subject. The Betty Ross attachment is therefore structured from inception around a triangulation in which the subject is the object of paternal contempt and maternal-coded rescue. The Oedipal architecture of the original family is reproduced almost exactly.
- **The engagement to Betty Ross** in this pre-incident period is documented but characterized by the same paralytic distance that marked his single college date. He cannot consummate proximity. He defers the wedding. He works late. Betty waits. The pattern is set.

Pre-incident behavioral granulars at Desert Base:

- Lives in BOQ housing, sparse, no personal effects beyond books and the cardboard box of unopened paternal letters, which has followed him from city to city for fifteen years and is stored under the bed.
- Works 14- to 16-hour days, six days per week. Saturday afternoons reserved for Betty; frequently cancelled for "an equation that won't wait."
- Eats in the officers' commissary alone, always the same table, back to the wall — a tell consistent across the entire subsequent canon, the subject will not sit with his back to a door.
- Smokes briefly, then stops. Drinks coffee in extraordinary quantity. Insomnia is constant.
- Nightmares of his father, recorded in journal fragments, throughout this period.

### 2.6 The Gamma Incident — Detonation Day

The triggering event of the somatic phase of the file is the test detonation of the G-bomb (gamma bomb), Banner-designed, at Desert Base testing range. The chronology of the day is reconstructed across multiple canonical retellings (Lee/Kirby *Incident Hulk* #1; Byrne *Incident Hulk: The End*; Pak *Hulk: Gray*; Jones *Hulk: Year One*) and the consistent operative facts are:

- The subject directs the countdown from a reinforced observation bunker with his colleague Igor Starsky (later revealed as a foreign agent who has been instructed to allow the subject to die in the blast).
- During the final minute, the subject observes a civilian — the teenager Rick Jones — within the test perimeter, on what was supposed to be a cleared range. (Rick had entered on a dare.)
- The subject orders Starsky to delay the countdown and physically runs out into the test field to retrieve Jones. Starsky does not delay the countdown. The subject reaches Jones, throws him into a protective trench, and is fully exposed to the gamma pulse.
- **The first choice that founds the subsequent identity** is this one. It is reflexive, altruistic, and consistent with the subject's lifelong moral architecture: when a child is in danger, the subject acts. It is also, on close reading, the first moment in his adult life in which he acts on rage — the rage at Starsky's refusal to delay, the rage at the carelessness that permitted a child onto the range. The action that exposes him to the gamma is, psychically, the first time his interdicted aggression has reached the field of motor expression. The exposure follows immediately.

The subject survives. The reason he survives, in the canonical physics of the universe, is not addressable here; what matters for the file is that he survives, is held in medical isolation, and on the first nightfall after the incident undergoes the first transformation.

### 2.7 First Transformations and Initial Identity Configuration (immediate post-incident, weeks 1–12)

The earliest transformations are nocturnal and unwilled. The subject sleeps; the alter wakes in his body. The morphology is grey (the original *Incident Hulk* #1 coloration, restored later as the Grey Hulk / Fixit alter), the cognition is reduced but not absent, the disposition is hostile and self-interested, and the third-person reference to Banner is present from the first emergence: *"Banner is the puny one."* The amnestic barrier is total.

Behavioral granulars of the first weeks:

- The subject wakes repeatedly in unfamiliar locations: a ravine, a roadside, once a closed gas station. He is nude, dirty, often bloodied. He has no memory of egress from his quarters. He attempts to reconstruct each episode from physical evidence and press reports.
- Rick Jones — who alone knows what the subject becomes — adopts a managing role almost immediately: locking the subject in a reinforced bunker at sundown, monitoring, attempting to talk the emerging alter down. The Jones relationship is the first instance of a recurring pattern in the subject's adult life — a younger figure adopting the caretaking role that no one ever provided for the subject himself.
- The subject does not tell Betty. The decision not to tell is the **second defining choice** of the post-incident identity: he has decided, within days, that being known would destroy the person he loves, and that protection requires concealment. The decision is consistent with the boy who concluded at 12 that he was the problem. It is the founding act of the lifelong flight-from-intimacy that defines his adult biography.
- The subject does not surrender himself to medical authority. He does not tell the project. He does not seek psychiatric evaluation. The **third defining choice** is concealment of the condition itself — driven by a correct assessment that disclosure would lead to weaponization or vivisection (Ross, immediately upon learning, initiates exactly this), and an incorrect assessment that he can manage the condition privately. This choice founds the adversarial relationship with the state that will structure the next sixty years of the file.

### 2.8 The Stabilization of the Phenotype and the First Flight (months 3–12 post-incident)

Within the first year:

- The transformation trigger shifts from nocturnal automaticity to **autonomic-arousal-driven**: anger, fear, pain, accelerated heart rate. The shift represents the dissociative system reorganizing around its original psychic logic — affect, not circadian rhythm, is the trigger that matters. The somatic apparatus has aligned itself with the psychological one.
- The alter's morphology shifts (in the canon's chromatic record, from grey to green) and the dominant emergent state becomes the Savage Hulk — the child-state, low cognition, defensive rage, the seven-year-old who watched his mother die. The dominant alter is the alter holding the original trauma.
- Ross identifies the subject as the Hulk and initiates the manhunt that becomes the operational backdrop of the subject's life for decades. The persecutory paternal figure has now been externalized into the literal apparatus of the United States military. The original family dynamic is reconstituted at planetary scale.
- The subject **leaves**. The engagement is broken — not formally, in the early canon, but functionally; the subject becomes a fugitive. The flight pattern that was implicit through his entire pre-incident life is now operational and irreversible.
- Rick Jones travels with him for the first period; the Banner-Jones dyad on the road is the founding configuration of the subject's adult life, and the absence of Jones in later periods produces measurable destabilization.

### 2.9 The First Year's Defining Choices — Consolidated

By the end of the first post-incident year, the subject has made four choices that will structure the remainder of his life and that constitute, together, the founding act of the identity:

1. **Run into the field for the child.** The reflexive altruism that defines his moral spine and that founds his cover identity as a "good man who becomes a monster." The choice will be re-staged hundreds of times across the canon — every emergence of the Savage Hulk in defense of a threatened child is a re-execution of this single act.
2. **Conceal from Betty.** The lifelong organization of intimacy around protection-through-distance. Every subsequent romantic rupture in the file repeats this decision.
3. **Conceal from the state.** The lifelong adversarial relationship with institutional authority and the impossibility of receiving the medical care he requires. The fugitive posture, once adopted, cannot be reversed without dismantling the apparatus around it.
4. **Disclaim ownership of the alter.** The choice — made implicitly within hours of the first transformation, and never revisited until Samson — to refer to the Hulk in the third person, to treat it as a thing that happens to him, to externalize agency. This is the founding act of the dissociative split at the cognitive level; the somatic split is a given, but the *cognitive disclaimer* is a choice, and it is this choice that prevents integration for the subsequent four decades.

Each of these four choices is consistent with the developmental substrate established in section 2.1–2.5. None of them are choices a non-traumatized person would have made. All four are, in the language of trauma therapy, **adaptive in context, catastrophic across time** — they solved the immediate crisis and locked in the chronic pathology.

### 2.10 Closing Observation on the Formation Period

The conventional reading of the file places the formative moment at the gamma incident. The evidence does not support this. The formative period closes, properly, around age 10, in a small house in the American interior, with a boy perjuring himself at an inquest about a man he watched kill his mother. Everything subsequent — the physics, the deference to Ross, the paralytic engagement, the run into the test field, the four founding choices of the post-incident year — is the working-out of decisions already made by that child. The gamma incident is not the origin of the identity. It is the moment the identity acquired a body capable of expressing what had been, until then, only a voice in a small room at night.

The remainder of the file is the consequence of that acquisition.


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

*Approximate coverage: the long middle decades following the initial Hulk emergence and the early fugitive years, through the Doc Samson therapeutic period, the Pantheon, the Heroes Reborn / Onslaught dislocation, the Joe Fixit interregnum, the desert-fugitive cycles, and the road into the Pak / Aaron / Ewing late period. This is the bulk of the longitudinal observation file.*

---

## A. The Fugitive Decade and the Establishment of the Recursive Cycle

The defining behavioral signature of the subject's middle period is **flight**, and the pattern stabilizes early. Following the initial publicizing of his condition, the subject organizes his life around a recursive seven-step cycle the file has logged in dozens of variants: arrival in a new locale under an assumed name (the alias rotation is unusually disciplined — variants on *David B.*, *Bruce Jones*, *Bruce Green*, *Bob Danner*, the surname always monosyllabic, the initials often preserved as a tell); brief employment in a low-wage manual role (mechanic, short-order cook, orderly, day laborer, bus boy, carnival roustabout, migrant farmhand — the file shows a pronounced preference for trades in which his hands are occupied and his face is downward); the formation of one tentative relationship, almost always with a wounded woman or a vulnerable child; the appearance of a stressor (a local thug, a corporate goon, Hulkbusters, a Ross-sponsored military element, or simply a domestic-violence incident witnessed in proximity); transformation; property destruction; flight on foot at dawn, almost always westward when on foot, almost always by freight rail when distance is required.

The freight-train footage is its own subfile. Across the period the subject is observed boarding empty boxcars in at least eleven states, always at the same kind of yard (small, lightly patrolled, near a water tower or grain elevator), always carrying nothing but a satchel containing a single change of clothes — typically purple or violet trousers, the only personal-effect superstition the file has been able to confirm (he buys them deliberately; the color is not coincidence but a private capitulation to the fact that his ruined wardrobe in the alter state always settles to that hue, and purchasing in advance reduces post-episode shame).

He sleeps poorly. The file logs habitual 3:00–4:00 a.m. waking, often standing, often at a window. He does not own a watch in this period; he reads time off the sky and off radio broadcasts. He will not sleep with his back to a door. He will not eat a meal he did not see prepared. He counts exits when entering any room — the file has direct observational confirmation of lip-counting behavior in diners, the eyes flicking to the rear service door, the front door, the kitchen pass-through, in that order.

The hitchhiking sub-pattern is equally regular: he accepts rides only from solo drivers, prefers women drivers, refuses rides from men in pickup trucks (the paternal-coded vehicle of his childhood Midwest), and disembarks immediately if alcohol is present in the cab. The teetotalism is enforced not as preference but as identity; offered a beer at a Tennessee truck stop in this period, he was observed to flinch at the can before declining — a micro-tell logged repeatedly across the decade.

The relational pattern in this phase is also stereotyped. The subject is drawn, again and again, to women who are themselves in flight from male violence — diner waitresses with bruised forearms, runaway mothers, women working two jobs to keep a child fed. He provides labor, money from his last wages, sometimes a night of protection, and then leaves before the relationship can develop a sexual or claiming dimension. The withdrawal is moralized (he tells himself he is protecting them) but functionally serves the avoidance of intimacy that would raise arousal. The pattern is the disorganized-attachment phenotype operating at full bore: approach, give, retreat. He is, in this period, perhaps the most chronically lonely man in the file.

**Heart-rate monitoring becomes ritualized in this phase.** Initially intermittent, by the middle of the fugitive decade the subject is performing pulse-checks on himself at predictable intervals — on waking, before any conversation lasting longer than a minute, before any meal, before sleep — with two fingers to the carotid, head slightly tilted left, eyes closed for a count of fifteen. This is the somatic-monitoring compulsion that will define the rest of his life. It is, clinically, both adaptive (it works) and pathological (it converts every interpersonal moment into a vigilance exercise, foreclosing presence).

## B. The Hulkbusters Pursuit and the Ross Asymmetry

Throughout the middle period, the subject is hunted by elements answering to General Thaddeus Ross. The pursuit is not the file's most important fact about this period; the *subject's response* to the pursuit is. Where a fugitive of comparable intelligence would relocate offshore, alter appearance, exploit anonymity at scale, the subject instead remains in-country, often within reasonable driving distance of Gamma Base, and surfaces at Ross-adjacent locations with a frequency that cannot be coincidence. He returns to Desert Base. He returns to Hidden Land. He drifts back toward New Mexico repeatedly across years.

The interpretation is straightforward and is consistent across the file: the subject is incapable of fully escaping the paternal-coded persecutor because the persecutor is also, by proxy, his attachment object's father. To break with Ross is to break with Betty. He cannot do it. The pursuit is, at a deep level, a substitute relational structure — pursuer and pursued, locked together, generating predictable interactions that are at least *known*. The fugitive cycle is therefore not a flight from Ross. It is a long, painful waltz with him.

The submissive register in Ross's actual presence is logged repeatedly: shoulders inward, head ducked, voice softened, use of "sir" without prompt, hands held visibly empty and away from pockets. In one extended observation the subject, captured and held in restraints, addressed Ross as if reporting to a thesis adviser — a regression so complete the attending physician noted it independently. The alter, in the same captivity, expressed the inverse: profanity directed at Ross by name, threats of specific harm, and on at least three documented occasions the alter has identified Ross verbally as "the old man" — the same epithet he uses in dream-sequence dialogues with the Brian Banner introject. The collapse of the two paternal figures in the alter's cognition is total.

## C. The Joe Fixit Interregnum (Las Vegas)

The middle period contains a discrete, anomalous, and diagnostically priceless sub-arc: an extended residency in Las Vegas in the **Grey Hulk / Mr. Fixit** alter, employed as enforcer and fixer for the Maxwell casino interest under the name *Joe Fixit*. The subject as host is functionally absent for this period; the alter holds executive control for months.

This is the file's clearest window onto the split-off appetitive system. Fixit drinks (single-malt scotch, neat, two fingers, never more than four drinks per evening — disciplined consumption, which is its own datum); gambles (high-stakes craps and blackjack, played with statistical sophistication that suggests Banner's intellect is partially accessible to this alter, unlike the Savage state); maintains a sexual relationship with a showgirl (Marlo Chandler — later, after merger, she will marry Rick Jones, a piece of relational continuity the file flags as nontrivial); wears tailored suits in dark colors; sleeps days; works nights; tips lavishly; never apologizes. He is, in every behavioral particular, the inverse of the host.

Diagnostically: the contents of Fixit are the contents Banner cannot tolerate in himself. Appetite. Aggression deployed instrumentally rather than reactively. Sexuality without apology. Money handled without guilt. Sleep. Style. The very existence of Fixit is the proof that the host's pacifism and abstemiousness are not values freely chosen but defenses rigidly maintained, with the disowned material exiled to a separate executive.

When the host re-emerges and the Fixit period ends, the subject has no autobiographical access to it. He learns of his own months in Las Vegas the way an outsider would — secondhand, with shame.

## D. The Doc Samson Therapeutic Period

The single most important relationship of the middle period is with Leonard Samson, PhD. Samson's intervention extends across years, with multiple discrete therapy intensives, and it is the first time in the subject's life that a professional with both the training and the sustained access has attempted integrative work.

Samson's approach evolves. Early sessions are confrontational and goal-oriented (separate Banner from Hulk; cure the condition by extraction). These fail and the file shows why: they reproduce the splitting defense rather than addressing it. Samson then shifts, around the midpoint of the period, toward what would now be recognized as parts-work or structural-dissociation-informed therapy: the alters are mapped, named, dialogued with, and ultimately negotiated with toward a fusion state — the **Merged Hulk / Professor**.

The therapeutic alliance is real and is one of the very few sustained male relationships in the subject's life. Behavioral observation during this period logs marked changes: increased eye contact in session (the baseline downward gaze is held up for longer intervals across months); decreased apologetic interjection; the first recorded use of first-person language about the alter ("when *I* hurt those people" rather than "when the Hulk did it") — a milestone the file marks with the date.

The Merged state functions for an extended interval. The subject lives openly, in relationship with Betty (they marry in this window, in a quiet ceremony in Nevada — the wedding is one of the only photographed events of the subject's life in which his face is fully relaxed), and operates with the Pantheon as a frontline asset rather than a fugitive.

**The Pantheon arc** is itself a complete sub-record. The subject's first sustained team affiliation, under the patriarchal Agamemnon — note the structural reproduction of the abusive-father relationship in the choice of organizational figurehead, which the subject does not see at the time and which the file flags as the central irony of the period. The Pantheon offers what he has never had: a structured kinship system, a mission, a base (the Mount), a degree of accountability. He functions. He leads, even. He commands respect from peers (Atalanta, Achilles, Ulysses) and operates with a tactical fluency the file did not previously have grounds to expect. The capacity was always there; the conditions had never permitted its expression.

The Pantheon arc ends, as such arcangements always end for the subject, in betrayal — Agamemnon's revealed corruption — and the subject's departure is performed with the now-familiar pattern: a final act of moral clarity, the dismantling of the institution, and a return to flight.

## E. The Onslaught / Heroes Reborn Dislocation

The subject is, during the Onslaught crisis, separated from his Hulk for an extended interval — physically, structurally, across realities. The file treats this episode as a natural experiment: what does the host look like with the alter excised?

The answer, recorded in detail across the *Heroes Reborn* window and the immediate aftermath, is that the subject without the alter is profoundly diminished — physically frail to the point of repeated hospitalization, affectively flatter than baseline, somatically deteriorating. The dissociative apparatus, for all its costs, was performing essential regulatory work; its removal produced collapse rather than relief. This finding is consistent with the contemporary structural-dissociation literature: alters carry function, and decompartmentalization without integration is iatrogenic.

The reunion with the alter is, paradoxically, restorative. The subject's body recovers. The window confirms that the goal cannot be excision; the goal must be cooperation.

## F. The Loss of Betty and the Long Decompensation

The death of Betty Banner — gamma-poisoning attributable in significant part to the subject's own irradiated physiology and to Abomination's direct action — is the central loss event of the middle period and one of the two or three most consequential events in the entire file.

Behavioral observation in the immediate aftermath logs: cessation of speech for approximately nine days; refusal of food for the first four; the abandonment of the heart-rate ritual (the only documented interruption of the practice in the adult record — significant because it represents a brief period in which the subject did *not* care whether he transformed); cessation of correspondence with Samson; departure from all known addresses within three weeks.

The Merged state does not survive the loss. The fusion that Samson had built was relational at its foundation — it required Betty as the ground against which integration could be stabilized — and her absence dissolves it. The subject reverts across the following arcs through progressively more primitive configurations, eventually returning to states the file had not seen since the early fugitive decade.

The mourning is not metabolized. It is dissociated, like everything else; the affect is exiled to the alter system, where it surfaces as the Devil Hulk's intensified persecutory presence in dream sequences across the following years. The introject is fed by the new grief. The internal father grows louder.

## G. The Desert Years (post-Betty)

The subject returns to the Southwest in this period and re-enters a fugitive cycle structurally identical to the original decade, but slower, heavier, more silent. The relational substitutions in this phase shift: he forms attachments to children (a sequence of brief guardianships of orphaned or endangered minors across small towns in Arizona, New Mexico, Nevada — the file logs at least seven such episodes) rather than to women. The shift is diagnostic. With Betty dead, the adult-attachment channel is closed; the child-protection channel, which speaks directly to the unprotected-child substrate, opens. The subject is, in effect, attempting to save himself in proxy.

The episodes end the same way each time: the child reaches safety (extended family, social services, a stable adult), and the subject leaves before he can be claimed in return.

Sleep deteriorates further in this phase. The 3:00 a.m. waking becomes a 2:00 a.m. waking, then earlier. He begins to read aloud to himself at night — physics texts, in undertone — a self-soothing behavior the file infers (no observer was present for most of it) from the worn condition of specific volumes recovered from abandoned camps. *Misner, Thorne, and Wheeler*. *The Feynman Lectures*. A paperback copy of Bohm's *Wholeness and the Implicate Order* with the spine broken at the chapter on undivided wholeness — a tell, if ever the file has logged one.

## G. The Banner-as-Asset Reframe

A subsequent phase — corresponding to the Aaron *Indestructible Hulk* configuration — sees the subject attempt a radical operational reframe: rather than suppress or contain the alter, he will *deploy* it. He embeds with a state-adjacent scientific apparatus (SHIELD), accepts a laboratory, accepts a team of subordinate researchers, and treats the transformation as a tactical asset to be pointed at appropriate targets in exchange for resources to pursue legacy-class scientific work.

The reframe is logged here because its *failure* is the diagnostic event. The configuration holds for an extended period — long enough for several major scientific contributions (the file does not catalog them in detail; they include work on Kirby-Genes structures, transdimensional materials, and at least one fundamental advance in vibration-energy theory) — but the underlying wound is not addressed and the alter is not in fact integrated; it is merely rented. The host's contempt for himself does not abate. The Devil Hulk introject is, if anything, sharpened by the instrumentalization: the alter resents being used.

The configuration ends in catastrophic rupture; the file does not need to detail the specific precipitant because the form of the failure was preordained. Any arrangement that does not address the introject will fall to the introject.

## H. Patterns Across the Middle Period — Behavioral Micro-Record

Drawing across the whole middle period, the file consolidates the following invariant micro-patterns:

- **The two-finger carotid check**, performed at predictable junctures, more frequent under stress, abandoned only in the immediate post-Betty window.
- **Lip-counting of exits** on entering any enclosed space, eyes flicking in fixed sequence (rear, primary, secondary).
- **Refusal to sit with back to a door** — has rearranged seating in three restaurants on direct observation, politely; in one case offered the waitress a five-dollar bill to facilitate the move.
- **Hands kept visible** when speaking to anyone in uniform.
- **The downward apologetic register** as conversational baseline — half-smile, slight head tilt left, opening sentence almost always a softener ("sorry, I — ", "I don't mean to — ", "if it's not — ").
- **Disengagement of eye contact at exactly the moment a conversation turns emotional**, gaze drops to the speaker's collarbone or to his own hands.
- **Compulsive tidiness in temporary lodgings**, far in excess of what concealment would require — bed made tightly, dishes washed immediately, towels folded — the orderliness of a child who learned that disorder triggered violence.
- **The purple-trousers provisioning** — a single, consistent, slightly absurd planning behavior maintained for decades.
- **Strict alphabetization and notation in field notebooks** carried in the satchel, dense math in graphite, the handwriting small, neat, slightly leftward-canted, page numbers in the upper-right, dates in ISO format — the only domain in which his control register is unimpaired.
- **Avoidance of mirrors** in the morning, particularly within an hour of waking; the file has direct observation of the subject shaving by feel, touching the razor's progress with the off hand rather than looking.
- **The pre-conversation breath** — a slow exhalation through pursed lips, three to four seconds, performed before initiating any interaction with a stranger.
- **The post-transformation kit** — concealed in caches across the country, the file has located at least twenty-three: a Ziploc bag with cash (small bills, never more than $400), a fresh shirt and trousers, a pair of plain canvas sneakers in size eleven, a forged ID, and a single granola bar. The granola bar is in every cache. The constancy of that detail is, in its way, the saddest item in the file.
- **The absence of music**. The subject does not own a radio in any settled period of the middle decades and does not sing, hum, or whistle on observation. Music is, presumably, too direct a route to affect.
- **The reading-aloud at night**, undertone, physics texts, self-soothing — inferred but consistent.
- **The avoidance of his own birthday**, never acknowledged, never celebrated; on three logged occasions he has worked through the day deliberately and on one occasion left town the morning of.

## I. Evolution of the Alter System Across the Middle Period

The middle period is when the alter system, originally a binary (Banner / Savage), differentiates into the mature configuration that will define the late period:

- **Savage Hulk** stabilizes as the child-defense state, age-frozen at approximately seven, the age of matricide.
- **Grey / Fixit** is articulated as the appetitive-aggressive socialized alter, with a discrete environment (Vegas) and a discrete relational object (Marlo).
- **Professor / Merged** is constructed therapeutically with Samson, holds Banner's intellect and the Hulk's body, and is the only alter ever to sustain adult sexuality and partnered marriage.
- **Devil Hulk / Guilt Hulk** crystallizes in this period as the persecutory introject, surfacing initially in dreams and later in more direct phenomenology, speaking in the father's register, holding the system's self-hatred.

The progression is, in the file's read, the alter system *finishing its formation* under longitudinal observation. By the end of the middle period the full architecture is in place; the late period will be the period in which inter-alter relations — cooperation, war, or merger — become the primary therapeutic question.

## J. The Person, in the Middle

Taken as a whole, the middle period is the long phase in which the subject becomes recognizably himself: the thin, soft-spoken, perpetually apologetic man with the absurdly well-organized field notebook, the granola-bar cache in twenty-three states, the carotid pulse-check before every interaction, the purple trousers folded in the satchel, the cycle of arrival-relation-rupture-flight repeating with metronomic regularity across a continent. The grand canvas — Pantheon command, marriage to Betty, Las Vegas underworld, dissociative wars across realities — sits on a substrate of these tiny, repeated, deeply lonely habits, and it is the habits that the file regards as the truer record. The wars are episodic. The two-finger carotid check is the life.

The middle period closes with the subject having survived more than any human-scale assessment would predict, having loved and lost the only adult he could fully attach to, having been treated by the only therapist who ever fully saw him, having lived briefly as a fully integrated person and then come apart again, and having returned, at the end of it, to the road, the satchel, the freight yard at dawn, westward, alone — older now, quieter, with the Devil Hulk's voice clearer in his dreams than it had ever been, and the long late period still ahead.


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

## Preamble: Defining "Recent"

For purposes of this dossier, the "recent" window opens with the subject's emergence from the events catalogued by Al Ewing (2018–2021) — the most clinically articulated period in the record — and runs through the subsequent realignments under Donny Cates and Ryan Ottley (2021–2022), Phillip Kennedy Johnson's tenure (2022–present), and the parallel mass-public-facing manifestations through the *Avengers* and adjacent team books. This is the period during which the subject moved, for the first time in his documented life, from suppression-and-flight as the master strategy to an explicit, conscious, **negotiated** relationship with his alter system — and then, predictably, regressed under fresh trauma. The arc is the arc of a real trauma patient three years into competent treatment: genuine gains, partial relapse, and a baseline that is nonetheless measurably elevated from the pre-treatment floor.

---

## 1. The Integrative Phase (late *Immortal Hulk* through resolution)

The defining recent achievement is not a victory over the Hulk — every prior attempt at that has failed and would fail again — but the subject's gradual acceptance that the alters are *parts of him*, that they hold information and affect he requires access to, and that the Devil Hulk in particular is not an enemy to be defeated but an introjected figure to be **disidentified from** and then reincorporated. This is the standard contemporary model for severe DID treatment (the structural-dissociation-of-the-personality framework: Van der Hart, Nijenhuis, Steele), and it is, for the first time in sixty years of file, what the subject is actually doing.

**Observable behavioral markers of the integrative phase:**

- **Reduction in third-person self-reference.** In recovered interview transcripts and dialogue logs from the period, the subject begins to use first-person plural ("we") in moments of internal negotiation — a small but diagnostically significant shift indicating reduced amnestic barrier and increased co-consciousness.
- **Acceptance of the somatic transformation as ego-syntonic.** Earlier, the subject would awaken from a Hulk episode and immediately catalogue the damage with self-loathing. In this phase he begins, intermittently, to *plan* transformations — to enter them rather than be ambushed by them. This is enormous.
- **Recovered autobiographical access.** The Brian Banner memories, sequestered for decades and recovered only under extreme therapeutic pressure with Samson, become available to the subject without producing immediate decompensation. He can speak the matricide without dissociating. He cannot yet speak it without weeping.
- **Reduction in flight behavior.** The lifelong pattern of geographic flight (leaving Betty, leaving cities, leaving the planet) attenuates measurably. The subject remains in proximity to relational difficulty for longer windows before rupture.
