The window is still narrower than a baseline adult's; it is wider than his own historical baseline by an order of magnitude.

**What was *not* achieved.** Full integration is not attained and the subject, if he is honest, would say he no longer believes it is the goal. The Savage state still emerges under acute threat. The Devil-introject still speaks in dreams. The subject still cannot reliably tolerate sustained sexual intimacy with Betty without arousal-triggered breach. What changed is not the apparatus but his relationship to it.

---

## 2. The Cates/Ottley Disruption — "Banner of War" Period

The integrative gains were partially undone by the subsequent period in which the subject submitted to a self-engineered structural reorganization of the alter system — recasting his interior as a "starship," with himself as the pilot in a control room and the Hulk as the engine. Read clinically, this is **a sophisticated relapse into instrumentalization**: a more articulate version of the Jason Aaron–era attempt to use the Hulk as a deployable asset, dressed in better metaphor. It re-establishes a hard host/alter barrier (pilot/engine), reintroduces the dissociative split that the prior integrative phase had been dismantling, and recruits the subject's exceptional cognitive capacities in service of the very defensive architecture that has failed him for sixty years.

The "starship" architecture failed, as it had to. Under sustained combat stress against another high-arousal subject (Thor), the alter system breached the engineered containment, the "pilot" was overrun, and a more primitive and less negotiated Hulk state took the field. The subject experienced the failure as confirmation of his core belief: that he cannot be trusted with himself.

**Diagnostic note.** This relapse is *not* evidence against the prior integrative work. It is evidence of the well-documented non-linearity of severe-DID recovery, in which the patient, having achieved partial co-consciousness, becomes terrified of full integration (which is correctly experienced as a kind of death of the parts) and recruits a more elegant defense to forestall it. The starship was a defense against integration, not a tool for it.

---

## 3. Current Phase (Johnson era, ongoing)

The subject is presently engaged in what the file would characterize as **post-relapse stabilization with elevated baseline insight**. The headline observable: he has stopped fleeing. He is on the road, yes — the itinerant pattern reasserts — but he is on the road with a stated purpose (locating and confronting other gamma-affected individuals; addressing the broader consequences of his own scientific work) rather than as pure flight. The distinction is small but real: prior flight was *away from*; current movement is *toward*. The locomotion is the same; the affective vector is inverted.

**Companion presence.** The subject is travelling with Charlie, a young woman granted limited gamma abilities. Diagnostically, this companion functions in the same structural role as Rick Jones did across decades: a younger person whose safety becomes the subject's organizing purpose, and whose presence provides the **co-regulating other** that the subject has never been able to provide for himself. This is not coincidence; it is the subject unconsciously reproducing the only relational template in which he has historically functioned without dissociative rupture — guardian to a younger figure, with the parental-rescuer role inverted from his own childhood. He is becoming, repeatedly and across decades, the adult he needed and did not have.

**Current somatic baseline.**
- Sleep: poor; documented nightmares with father-content; subject still wakes braced.
- Resting heart rate: elevated relative to a non-traumatized adult, depressed relative to his own historical baseline — the chronic-vigilance signature attenuated but not resolved.
- Weight: low-normal in host state; the lifelong slightness persists.
- Diet: ascetic, low-stimulus, predictable. The subject continues to avoid caffeine in any quantity, avoid alcohol absolutely, and consume food in routinized small portions — all consistent with autonomic-arousal management as a life practice.
- Substance use: nil. Unchanged across the entire file.
- Self-monitoring: continuous. Subject still checks pulse in moments of escalation, still performs breath-regulation behaviors that have become so habituated they no longer register to him as deliberate. The right hand to the inside of the left wrist remains the single most reliable behavioral tell in the file.

**Current relational status — Betty Ross.** The relationship is, at present, neither active nor severed. Betty's own gamma-affected trajectory (the Red Harpy state) has produced a parallel and now-converging dissociative arc, and the two subjects are, for the first time in the record, **structurally peers** in their relationship to their respective alter systems. This is potentially the most therapeutically significant relational development of the subject's adult life. It is also acutely dangerous: two high-arousal dissociative subjects in proximity can co-regulate, but they can also co-destabilize, and the file would project either outcome as roughly equally probable in any given six-month window. The subject does not currently permit himself to hope, which is, for him, a form of progress — earlier-era Banner would have either fled the situation entirely or romanticized it into a magical-thinking reunion fantasy. Present Banner sits in the not-knowing.

**Current relational status — Avengers and institutional ties.** Episodic, instrumentally cooperative, affectively distant. The subject maintains professional contact with Stark, Richards, and other scientific peers; participates in team operations when called; declines team residency. He keeps the relationships at the precise distance at which they remain accessible without becoming sources of arousal. This is well-managed. It is also lonely, and the subject knows it.

**Current relational status — Samson.** Doc Samson, the only sustained therapeutic alliance of the subject's life, has been intermittently available and intermittently absent (and intermittently dead) across the canon. At present the alliance is dormant rather than active. The subject has internalized enough of the therapeutic frame to do significant self-work without him, but the absence of the external mirror is a genuine clinical gap.

---

## 4. Current Daily Pattern (granular)

The exhaustive surveillance read of a present-day week:

- **0430–0530 — wake.** Almost always pre-dawn, almost always not by choice; the chronic-hyperarousal sleep signature. Subject often wakes with the residue of dream-content involving his father, his mother, or both; he does not always remember the content but recognizes the affective signature.
- **First fifteen waking minutes — vitals check.** Pulse, breath, orientation to location (a tell of the lifelong fugue-risk; he reflexively confirms where he is upon waking), brief inventory of body for injuries that were not there the night before.
- **Morning — coffee substitute (herbal, decaffeinated), minimal food, reading.** The reading is technical when possible — physics journals when accessible, salvaged paperbacks when not. The reading is itself a regulatory practice; intellectual engagement keeps the system in the prefrontal mode that is least conducive to switch.
- **Mid-morning through afternoon — movement.** Whether the subject is travelling with Charlie, working in a borrowed lab, or transient through a small town, the day is organized around predictable, low-arousal task sequences. The subject has learned, the hard way, that unstructured time is dangerous time.
- **Interpersonal contact — rationed, gentle, and brief.** The subject is unfailingly polite to strangers, gives the same small smile to waitresses and clerks, makes eye contact briefly and then looks down and to the right, tips well, leaves rooms before he is noticed leaving. The exit-without-being-seen behavior is decades old and is performed without conscious thought.
- **Evening — perimeter check.** Whether in a motel, a safe house, or a borrowed bed, the subject conducts a quiet survey of exits, lines of sight, and adjacent occupancy before settling. This is the abused-child somatic legacy, layered with the operational reality that he is, in fact, hunted. The two reinforce each other.
- **Pre-sleep — breath work, brief meditation, lights off early.** Subject sleeps in worn, soft clothing that will tear without binding him — a learned accommodation to the somatic reality of his condition. He does not sleep nude unless circumstances make clothing impossible. The clothing is also, at a deeper register, a refusal to be again the naked, post-fugue, ashamed figure of his earlier years.

---

## 5. Current Internal State (best inference)

The subject, at present, is the most integrated version of himself the file has ever recorded, and he is also exhausted. The work of holding co-consciousness, of not fleeing, of meeting his own parts rather than dissociating them, is work — and the subject has been doing it largely alone, in a body that punishes him for any failure of self-regulation, while the world continues to throw at him the precise stimuli (paternal authorities, threatened children, restraints, monster-naming) that his trauma-architecture is most reactive to.

He does not believe he will ever be well. He does, for the first time in his life, believe he can be *better*, and he has assembled enough lived evidence (the integrative gains, the surviving relationships, the sustained absence of catastrophic flight) to make that belief defensible to himself on the days he doubts it.

The Devil-introject still speaks. It speaks less often, and the subject has learned to recognize the voice as his father's and not his own. This is the single most important piece of clinical real estate the subject has gained in sixty years of file: he no longer fully believes the voice that hates him.

That is where he is. That is how he got here.


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — SUBJECT: BANNER, ROBERT BRUCE, PhD

*Compiled from longitudinal observation, recovered records, post-incident medical examinations conducted under SHIELD, Avengers, and Pantheon auspices, with retrospective reconstruction of pre-incident pediatric history from family and educational sources. This file is unusually voluminous because the subject's body has been, since November 1962, the site of more catastrophic somatic events than any other documented human organism, and because the boundary between "medical" and "psychiatric" in this case is itself diagnostically meaningless: the body is the dissociative apparatus.*

---

## 1. CONSTITUTIONAL BASELINE AND PEDIATRIC RECORD

The subject's pre-incident constitution is that of a chronically under-thrived male of European ancestry, born to a mother (Rebecca Banner, née Walters) with no documented significant pathology and a father (Brian Banner, PhD, nuclear physicist, Los Alamos contractor) with a documented history of alcoholism, paranoid ideation, and at least one psychiatric hospitalization prior to the subject's birth. There is no recovered obstetric record of complications at delivery; the subject was born at term in upstate New York (the Mantlo-era recovered record places the family at Dayton, Ohio, in the subject's earliest years).

Pediatric physical examination records — partially reconstructed from school nurse files at the subject's elementary school and from one ED admission at age six (the official chart records "fall from stairs"; the recovered traumatic memory in *Incident Hulk* #312 and elaborated in *Immortal Hulk* establishes paternal assault as the actual mechanism) — show the somatic signature of a chronically abused child. Specifically: percentile height tracking at or below the 25th throughout pediatric years against family genetic potential considerably higher; weight consistently below the 10th percentile; recurrent unexplained ecchymoses on the upper arms, back, and posterior thighs (locations diagnostic for grip-and-throw assault); two healed rib fractures visible on the single chest film in the file (the film was obtained for suspected pneumonia at age seven; the radiologist noted but did not pursue the old fractures, a common pattern in mid-century pediatric records); a healed mid-shaft ulnar fracture of the left forearm (the classic "nightstick" defensive fracture); and chronic mild anemia consistent with childhood undernutrition and stress.

Dental examination from the subject's adolescent records, retrievable through his Science High academic file, shows two crowned anterior teeth — both replacements for incisors lost in the same incident at age nine (the file notes "playground accident"; the actual incident, per the *Immortal Hulk* recovered material, was a blow to the face). Bruxism wear is severe on the molars and remains so throughout adult dental records; the subject ground his teeth, asleep and awake, from at least age six. He has worn a night guard intermittently since his late twenties when issued by Betty Ross during the brief Hulkbuster-base period. He does not wear it consistently. The wear pattern across forty years of adult dental imaging shows progressive flattening of the cuspids and a chronic temporomandibular click on the right, never surgically addressed.

**Sleep history, pediatric.** Reconstructed from his aunt Susan Drake's later interviews and from one school counselor's note: chronic nightmares from age four or five onward; episodes of sleepwalking and at least one documented episode of night terrors with screaming the household had to physically restrain him through; persistent enuresis until age eleven, undocumented in any medical chart because no one was taking him to physicians.

**Endocrine inference.** The subject's pubertal development was late (full adult height not attained until age nineteen, per Science High and Penn State athletic records — though he did not play sports). This pattern, combined with the somatotype, is consistent with chronic hypothalamic-pituitary suppression from sustained childhood stress. The pre-incident adult subject — a 5'9", 128-pound man at the time of the gamma detonation — was, in straightforward endocrinological terms, a developmentally arrested phenotype. He looked, throughout his twenties and early thirties, perceptibly younger than his chronological age, with poor muscle definition, fine vellus hair across the chest and abdomen, soft features, and the small-frame habitus characteristic of adolescent-onset chronic stress.

---

## 2. MATRICIDE EVENT — SOMATIC SEQUELAE (AGE ~9)

The witnessed killing of Rebecca Banner by Brian Banner, with the subject restrained or knocked aside (accounts in the recovered material vary slightly), is recorded as the central traumatic somatic event of the pre-gamma life. The subject sustained a closed head injury in this episode — concussive in severity, with brief loss of consciousness, no imaging obtained at the time. Subsequent migraine pattern (cluster-type with photophobia and prodromal scotoma, lateralized left) dates from this incident and recurs across the adult record at moments of stress and recovered-memory work. He has self-medicated migraines with acetaminophen across his adult life, never opiates, never triptans — the avoidance of stronger pharmacology being part of his lifelong refusal of disinhibitors and altered states.

He developed, in the months after the killing and the father's commitment, a startle response that has never remitted: a full-body flinch with bilateral upper-extremity guarding, present in adult footage from Avengers debriefings, SHIELD interviews, and informal recordings. Closing doors, dropped objects, raised voices, and male footfalls behind him produce the response reliably. He has trained the visible startle down over decades but the autonomic component — measurable HR jump, palmar diaphoresis, brief breath-hold — is preserved and is one of the most consistent somatic findings across the file.

---

## 3. ADOLESCENT AND YOUNG-ADULT MEDICAL HISTORY (1949–1961)

The subject lived with maternal aunt Susan Drake from approximately age ten until college matriculation. The medical record from this period is sparse — the aunt was attentive but the subject was a clinically silent patient who concealed symptoms. Documented presentations: one episode of "stomach pain" at age twelve diagnosed as gastritis (likely stress-related; he has had a chronically reactive upper GI tract since); a hand laceration at age fourteen requiring sutures, mechanism listed as "broken glass" (his account, never elaborated); orthodontic work for the previously noted crown maintenance; standard vaccinations on schedule.

His undergraduate years at Penn State and graduate years at Desert State / Caltech (the canon varies on the institution; the file records both) include the first appearance of what would become a lifelong pattern: episodes of profound exhaustion alternating with periods of near-sleepless hyper-productivity, never reaching DSM bipolar criteria but consistent with a trauma-dysregulated arousal system. He was, in laboratory observation, the graduate student who would be found at his desk at four a.m. having not eaten since the previous noon, with three pages of equations done, no recollection of having sat down to begin.

**Pre-incident adult somatic baseline (1960–1962):** 5'9", 128 lb (BMI 18.9, low-normal), resting HR documented in his Project Greenskin physical at 78 (elevated for his fitness level — a tachycardic baseline that the file's subsequent thirty years of HR awareness would obsess over), BP 118/76, no significant labs, no medications, no allergies recorded, no surgical history, no substance use. Visual acuity 20/20 uncorrected at intake; he began wearing reading glasses by age thirty.

He had, in the year before the incident, lost approximately eleven pounds — eating poorly, working obsessively on the gamma device, in tension with Betty Ross and in active aversion-contact with her father. He arrived at the Project Greenskin test site clinically underweight, sleep-deprived, and (the pre-detonation interview footage shows it plainly) dissociating intermittently during the briefing — staring through interlocutors, missing direct questions, recovering with a brief head-shake.

---

## 4. THE GAMMA INCIDENT — ACUTE EXPOSURE (NOVEMBER 1962)

The detonation event has been reconstructed in extraordinary detail by subsequent investigators. Operative facts: the subject, observing an unauthorized civilian (Richard Jones) on the test range, broke containment, drove a Jeep approximately 0.4 miles into the blast footprint, physically threw Jones into a protective trench, and remained exposed during the detonation. Estimated acute dose: in conventional radiobiological terms, on the order of tens to hundreds of grays whole-body, which is to say a dose at which no human organism survives. The subject did not die.

**Acute presentation (first 72 hours):** vomiting, transient erythema, no acute radiation syndrome of the conventional sequence; isolated in a base infirmary under armed observation; first transformation occurred at dusk of day one (the Lee-Kirby original frame: the gamma effect was initially circadian, triggered by sunset, before later writers reframed it to autonomic arousal). The transformation itself, in the subject's recollection (recovered piecemeal across the canon), is experienced as a wave of cardiovascular distress — pounding chest, heat, tunnel vision, a sense of "falling into" something — followed by amnestic discontinuity. He woke nude, in restraints that had failed, with the infirmary destroyed and one orderly hospitalized. He had no memory of the intervening hours.

**Chronic post-incident somatics:** the gamma exposure restructured the subject's biology in ways that have never been fully characterized. Cellular regeneration vastly accelerated; resting cardiovascular and metabolic function essentially normalized into the baseline of a healthy adult male, the chronic childhood-stress signature finally relieved (his pre-incident anemia resolved; his weight stabilized at approximately 145 lb; the migraine pattern persisted but the gastritis remitted). The subject is, in his Banner-state body, healthier than he has ever been. The transformation, when it comes, occurs in seconds: mass increase by a factor of five to fifteen (variable, alter-dependent), height to between seven and eight feet (Savage and Professor states) or larger (Worldbreaker emergent states), with corresponding endocrine, skeletal, dermal, and pigmentation changes that violate every constraint of conservation. The conventional medical literature has no framework for this and has stopped trying. The relevant question for this file is what the subject *experiences*, which is: a roar in the ears, a sense of the body being taken from him, and then nothing — until he wakes, sometimes hours, sometimes days, sometimes months later, in a different place, often a different country, his clothes torn, blood (not always his) on him, and the news cycle full of footage he cannot bear to watch.

---

## 5. THE TRANSFORMATION CYCLE — SOMATIC AND PSYCHOLOGICAL IMPACT

Each transformation episode functions, for the host, as a discrete medical event of which the following are constant features:

**Pre-episode prodrome.** Tachycardia (the subject's self-monitored "above 110" threshold, obsessively tracked from the mid-1980s onward with successive generations of wristworn pulse monitors); diaphoresis, particularly on the palms and upper lip; flushing of the neck and ears; a particular pattern of capillary dilation in the sclera that close observers (Samson, Betty) have learned to read; tremor in the dominant hand; speech slowing as cortical resources are diverted to suppression; the subject's characteristic verbal tic — *"You're making me angry. You wouldn't like me when I'm angry"* and its dozens of variants — which is, read clinically, a desperate de-escalation protocol toward an interlocutor and simultaneously a self-soothing incantation to delay the switch.

**Switch.** Approximately three to fifteen seconds, depending on which alter is emerging and how aggressively the host has resisted. Savage emergence is fastest. Professor emergence (during the Merged period) was slower and more graduated, sometimes describable as a "stepping forward" rather than a rupture. Devil Hulk emergence, when it has happened in the canonical record, is preceded by a period of profound stillness — the host's eyes go flat, his speech stops, and the transformation proceeds almost gently.

**Episode.** Variable duration; minimum minutes, maximum the entire *Planet Hulk* exile. The host is, in clinical terms, absent. There is no continuous memory bridge. Fragmentary impressions are sometimes recovered in dreams or in deep therapy work — "I remember the cold," "I remember a child crying," "I remember running" — but these are the texture of dissociated material, not narrative recall.

**Post-episode.** Sudden retransformation, typically with collapse; the body has just lost two hundred to two thousand pounds of mass in seconds and the cardiovascular response is, by anyone's account, brutal. The subject wakes hypotensive, profoundly hypoglycemic (he eats voraciously after episodes when food is available — pancakes and eggs being the recurring canonical image), thermally dysregulated (often cold, shivering), and disoriented. He is almost always nude or in shredded remnants of clothing. Genital exposure, sleeping in fields and gutters, waking under the gaze of strangers — these are the recurring shame-images of his life and a chronic re-traumatization that the file cannot overstate. He has developed coping habits: traveling with cached clothing in plastic bags buried at known coordinates; cultivating contacts in dozens of cities who will provide pants without questions; the famous "purple pants" being a wardrobe choice driven entirely by elasticity and visibility (he could find them again when he came down).

**The shame-flight cycle.** Post-episode, the subject's first cognition once oriented is invariably an accounting of damage. He has, over decades, developed an almost compulsive ritual of finding a newspaper, a radio, an internet connection, anything, to determine what the Hulk has done and to whom. The resulting affect — shame, horror, self-loathing — is the somatic-psychiatric injury of each transformation, layered on top of the literal bodily aftermath. He then flees. He has fled, by reasonable count, in excess of three hundred times in the canonical record. The flight pattern is itself a medical event: weeks of undernutrition, exposure, sleeping rough, untreated minor wounds, until he stabilizes somewhere new and the cycle resets.

---

## 6. SPECIFIC INJURY RECORD (POST-INCIDENT, NON-EXHAUSTIVE)

The subject has sustained, in Hulk state, injuries that would constitute the lethal medical record of any other organism. Selected entries:

- **Multiple gunshot wounds**, hundreds of incidents, calibers from .22 to anti-materiel rifle rounds, the latter producing temporary penetration that closes within seconds.
- **Tank rounds, direct impacts**, repeatedly, beginning with the earliest Ross pursuit operations and continuing through every iteration of military containment effort.
- **Nuclear detonation, direct exposure** (the Abomination-related incident, the New Mexico event, the *Immortal Hulk* gamma bomb), survived without persistent injury to the alter and without measurable additional psychological injury to the host beyond what is constant.
- **Orbital reentry, unprotected**, multiple occasions; the *World War Hulk* return is the documented exemplar.
- **Submersion to abyssal depths**; survived.
- **Disintegration and reformation events**, documented in *Immortal Hulk* and earlier in Pak's work; phenomenologically a dissociative experience of indescribable horror in the host fragments that retain awareness.
- **Vivisection**, recorded under the Shadow Base captivity, with full host awareness during recovery — among the most psychologically damaging episodes in the file and one that recapitulates with appalling fidelity the original paternal violation: a male authority figure cuts into him while he is restrained, awake, unable to escape, and ashamed.

Each of these heals. None of them stops occurring. The cumulative effect on the host — who must live with the knowledge of what has been done to his body even though the alter took the impact — is the slow-motion accumulation of a trauma load that ordinary humans simply do not survive long enough to acquire.

**Banner-state injuries** (i.e., damage sustained in host phenotype, before any transformation reflex can engage): blunt-force injuries from falls and beatings during fugue-state arrivals in unfamiliar locations; one documented stab wound to the right flank (Las Vegas, mid-Fixit era, transitional); cigarette burns to the dorsal forearms from one captivity incident; chronic wear from sleeping rough — sun damage on the posterior neck, plantar fasciitis from years of walking in poor footwear, recurrent dental abscesses untreated for months at a time, parasitic infections acquired in Central and South American travel. He has self-treated most of these. He is a competent autodidact in field medicine and has performed minor sutures on himself with whatever was available.

---

## 7. SUBSTANCES — A FORENSIC ABSENCE

The subject is teetotal. He has never, in any canonical account, voluntarily consumed alcohol in his adult life as Banner. He does not drink coffee — a striking habit-absence for a physicist of his generation — having determined in his twenties that caffeine elevated his resting HR enough to be intolerable. He drinks tea, weakly brewed, almost exclusively. He does not smoke; has never smoked. He does not use recreational drugs. He has refused, across decades of medical encounters, benzodiazepines, opioids, and any sedating prescription not absolutely required, citing the transformation risk but driven, more fundamentally, by a horror of being not-himself that predates the gamma incident and is the central organizing principle of his life. He will not be his father. His father drank. He will not drink.

The Grey Hulk / Fixit alter, conversely, drinks bourbon, smokes, frequents casinos, propositions women. The disinhibited functions have been entirely externalized into the alter system; the host carries the rigid abstinence and the alter discharges everything the abstinence forbids. This is the cleanest single example of dissociative splitting in the file.

**Psychiatric medication trials.** Doc Samson initiated, in the late 1980s, a trial of unspecified mood stabilizer; discontinued after the subject reported (and Samson confirmed) that the medication blunted host affect enough to lower the threshold for switch rather than raise it. A later trial with SSRIs during the Pantheon period produced anorgasmia and worsened the Betty-relationship strain; discontinued. The subject has, since approximately 2000, declined all psychotropic pharmacology and has relied on meditation, breath work, somatic regulation techniques (counted exhalation, peripheral-vision broadening, cold-water face immersion to invoke the diving reflex and depress HR), and intermittent talk therapy when available. The breath protocol is constant; he runs it under stress, in conversation, in laboratory work, often without awareness that he is doing it. Close observers note the four-count inhale, seven-count exhale rhythm beneath his speech in any tense exchange.

---

## 8. SUICIDALITY — THE DEFENDERS BULLET AND ITS LINEAGE

The documented suicide attempt with a specially constructed projectile, conducted in solitude and aborted by the Hulk's emergence (the projectile struck, the alter formed around the wound, the host survived), is the most explicit instance of a recurrent pattern: the subject's ideation that the world would be safer without him, weighed against the empirical fact that his body refuses to permit cessation. Other entries in the suicidality record include passive ideation across virtually every Banner-narrated arc; deliberate exposure to lethal hazards reframed as altruism (driving into volcanic events, standing on collapsing structures, accepting missions with no return projection); and the *Immortal Hulk*-era confrontation with the fact of literal inability to die — which the subject experienced not as relief but as a closing-off of the last available exit and a deepening of the existential injury.

The psychological impact of failed death is itself iatrogenic. Each attempt confirms his unworthiness even of escape; each survival reinforces the Devil Hulk's narrative that he is being kept alive to suffer, by something that has him and will not release him.

---

## 9. REPRODUCTIVE AND SEXUAL HEALTH

Documented sexual history with Betty Ross, intermittent, complicated throughout by the subject's chronic fear of transformation during arousal (the autonomic overlap is the obvious problem and one the subject has discussed with Samson in extant therapy transcripts). The pregnancies are canonically complex; the subject has lost at least one child to events surrounding his condition, with attendant grief responses that have produced major decompensations. Genetic counseling — that he sought, repeatedly, after the gamma incident — established the heritability concern as real and unresolved; this knowledge structures his approach to all reproductive possibility and is a chronic source of his self-monstering. He has used barrier contraception with absolute consistency outside marriage to Betty.

The Fixit alter's sexual conduct is separate and is, from the host's later-recovered awareness of it, a source of significant shame.

---

## 10. CURRENT MEDICAL STATUS (NARRATIVE PRESENT)

Subject is, in Banner state, physically healthy. Resting HR runs at 62, on his current monitor. BP 116/74. He is mildly underweight by his own standard, eats erratically, sleeps poorly (four to five hours in fragmented blocks, frequent vivid dreams with content consistent with traumatic re-experiencing). He has the migraine pattern, the bruxism, the startle, the GI reactivity, the chronic mild thoracic kyphosis of a man who has spent sixty years making himself small. He has, on the dorsum of his left hand, a small scar he does not remember acquiring and which is older than the gamma incident.

He has, in the alter system, a body that cannot be killed by conventional means and has been killed by unconventional ones, repeatedly, and returned. The medical history of that body is the medical history of every catastrophe it has been sent or thrown into across six decades.

The body he inhabits between these events — the Banner body, the small body, the body that was the abused child's body and remains, in posture and habit and breath, that child's body still — is the body of a man with a chronic, untreated, profoundly serious illness who has nevertheless walked out of every clinic he has ever entered and gone back to work.


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT: BANNER, ROBERT BRUCE, PhD

*The body of a man who has spent forty adult years trying not to be in it. What follows is the granular bodily record — the file a continuous-observation apparatus would compile across decades of footage, medical telemetry, surveillance photography, and intimate-partner debrief. The subject's somatic life is organized around a single problem: every involuntary signal his body generates is also a potential trigger for catastrophic transformation. He has therefore developed the most exhaustively self-monitored body in the file.*

---

## 1. BASELINE MORPHOLOGY AND CARRIAGE

The subject is approximately 5'9½", and across the entire surveillance record has fluctuated between 128 and 142 lbs in the host state — chronically underweight for height, with a body-mass profile more consistent with a long-distance runner or a recovering anorectic than a man in his forties. Shoulders narrow, clavicles prominent, sternal notch visible in any open-collar shirt. Forearms wiry, with the distinctive cabled musculature of someone who clenches a great deal. Hands disproportionately large for the frame, knuckles slightly enlarged (chronic micro-trauma from clenching, not from striking). Posterior cervical musculature is hypertonic on palpation across every medical exam in the record; the subject carries his stress in the trapezius and suboccipital triangle, and a trained observer can read his arousal level from the visible tension at the base of his skull.

**Resting carriage.** Slightly forward-leaning thoracic posture — what physical therapists call protective rounding, the body of someone who has spent decades minimizing his apparent size and presenting a smaller target. Head carriage is forward of the shoulder line by 2–4 cm. Chin tucked. Eyes habitually directed downward and at a 15–20° offset from any interlocutor — almost never direct sustained gaze in baseline. When seated, knees together, feet flat, hands folded in lap or wrapped around a coffee mug; he occupies the smallest possible volume of any chair.

**Gait.** Short stride, low arm swing, soft heel strike — the gait of a man who has trained himself not to make noise. Pace is brisk but not hurried; he walks with a forward inclination that reads as urgency to the casual observer but is actually the gait of someone going somewhere he hopes not to be noticed leaving. He does not stop and stand in open spaces; he edges along walls, takes the perimeter of rooms, sits with his back to a corner. This is hypervigilance, not tradecraft, though it has functionally become tradecraft.

---

## 2. THE FACE

The subject's face is the most surveilled feature in the file because it is the early-warning system. Several patterns are consistent across decades of observation.

**Resting affect.** Mild, slightly sad, attentive. The mouth held in a closed, soft line with a faint downturn at the corners. Eyebrows slightly elevated at the medial ends — the brow position of chronic mild distress, sometimes called Darwin's grief muscle. This is the subject's *neutral*. Photographs of him at rest are routinely read by observers as "tired" or "worried"; this is simply his face.

**Smile.** Asymmetrical, brief, almost always closed-mouth in baseline. The right corner lifts marginally higher than the left. Genuine Duchenne smiling — orbicularis oculi engagement — is documented only in a handful of contexts: with Betty Ross in unguarded moments, with Rick Jones in the early years, with Jennifer Walters, occasionally over a successful equation. The smile is rapid in onset and rapid in decay; it never lingers. Within 1–2 seconds the face has returned to baseline, often with a small downward glance, as if the smile itself were a transgression he has caught himself committing.

**Eyes.** Mid-color, often photographed as appearing greener under fluorescent light and browner in tungsten. Blink rate at baseline approximately 18–22 per minute (normal-high); rises to 30+ under stress; drops sharply (to 6–10) in the seconds immediately before a transformation, when autonomic systems are being captured by the alter switch. This drop is the most reliable single facial pre-transformation marker in the file. The pupils dilate prior to switch — readable at conversational distance.

**Micro-expressions.** The subject has, through decades of self-monitoring, achieved a degree of facial control unusual outside of trained operatives. He suppresses anger so completely that the standard FACS anger configuration (AU4 brow lower, AU5 lid raise, AU7 lid tighten, AU23 lip tighten) is essentially absent from his repertoire — when the anger comes, it comes not as expression but as the switch. What does leak: AU1+AU4 (the sadness/distress configuration) at exceptionally high rates; AU14 (dimpler / contempt) almost never directed outward and frequently self-directed in mirror behavior; AU17 (chin raiser, the pouting/suppression marker) immediately before he stops speaking. He swallows his sentences. Watch for AU17 followed by a downward glance and a small head shake: this is him deciding not to say what he was going to say. He does this perhaps 40–60 times per recorded hour of casual conversation.

**Jaw.** Chronic masseter hypertrophy on dental exam — he clenches asleep and awake. Bruxism documented. The jaw is the second early-warning site after the suboccipitals; a visible flex of the masseter under the cheekbone, sustained for more than 2 seconds, is a pre-arousal indicator.

---

## 3. THE HANDS

The subject's hands are the most expressive part of him and the part he controls least successfully. They tell the story the face is suppressing.

**Baseline.** When not occupied, hands clasp loosely in front of the body or behind it; when seated, fingers interlace in his lap with thumbs touching, a self-soothing posture documented from childhood photographs onward. He does not gesticulate broadly; gestures are small, kept close to the torso, fingers often slightly curled.

**Tells.**
- **Index-finger-and-thumb rub** — pad of the thumb against the lateral edge of the index finger, repetitive, often unilateral (right hand). This is his primary self-regulation tic; observed across every era of the record. Frequency rises sharply with cognitive load and with proximity to triggers. Counting the rubs per minute is a quantitative arousal proxy.
- **Knuckle press** — interlaced hands, presses the pad of one thumb hard into the opposite palm or into the dorsal surface of the opposite hand. Pain as grounding. Often produces visible blanching.
- **Wedding ring / watch fidget** — across periods when he has worn a ring or a watch, he rotates it, slides it on the finger, taps the watch face. In ringless periods this displaces to the cuff of his shirt, which he tugs and adjusts compulsively.
- **The pen click** — when seated at a desk, persistent retractable-pen actuation, at a rate that correlates near-linearly with his cortisol levels. Colleagues across institutions report it as his most recognizable signature.
- **Pulse check** — the single most diagnostic tic in the file. The subject takes his own radial pulse, often without conscious awareness, with the index and middle fingers of the right hand against the left wrist. He does this dozens of times per day. He will pretend to be adjusting his sleeve or his watch; what he is doing is checking heart rate. Across the cardiopulmonary literature this is called *interoceptive monitoring* and in his case it is a compulsion. He does it before entering crowded rooms, before answering phones, after raised voices, before sleep, on waking, in elevators.

**Stress-state hand behavior.** As arousal climbs, the hands progress through a stereotyped sequence: (1) thumb-index rub accelerates; (2) hands separate and one or both find a self-touching anchor (back of neck, bridge of nose, lower face); (3) full hand-over-mouth or hand-pinching-bridge-of-nose with eyes closed; (4) hands drop to grip something — the edge of a desk, the arms of a chair, his own thighs above the knee — with whitened knuckles; (5) the fingers begin to extend involuntarily as the somatic transformation engages. Stage 5 is the point of no return.

**Intimacy-state hand behavior.** Notably different. With Betty Ross in documented unguarded moments, the hands relax in a way they almost never otherwise do — fingers loose, palms open, an unfamiliar slackness through the wrist. He cups her face with his whole hand rather than touching with fingertips. He holds her hand with the fingers interlaced rather than palm-to-palm, which in attachment-coded touch behavior reads as the choice of someone seeking maximal contact rather than minimal commitment. This is the body of a man for whom touch is not assumed.

---

## 4. VOICE AND SPEECH

**Pitch and timbre.** Mid-baritone, soft, with a slight breathiness consistent with chronic shallow breathing. Resonance is anterior — he speaks from the front of the mouth, lips barely opening, a habit consistent with someone who learned not to be loud. Volume baseline is approximately 55–60 dB at one meter, well below conversational norm.

**Cadence.** Slow to begin, accelerates within a sentence, then often trails off before completion. The trailing-off is characteristic: he starts strong, loses confidence in his right to finish the thought, and either pivots into qualification ("I mean, possibly, I don't know") or stops mid-clause. Filled pauses ("um," "uh") cluster at the start of sentences, not the middle — the hesitation is about whether to speak, not what to say.

**Lexical patterns.** Heavy use of hedging ("perhaps," "I suppose," "it might be," "I could be wrong but"); chronic preemptive self-deprecation ("I'm probably overthinking this"); apologetic openings ("sorry, can I — sorry"). The word *sorry* appears in the surveillance corpus at roughly 8–12 times the population-mean frequency. He apologizes for interrupting people who interrupted him.

**Technical register.** When discussing physics or any domain of expertise, every one of the above patterns reverses. Pitch drops, pace steadies, hedging disappears, volume rises to normal, eye contact extends to multi-second sustained gaze. This is the only context in which the subject's voice carries the natural authority of his intelligence. It is, not coincidentally, the only context in which he is operating purely above the dissociated material.

**Stress register.** As arousal climbs, the voice flattens — affect drains from the prosody, intonation becomes monotone, sentences shorten, articulation tightens. Approaching transformation, the voice drops half an octave and acquires a strained quality as the laryngeal musculature engages with whole-body tension. The final pre-transformation utterances are typically warnings — "you need to go," "get away from me," "I can't —" — delivered in this tight, low, abbreviated voice.

**Alter voice.** Distinct. The Savage state speaks at a pitch and resonance the host's anatomy cannot produce; the Grey/Fixit state speaks with an entirely different prosodic profile — flatter, faster, with a different regional coloring; the Professor state speaks in the host's voice but without the hedging, without the apology, and with a fluency the host never achieves. The Devil voice, when heard in dreams and in the subject's own self-reports, is described as his father's.

---

## 5. RESPIRATION AND CARDIAC PATTERNS

**Baseline respiration.** Shallow, thoracic-dominant, with a respiratory rate of 16–20 — at the high end of normal even at rest. Diaphragmatic excursion is minimal. He has known about this for decades; it is the subject of the meditation and breathing regimens he has pursued across the record (vipassana, pranayama, zazen, biofeedback, varied periods of practice with the monks of K'un-Lun and other traditions).

**Trained breathing.** When he is exercising his containment regime — which is most of his waking life — he performs paced box-breathing (4-in / 4-hold / 6-out / 2-hold) with the regularity of a metronome. Observable in any sustained video as a slow, deliberate chest-and-abdomen rhythm; he counts internally. In conversation he will sometimes briefly stop responding to perform a full breath cycle and then resume — what reads to interlocutors as thoughtfulness is in fact pharmacological self-regulation.

**Heart rate.** The single most monitored parameter in his life. Resting HR is 58–64 (athletically low for his fitness level — the product of obsessive vagal training, not aerobic conditioning). His functional threshold — the rate above which transformation risk becomes acute — has historically been characterized in the canon at around 200 bpm, but the operationally relevant figure is the rate at which his self-monitoring becomes panicked, which is approximately 110. Above 110, behavior changes visibly: he begins to count breaths aloud, seeks an exit, requests space, removes himself from rooms. He wears a heart-rate monitor under his shirt almost constantly across the modern record; it is the only consistent piece of jewelry-grade hardware on his body.

---

## 6. SLEEP

Sleep is the single most disturbed domain of the subject's somatic life and the one in which his condition is least controllable.

**Architecture.** Sleep-lab data across multiple eras shows fragmented sleep with markedly reduced slow-wave (Stage 3) proportion, frequent micro-arousals (15–25 per hour), and REM density well above population mean. He spends an unusual proportion of the night in REM, and his REM sleep is unstable — frequent REM-without-atonia events have been recorded, consistent with REM behavior disorder, and almost certainly the proximal substrate for the documented nocturnal transformations of the early record.

**Sleep onset.** Difficult. Subject reports across decades that he is afraid to fall asleep. Sleep latency in observation is 45–90 minutes; he reads (technical journals, never fiction past 11 PM — fiction "lets things in"), performs breathing exercises, and resists sleep until exhaustion overcomes vigilance. He prefers to sleep sitting up or semi-reclined; multiple safehouse observations record him asleep in chairs, against walls, in the corners of rooms.

**Sleep position.** When supine, fetal-curled on the right side, knees drawn, one hand under the cheek, the other tucked between the knees — a self-containing posture observed by every long-term intimate in the record. Often a pillow or blanket is held against the abdomen.

**Dreams.** When he reports them — which is rarely, and only in therapeutic contexts — they cluster around three themes: the matricide scene, sometimes recurring with variation; pursuit by an unseen large figure; and conversations with a figure who is sometimes his father, sometimes the Devil-Hulk alter, in which he is small and the figure is large. Night terrors documented in childhood records; reduced in frequency in adulthood but never absent. He sleep-talks; he grinds his teeth; he sometimes wakes with his own hand clenched in his hair.

**Waking.** Sharp, full-system arousal — no grogginess. Eyes open, pulse check at the wrist within 3 seconds of waking, orientation check (where am I, what day is it, am I clothed, is anyone hurt) within 10 seconds. He does not lie in bed. He is upright within 30 seconds of consciousness in 80%+ of observed wakings.

---

## 7. EATING AND ORAL PATTERNS

**Volume.** Chronically under-eats. Single meals are small, slowly consumed, often abandoned. He skips meals when working, sometimes for 24–36 hours, with no apparent awareness of hunger — interoceptive blunting for hunger consistent with the broader pattern of disowned bodily signals.

**Food choices.** Bland-tendency. Plain rice, eggs, bread, tea. Vegetarian for substantial periods of the record (the discipline reads as both ethical and self-punitive). Avoids red meat. Avoids spicy food — likely because spice produces autonomic flushing, sweating, and elevated HR, all of which his monitoring system codes as pre-transformation signals. Will eat what is offered out of courtesy and apologize for not finishing.

**Tea.** The signature beverage. He prefers green tea, made with water below boiling, steeped 90 seconds, no additives. Holds the cup with both hands, often at sternum height, near the face — a self-soothing posture, the cup functioning as both warmth and barrier. Across the surveillance corpus he is photographed holding a tea cup more often than not.

**Alcohol.** Abstinent. Will accept a glass at social functions and not drink it; will sometimes wet his lips and set it down. The single most consistent abstention in the record, with the etiology obvious — his father's alcoholism, his fear of disinhibition, the alter-state correspondences.

**Caffeine.** Moderate. Tea, occasionally coffee in laboratory contexts. He is sensitive to it; over-caffeination produces tremor and tachycardia, which produces panic, which produces transformation risk. He has self-titrated for decades.

**Tobacco / drugs.** None. The longest-running and most rigorously enforced abstentions in the file. Brief documented periods of prescribed sedatives (chlorpromazine, benzodiazepines, lithium across various therapeutic regimes); the subject discontinues these compulsively because they blunt the self-monitoring he depends on.

**Oral tics.** Lip-biting (lower lip, left side); tongue against the inside of the cheek during thought; light teeth-grinding under stress. Frequent throat-clearing immediately before speaking — a vocal-cord engagement check, the somatic version of his lexical hedging.

---

## 8. GROOMING AND DRESS

**Hair.** Dark, fine, kept short but not stylishly so — the haircut of a man who finds barbers difficult and reschedules; cuts run 6–10 weeks. Self-cuts with scissors documented in safehouse periods. No gel, no product, parted with fingers in the morning. Goes gray at the temples first; he does not color it.

**Facial hair.** Variable. Clean-shaven in institutional periods (universities, S.H.I.E.L.D., laboratory contexts); stubble-to-short-beard in fugitive periods; full beard in the longest withdrawals. He shaves with a safety razor, not an electric — the slowness is the point; it is part of his morning regulation routine. Cuts himself rarely (steady hands when controlled). When stubble develops, he touches it: a flat palm passing over the jaw, downward, a self-soothing gesture that also functions as a tactile reality-check.

**Dress.** Conservative, plain, deliberately unremarkable. The signature is the purple shirt across certain eras — but in the operational baseline, the wardrobe is button-down shirts in muted colors (lavender, slate, white, pale blue, occasionally olive), worn untucked, sleeves rolled to mid-forearm, top button open. Trousers loose-fit, brown or grey, often slightly too large (he is sized for a heavier body he expects to need to fit when he reverts). Belt cinched extra notches. Soft-soled shoes — desert boots, plain leather lace-ups, occasionally sneakers — selected for quiet and replaceability. He does not wear jewelry beyond a watch (analog, often a cheap one — he loses or destroys watches monthly), and a wedding ring when married. Pockets carry: cash in small bills, a notepad, a pen, a small folding knife (utility, not weapon), keys on a single ring with no fobs or identifiers, and across decades, a folded card with names and phone numbers in case of dissociative episode.

**Glasses.** Worn for reading and close work; mild myopia, modest astigmatism. He cleans them compulsively with the tail of his shirt — perhaps the most common single grooming behavior in his repertoire — and the gesture (glasses off, two-handed shirt-tail polish, glasses inspected, glasses on, brief blink) is a thinking ritual as much as a hygienic one.

**Hygiene.** Meticulous in stable periods, lapsing in fugitive ones. Showers long and hot (the heat is sedating); soap is unscented; no cologne — scent is sensory load. Nails kept short and clean, sometimes bitten in high-stress periods (cuticles, more than nails).

---

## 9. SEXUAL AND INTIMATE BEHAVIOR

The most carefully suppressed domain in the somatic record. Sexual arousal is autonomic arousal; autonomic arousal is transformation risk; the subject has therefore organized his erotic life around the avoidance of his erotic life.

**Libido.** Present but inhibited. The subject's pre-incident affect already suggested low expression of erotic energy; post-incident, the inhibition is structural and conscious. He has spoken across the canon of his fear of intimacy with Betty Ross — not metaphorically but somatically. The fear is that orgasm itself, with its associated sympathetic surge, will trigger transformation.

**With Betty Ross.** The only sustained sexual relationship in the record. Documented intimacy across multiple eras; the subject's pattern is prolonged tenderness, extended kissing, extended holding, with the genital phase carefully managed via the breathing regimens described above. He has reported (in confidential therapeutic context recovered into the published record) practicing the same paced breathing during sex that he practices in lab and meditation. When the relationship has been physically successful it has been because Betty has been willing and able to be the regulating presence in the encounter — to slow him, to ground him, to keep his eyes on her face.

**The Grey alter.** Sexual behavior of the Grey/Fixit alter is markedly different — disinhibited, transactional, casino-and-cocktail-coded, with the appetitive drive split entirely from the host. This is the dissociation of erotic life as such: the host cannot have it, so a state was generated that could.

**Touch tolerance.** Variable. Casual touch from non-intimates produces a small visible flinch — a 100-ms shoulder retraction and a controlled non-response. He does not initiate handshakes; he completes them when offered. He does not hug; he accepts hugs with arms loose. With Betty, with Rick Jones, with She-Hulk, the threshold collapses and he becomes a tactilely seeking person — leans into shoulder contact, accepts head on shoulder, returns embraces fully. The contrast between guarded touch with the world and unguarded touch with intimates is one of the more poignant single dimensions of the file.

---

## 10. MICRO-MOVEMENT AND ENVIRONMENTAL BEHAVIOR

**Spatial habits.** Always knows where the exits are. On entering any room, performs a brief sweep — eyes scan left, right, ceiling, identifies exits, identifies populated areas. Selects a seat with back to wall and line of sight to door. Does not sit at the head of a table. Does not sit at the center. Sits at the corner nearest the exit.

**Distance keeping.** Maintains greater interpersonal distance than the cultural norm — roughly 1.2–1.5 meters in conversation versus the American norm of ~0.7. Steps back when others step in. Compensates with attentive face and warm voice so the distancing reads as thoughtful rather than cold.

**Object handling.** Gentle to the


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS — BANNER, R.B.

## 1. Attachment Classification and Its Developmental Source

The subject's attachment organization is **disorganized-fearful** (Main & Solomon's Type D in childhood; Bartholomew & Horowitz's fearful-avoidant quadrant in adult typology), with strong secondary features of **anxious-preoccupied** activation under proximity and **dismissive-avoidant** retreat under threat. The disorganization is etiologically overdetermined: the same caregiver dyad (Rebecca and Brian Banner) housed both his safe-haven figure and his terror-source, and the safe-haven figure was killed by the terror-source in his presence. The neurobehavioral signature of disorganized attachment — simultaneous activation of the approach and flight systems toward the same object — became, in the subject's case, somatic. He does not merely *feel* the contradiction of wanting and fearing closeness; under sufficient proximity he literally splits at the body level into the approach-figure (Banner: soft, apologetic, hand-extending) and the flight-or-attack figure (the Hulk alter complex: large, repelling, removing distance by force).

Three developmental facts are load-bearing for everything that follows.

**First**, the mother was lost during the consolidation window for self-other differentiation and was lost *while attempting to protect him*. The template installed is: those who love me are killed for loving me. This is not a metaphor for the subject's behavior — it is the operational rule by which he organizes adult intimacy. Every sustained departure from a loved object is, at the unconscious level, a protective act.

**Second**, the father not only beat the child but did so under the delusional belief that the child was *contaminated*, *monstrous*, *not-fully-human*. The subject thus had the experience, from preverbal periods forward, of being looked at by his primary male attachment figure and seen as a thing-to-be-destroyed. This installs the **monster identity** at the level on which one ordinarily installs basic mirroring. The introject does not say "you are bad"; it says, in the father's exact register, *"you are the Hulk and you always were."* This is the diagnostic content of the Devil Hulk's speeches.

**Third**, the post-matricide arrangement — coerced perjury, aunt's household, trauma never spoken — taught the child that survival in relationships requires the suppression of his own history. He learned to enter every new bond with the foundational data of his self redacted. Every adult relationship in the file is therefore built on a partial subject; rupture occurs reliably at the moment the redacted material surfaces.

## 2. The Bonding Sequence — Stages and Tells

The subject's mode of forming attachment is sufficiently stereotyped across six decades to be charted as a phase sequence.

**Phase I — Soft Approach (weeks to months).** Initial contact is characterized by a recognizable cluster of micro-behaviors: averted gaze with brief upward checks, near-inaudible vocal volume that forces the other to lean in (a covert intimacy-elicitor he is not aware of using), hands clasped or pocketed, the verbal tic of pre-emptive self-deprecation ("I'm not — I'm not really good at —"), and a marked tendency to compliment the other person's competence as an opening relational move. He metabolizes attention from women through scientific or task-shared framing — labs, fieldwork, problems-to-solve — because shared instrumental focus permits proximity without the autonomic load of pure relational gaze. This is the courtship register he ran with Betty Ross, with Jennifer Walters (cousin, but the same affiliative grammar), with Jarella, with Marlo Chandler in the Grey period (filtered through the alter, but structurally identical), and, in muted instrumental form, with every team handler he has ever accepted (Samson, Fury, occasionally Stark).

**Phase II — Disclosure Asymmetry.** As the bond deepens, the subject draws extensive autobiographical information from the other while disclosing almost nothing reciprocally. He is an excellent listener — patient, non-judgmental, retentive — and this is partly genuine care and partly a defensive maneuver: as long as the conversation is on the other person, his own redacted history is not in play. The first significant rupture in any of his relationships occurs at the moment this asymmetry becomes too pronounced to ignore and the other person presses for disclosure. His response is uniform across the record: visible startle (heart-rate elevation is the somatic tell), a half-step back, a deflection-by-physics or deflection-by-apology, and, within hours to days, a flight episode.

**Phase III — Approach-Avoidance Oscillation.** Once the subject has admitted attachment, he begins the cycle that defines every long bond he has formed. Periods of high proximity (cohabitation, joint work, sexual contact in the Betty record) alternate with abrupt withdrawals — geographic, communicative, or affective. The withdrawals are not negotiated; they are enacted, typically at night, often with a written note rather than spoken farewell. The hand-written departure note is so frequent across the canon it functions as a relational signature: he can write what he cannot say. The note is invariably some variant of *I'm doing this because I love you; do not look for me.* This is the matricide rule operationalized.

**Phase IV — Distant Maintenance.** After flight, the subject maintains the bond at a tolerable distance through small acts: anonymous monetary transfers (documented in the David and Pak runs — money sent to Betty, to Marlo, to the aunt), strategically timed reappearances at thresholds of the other's life (weddings, funerals, illness), and a habit of intelligence-gathering from afar (he tracks Betty's life with a precision that, in any non-trauma frame, would read as stalking; in the trauma frame, it is vigil). He cannot be present and he cannot leave; he therefore hovers.

**Phase V — Catastrophic Re-entry.** Eventually, almost always under crisis (her endangerment, his pursuit, a third party's attack on the shared circle), he returns at high arousal. Re-entry is somatically charged, frequently produces transformation, and re-anchors the bond at a higher level of mutual dependency and lower level of mutual safety. The cycle then restarts at Phase III.

## 3. Trust — Architecture and Failure Modes

Trust, in the subject's economy, is bifurcated. He extends **task trust** generously and almost without screening — he will hand sensitive scientific work, his own physiological data, his location, and his cooperation to near-strangers if a problem-frame is established. He extends **affective trust** almost not at all, and when he does extend it, he extends it totally and to one person at a time. This is the developmental signature of a child who had exactly one safe person (mother) and lost her: the adult cannot distribute affective trust across a network; he can only invest it in a single object, which makes the loss of that object catastrophic and the protection of that object overriding.

The failure modes of his trust are also stereotyped.

- **Betrayal by paternal-coded figures** — Ross most centrally, but also institutional fathers (the Army, SHIELD command at intervals, Hydra-infiltrated structures, Fury when Fury runs a long game) — produces not rage in the host but **submissive collapse and self-blame**, with the rage routed through the alter. The host's verbal response to discovering betrayal is consistently some form of *"I should have known"* or *"It was my fault for trusting"* — a rule learned in childhood, where trusting his father not to hit him that night was the child's "error."
- **Betrayal by peer figures** (Stark, Richards, Strange, the Illuminati's decision to exile him into space) is the most psychologically destabilizing class of event in the record. It violates the only relational compensation he has — the idea that *colleagues*, men who share his cognitive register, are a safe category — and it directly produces the Worldbreaker organization of the alter, because it gives the dissociated rage a coherent grievance. The relational lesson the subject extracts from the Illuminati exile is foundational and never fully revised: *even men who are like me will dispose of me if I become inconvenient.* This is the father-rule generalized.
- **Betrayal by the attachment figure** (Betty, in her various estrangements, marriages-of-rebound, periods of her own anger at him) is the only class of betrayal he does not respond to with flight. He absorbs it. The reason is structural: she is the mother-substitute, and the matricide rule forbids him from withdrawing from her on his own initiative — he can only leave to protect her, never to punish her.

## 4. How He Betrays

The subject does not betray in the active register — there is no deceit, no instrumental use of others, no withheld information used as leverage. His betrayals are of two kinds, both passive and both characterological.

**Betrayal by absence.** He disappears on people who need him. Children he has fathered or quasi-fathered (Skaar, the Hulk's offspring in various continuities; protégés; team members in crisis) experience the abrupt removal of his presence as the original wound. He cannot stay through the period when his presence would be most stabilizing because that period is also the period of highest autonomic load on him. The betrayal is not chosen; it is the matricide rule executing.

**Betrayal by transformation.** Every intimate of the subject is, at some point, harmed by the alter — directly (struck, thrown, endangered in collapse of a building he has caused) or indirectly (caught in the response that the alter draws). He cannot prevent this and he carries the guilt of every instance, but from the standpoint of the other party, the relational fact is: the person they trusted *became* the thing that harmed them. This is the most particular and unusual feature of his relational record, and it is the somatic literalization of the disorganized attachment dynamic — the safe-haven and the threat-source are the same body.

## 5. Repair

Repair is one of the subject's strengths and one of his traps. He repairs through three reliable mechanisms.

**Sustained patience under the other's anger.** He does not defend, does not counter-blame, does not match heat. He receives the other person's rage with a stillness that is, in part, genuine humility and, in part, the dissociative dampening that keeps him out of his own anger. This is unusually effective relationally — it permits the other to fully discharge — but it is also pathogenic in him, because the un-metabolized affect goes into the system and accumulates toward the next breach.

**Material reparation.** He rebuilds what was broken — literally (he has rebuilt Betty's home, contributed to civic reconstruction in cities he has damaged, paid medical bills anonymously) and figuratively (long letters of accounting, often unsent). The material gesture is partly genuine and partly a substitute for the apology he cannot fully form, because to fully form the apology would require fully owning the alter as himself, which he cannot do without decompensating.

**Therapeutic alliance with witnesses.** Where another person — Samson most clearly, Betty intermittently, in *Immortal Hulk* the figure of Charlene McGowan and the broader treatment-team configuration — is willing to bear witness without flinching, the subject can engage in repair work that approaches genuine integration. The condition is that the witness must not flinch at the alter, must not collude in the splitting (must not love Banner-and-hate-Hulk), and must be able to hold the whole system. The number of people across six decades who have met this bar can be counted on one hand.

The trap is that the subject *over-repairs*. He continues to perform repair after the other person has moved on or has accepted the original injury, because the repair is also a self-soothing of the introject. Long after Betty has forgiven a given episode, he is still building the gesture for it.

## 6. Intimacy and Dependency

Sexual and physical intimacy is the most autonomically loaded category of contact for the subject and is therefore the most defended. The canon is genteel about it, but the longitudinal record is consistent: physical intimacy with Betty is rare, episodic, frequently followed by transformation or by departure, and surrounded by a striking quantity of verbal apology. Periods of stable cohabitation tend to coincide with one of three conditions — (a) the Professor Hulk merged state, in which the dissociative apparatus is temporarily reorganized; (b) the Hulk being suppressed by external means (technological inhibition, pharmacological intervention, Doc Green protocols); or (c) periods of Betty's own altered state (Red She-Hulk), in which she is somatically equipped to absorb his arousal without endangerment. The pattern is diagnostic: intimacy is possible only when the somatic risk is engineered down to zero, which is almost never.

Dependency runs in the opposite direction from what the surface suggests. The subject *appears* to need very little — he can live out of a duffel, work anywhere, eat the same purple-pants-and-rice subsistence diet, sleep on floors. In fact he is profoundly dependent on a small set of relational anchors (Betty above all, then Rick Jones as the inaugural companion-witness, then Samson as the therapeutic figure) and his apparent self-sufficiency is a mask over an attachment system that cannot bear the loss of any of them. The deaths or estrangements of Rick Jones, across his various canonical losses, have produced some of the most pronounced decompensations in the record — disproportionate to the surface relationship, exactly proportionate to the underlying anchor function. Rick was the witness to the original somatic dissociation (the gamma incident itself); to lose Rick is to lose the only person who saw the moment the system formed.

Conversely, others depend on him in a pattern he cannot tolerate and cannot refuse. Younger figures (Rick in early years, Jen Walters at moments, Amadeus Cho, Skaar, the various protégés) attach to him in mentor-register, and he responds with a mixture of genuine care and a low-grade panic, because dependents activate the unprotected-child substrate — the part of him that knows what happens to people who depend on him.

## 7. The Repeated Template — One Relationship, Many Names

The relational template the subject runs is recognizable across every significant bond in the file and can be stated as a single sentence: *I will find a person who can see me, I will love them quietly and at distance, I will be unable to stay close, I will leave to protect them, I will hover, I will return under crisis, I will harm them in returning, I will repair until they forgive me, and then I will leave again.* The names rotate. The shape does not.

- **Betty Ross** is the template in its fullest form — six decades of pursuit, retreat, marriage, estrangement, death, return, transformation into Red She-Hulk, re-estrangement, re-pursuit. Every phase of the sequence above is documented in her arc.
- **Rick Jones** is the template in companion-witness register — guilt-bound attachment ("I owe him my life and he owes me his condition"), long stretches of separation followed by re-anchoring, the same protective withdrawals.
- **Jennifer Walters** is the template in family register, with the additional complication that he transmitted the condition to her in the blood transfusion; the guilt-structure is doubled and the protective distance is correspondingly greater.
- **Jarella** is the template foreshortened — sustained intimacy became possible only in a sub-atomic world where the somatic risk was reduced, and her death (caused by collateral violence in his presence) confirmed the matricide rule with brutal specificity.
- **Doc Samson** is the template in therapeutic register — initial idealization, deep collaboration, eventual ambivalence as Samson's own arc complicated, return to alliance under crisis.
- **Thaddeus Ross** is the inverted template — the paternal-coded figure he cannot leave, the one bond in his life organized around being pursued rather than pursuing, and the relationship in which the alter most reliably emerges, because Ross is the closest available proxy for the father he killed.
- **Brian Banner**, the father himself, is the original and never-completed relationship; every other bond in the file is, in part, an attempt to find a paternal figure who will not be Brian (Ross, repeatedly, fails the test) and a maternal figure who will survive being loved (Betty, repeatedly, almost does).

The Devil Hulk alter is, in the relational frame, the introjected father carried forward as an internal object — a permanent relational presence inside the system, scripted in Brian Banner's voice, hostile, sadistic, paternal. The subject's most stable long-term relationship, in the strict sense of duration and continuity, is therefore with his abuser. The integration work depicted in the late *Immortal Hulk* arc is, in attachment terms, the slow and incomplete renegotiation of that internal relationship from persecution toward something approaching coexistence — the only repair that, if achieved, would free the others.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

## Preface: The Architecture in Overview

The subject's defensive architecture is, in formal terms, a paradox: an individual of demonstrably superior cortical capacity — among the most intellectually gifted humans in the canonical record — whose moment-to-moment ego defenses are drawn almost entirely from the primitive end of Vaillant's hierarchy. This is not a contradiction but a signature. It is the precise pattern produced when a developmentally traumatized child grows into an adult whose neocortex matures around an unhealed limbic wound: the higher functions are recruited *in service of* the primitive defenses rather than replacing them. The subject thinks brilliantly in order to dissociate efficiently. He computes in order not to feel. The architecture is therefore best read as a layered system in which the primitive defenses constitute the load-bearing structure and the mature defenses appear as intermittent ornamentation — present, real, but unable to bear weight under stress.

What follows is an exhaustive inventory, ordered from most primitive (and most operationally central) to most mature (and most operationally fragile), with the somatic, behavioral, and interpersonal expression of each.

---

## I. PRIMITIVE / PSYCHOTIC-LEVEL DEFENSES

### 1. Dissociation — Structural, Somatic, Total

This is the master defense and the organizing fact of the entire case file. In most patients, dissociation operates as a psychic phenomenon: derealization, depersonalization, fugue states without somatic transformation. In the subject, dissociation has achieved somatic literalization: the dissociative switch produces a different body. This is unprecedented in the clinical literature and forces the analyst to read every other defense as auxiliary to this one.

**Behavioral signature in baseline state.** A continuous, low-grade derealizing posture — the subject moves through environments at a slight perceptual remove, as if observing rather than inhabiting. He does not look directly at people for sustained periods; gaze averts to middle distance, to instruments, to hands. Photographic and depicted record consistently shows him with hands occupied (pen, slide rule, glasses, coffee cup, equipment) — manual fidgeting is a known dissociation-management tactic, a tether to the somatic present.

**Behavioral signature under stress.** The pre-switch sequence is observable across decades of canon and follows a stereotyped pattern: (1) micro-withdrawal of eye contact, (2) lowering of vocal register and slowing of speech, (3) a particular self-soothing gesture — pinching the bridge of the nose, removing and cleaning the spectacles, pressing the heel of the hand to the sternum (over the heart, where he monitors rate), (4) verbalized de-escalation phrases delivered to no one in particular ("you need to leave," "I can't — I can't —"), (5) backing away while maintaining a fixed point of visual focus on an inert object, (6) the breach. The pre-switch ritual is itself a defense — an attempt to deploy dissociation in slow motion, before the alter takes the field.

**Why it is primary.** A child cannot escape a violent father physically and cannot psychologically tolerate matricide while remaining intact; the only available option is to *not be there* while remaining there. Dissociation is the defense that makes the unbearable survivable, and in this subject's case it was rehearsed to such a degree of structural integration during the developmental window that it became the body's default response to overwhelming affect. The gamma exposure did not create this defense; it amplified its somatic expression.

### 2. Splitting

Operationally inseparable from dissociation but conceptually distinct: the inability to hold ambivalence within a single self-representation. The subject experiences himself as wholly good (gentle, scientific, pacifist, apologetic) and the alter as wholly bad (destructive, primitive, monstrous). There is no integrated self that contains both. This is the Kleinian paranoid-schizoid position never resolved into the depressive position — a developmental arrest precisely consistent with trauma onset before the integrative capacity consolidates.

**Behavioral signature.** Speaks of "the Hulk" in the third person with unwavering consistency across six decades of record. Refers to Hulk actions using grammatical constructions that exclude self-agency ("when *it* happens," "what *he* did"). Will not say "I broke that," "I killed that person," even when intellectually he knows there is one body and one continuous nervous system. The grammar is the defense.

**Interpersonal expression.** Cannot accept that loved ones might love the entire system — only the Banner-half. When Betty Ross or others express affection or acceptance toward the Hulk-half, the subject experiences acute distress and frequently destabilizes; the offered integration threatens the split that organizes his identity.

### 3. Projective Identification (onto the Alter System)

Closely allied to splitting but with an operational distinction: the subject does not merely disown his aggression and appetite — he projects them into a container (the alter) that then enacts them, and he experiences the consequences as if perpetrated by a non-self entity while nonetheless retaining the guilt. This is the perfect dissociative bind: the disowned material acts in the world, and the host experiences the moral cost without the experiential ownership.

**Behavioral signature.** The Grey Hulk / Mr. Fixit alter is the cleanest demonstration: gambling, drinking, sexual appetite, intimidation tactics — every appetitive and aggressive function the host has interdicted in himself is operating in a fully articulated form, in his body, at night, in Las Vegas, while the host has no access.
