The host does not say "I went to Vegas and gambled"; he says "I lost three weeks."

### 4. Somatization

Affect that cannot be felt is expressed in the body. The subject's life is a continuous somatic readout of unmetabolized states: gastric symptoms under stress (canonically depicted), tension headaches, the famous heart-rate elevation that is both trigger and tell, chronic muscular bracing in the jaw and shoulders, sleep disruption with parasomnias (he has been depicted thrashing, vocalizing, switching during sleep — the most dangerous and least controllable breach vector). The pulse-monitor habit — wearing a watch with heart-rate function, fingers to wrist or carotid — is the subject's chronic, ritualized externalization of interoceptive monitoring he cannot tolerate doing internally.

### 5. Acting Out (via the Alter)

Strictly speaking, the host does not act out — but the system does. Every catastrophic destructive episode in the record is an acting-out of affect the host could not contain. This is acting out at a structural rather than behavioral level: the impulse never reaches the host's awareness as impulse; it bypasses the host entirely and reaches the world as the alter's behavior. From a systems perspective the diagnosis is unambiguous; from the host's phenomenology, it is invisible.

### 6. Introjection (the Devil Hulk / Guilt Hulk)

The most clinically significant defense after dissociation itself, because it is the mechanism by which the abuser has been preserved inside the subject for the entirety of his adult life. The introjected paternal object — Brian Banner, alcoholic, paranoid, contemptuous, sadistic — speaks in the register of the original abuser and constitutes the subject's superego. Self-hatred in the subject is not generated freshly; it is *recited* from an internal voice that is recognizably someone else's.

**Behavioral signature.** Self-deprecating speech that uses formulations no spontaneous self-assessment would generate — "stupid Banner," "weak," "worthless," "puny" — language that maps too cleanly onto a specific imagined speaker. The subject's internal monologue (depicted in thought-balloons and recovered in therapy) routinely uses a second-person accusatory grammar: "you did this," "you should have known," "you'll never —" — the grammar of an internalized other, not of self-talk.

**Why this defense is so durable.** Introjecting the abuser is, paradoxically, a form of attachment preservation. The child cannot survive without the parent; if the parent is murderous, the child must internalize the parent's view of him in order to maintain even a malignant tie. The introject is the price of the bond.

---

## II. NEUROTIC-LEVEL DEFENSES

### 7. Isolation of Affect

The pre-incident baseline and the host's chronic mode: the subject knows what he is feeling propositionally — he can name it, describe it, analyze it — but cannot feel it as embodied experience. He discusses his own fear, grief, and rage as data. This is the dominant defense in clinical encounters: the subject is an articulate, insightful informant about himself, and this very articulateness is the defense in operation. He has converted affect into information so that information can be processed where affect cannot.

**Behavioral signature.** The unmistakable affective flatness when discussing his own history; the academic vocabulary deployed against personal material ("the incident," "the condition," "the entity"); the absence of tears in contexts where tears would be expected; the precise, almost forensic recounting of childhood events.

### 8. Intellectualization

The cognitive companion to isolation of affect. Physics is the subject's domain not by accident but by selection: it is the field in which the unbearable (energy, force, transformation, destruction at scale) can be rendered abstract, predictable, and subject to equation. The gamma device itself is, read psychodynamically, a sublimation-attempt at mastering paternal destructive power that has failed and rebounded — but the *recourse to physics* is the defense.

The subject's compulsive deployment of scientific apparatus around his own condition — biometric monitors, transformation logs, EEG records, attempts to derive gamma equations that predict his switches — is intellectualization weaponized against his own pathology. It does not work. The condition is not equation-tractable. But the defense persists because the alternative is feeling.

### 9. Reaction Formation

The subject's baseline persona — soft-spoken, deferential, apologetic, pacifist, conspicuously gentle — is in part reaction formation against the rage held in the alter. The pacifism is genuine; it is also a defense. The exaggerated mildness, the formal courtesy, the tendency to apologize for things he has not done, the physical posture of self-effacement (shoulders curved inward, hands clasped or pocketed, voice consistently below conversational volume) — these are the antithesis of the alter, and their rigidity betrays them as defenses rather than free expressions. A man with nothing to hide does not need to be this gentle.

### 10. Undoing

Pervasive in interpersonal repair behavior. The subject's life is a continuous attempt to undo damage — financial restitution sent anonymously to towns the Hulk has damaged, return visits to victims, charitable work, the entire instrumentalization arc in which he attempts to make the Hulk a net contributor as moral ledger-balancing. Undoing is also visible in the micro-behavior: he picks up dropped items, straightens disturbed objects, apologizes for trivial collisions — small somatic rituals of restoration.

### 11. Identification with the Aggressor

A complex variant of introjection: the subject has, in certain registers, identified with his father's view that he is contaminated and dangerous — and this identification has paradoxically organized his pro-social behavior. He withdraws *because* he believes himself dangerous, an assessment he learned from a man who was projecting his own dangerousness onto a child. The defense is doubly tragic: it borrows the abuser's distorted perception and uses it to power a life of moral self-restraint that is, while ethically admirable, etiologically pathological.

### 12. Displacement

Less central than in other trauma profiles because the alter system absorbs most of what would otherwise displace, but visible in minor registers: irritability with equipment, frustration directed at theoretical problems when the actual frustration is interpersonal, the redirection of helplessness with Betty into intensive lab work.

### 13. Repression (Distinct from Dissociation)

The subject's relationship to specific autobiographical material — most centrally the killing of Brian Banner in adulthood — involves classical repression as well as dissociation. The memory was not stored in an alter; it was forced from consciousness entirely and required therapeutic excavation to recover. Repression is a less efficient defense for this subject than dissociation (no alter to do the work), and its products tend to return as intrusive imagery, nightmares, and somatic symptoms rather than as enacted behavior.

---

## III. MATURE DEFENSES (Present, Intermittent, Non-Load-Bearing)

### 14. Sublimation

Genuine and substantial. The subject's scientific career, despite being recruited for intellectualization, has also produced authentic contributions to physics, biophysics, and medicine — work in which destructive energies are channeled into knowledge of real benefit. The recurring arc in which he uses gamma research to cure cancer, treat radiation victims, or otherwise convert his catastrophe into healing is sublimation in its textbook form. It is the most reliable mature defense in the file.

### 15. Altruism

Documented from the originating incident itself: he shielded Rick Jones at certain personal cost. Altruism recurs across decades — protection of strangers, defense of teammates at risk to himself, voluntary deployment of his condition in service of others. This is not reaction formation alone; some component is genuine. The subject is, by any honest reading, a morally serious person who has organized his life around minimizing harm.

### 16. Humor

Present, dry, self-deprecating, occasionally pointed. Most visible in calm interludes with intimates (Betty, Jennifer Walters, Rick Jones in adult years). Functions as it should — to make the unbearable momentarily bearable through perspective. Cannot be sustained under genuine threat; the first casualty of rising arousal is wit.

### 17. Suppression (Distinct from Repression)

The subject's capacity for *conscious* setting-aside of distressing material in order to function — the trained physicist's capacity to complete the experiment before grieving — is real and adaptive. It is also frequently exhausted; suppression requires resources, and the subject's resources are chronically depleted by the maintenance cost of dissociation.

### 18. Anticipation

The subject's continual forward-modeling of stressors, environments, and proximities — choosing routes, choosing accommodations, choosing relationships with an eye to threat-management — is anticipation in Vaillant's sense, and it is one of his more functional defenses. The lab-of-one's-own, the off-grid cabin, the carefully selected affiliations: all are anticipatory structures designed to manage breach-risk before it materializes.

---

## IV. COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS — POSITIVE

Distinct from defenses (which manage internal pressure) are compensations (which substitute or restore). The subject's positive compensations are notable and partly explain why a person with this defensive architecture has remained, on balance, a force for good rather than for harm.

- **Therapeutic alliance capacity.** The subject can form and use a treatment relationship (Samson, intermittently others). This is rare in DID with this severity and reflects unusually preserved reflective function.
- **Intellectual community.** Scientific peers and collaborators (Richards, Pym, McCoy, Stark in some periods) constitute a chosen family of minds in which the subject can be wholly himself in the cognitive register, even when the relational register is closed.
- **Animal-comfort tolerances.** Depicted across the record: the subject is consistently safer with animals, children, and the powerless than with peers, because these relationships do not raise the threat-of-intimacy that destabilizes him. He is gentle with the small.
- **Wilderness solitude.** Long stretches in remote environments — desert, mountain, isolated rural — function genuinely restoratively. The absence of human stressors permits the host to operate without the maintenance cost of social monitoring.
- **Meditation / somatic regulation practice.** Across multiple eras the subject has trained in breath-control, heart-rate biofeedback, and contemplative practice. These are the most genuinely curative behaviors in the file because they address the autonomic substrate directly rather than recruiting cognition against affect.
- **Capacity for love.** The Betty relationship, however interrupted, demonstrates that the subject is capable of sustained adult attachment when conditions permit. This is the single most prognostically important fact in the dossier.

---

## V. COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS — NEGATIVE

The maladaptive compensations are correspondingly numerous and often appear, superficially, as virtues.

- **Flight as a way of life.** The subject's defining adult behavior is leaving. Cities, countries, planets, relationships, identities, names. He has lived under dozens of aliases (David B., Bruce Jones, etc.), held dozens of cover jobs (mechanic, orderly, day-laborer, English tutor). Each flight is framed as protective — and is — and each flight reinforces the operational rule that proximity is unsafe.
- **Self-imposed celibacy / sexual avoidance.** Beyond the Betty relationship the subject is largely asexual in expression — a containment strategy, since arousal of any kind raises autonomic baseline. The Grey Hulk alter holds what the host has interdicted.
- **Teetotalism as rigidity.** The complete avoidance of alcohol is overdetermined: medically wise, paternally counter-identified, and rigidly maintained to the point that the subject cannot tolerate even social-ritual consumption. The rigidity itself is a defense; flexibility would mean trusting his own judgment about disinhibitors, which he does not.
- **Workaholism.** Sustained engagement with research and problem-solving as a substitute for unstructured time. Unstructured time admits affect; structured time does not.
- **Instrumentalization of the alter.** The recurrent attempt to "use" the Hulk — as Avenger, as weapon, as deployable asset — is a sophisticated negative compensation. It permits the host to feel he has mastered what he has not faced. It fails consistently because mastery cannot substitute for integration.
- **Self-isolation framed as care.** The most morally legible of the negative compensations: he leaves because he loves. This is true and it is also a defense; the loved one is also a stressor and the departure is also a self-protection. The two motives are inseparable, and the subject has never been able to disentangle them.
- **Refusal of help in extremis.** When most destabilized, the subject withdraws from precisely the people who could help. This is consistent with a child who learned that revealing distress brought escalation rather than relief.

---

## VI. THE INTEGRATION QUESTION

The defensive architecture is not static. The longitudinal record shows two genuine moments of structural improvement — the Samson fusion period and the late inter-alter cooperation arc — both of which involved the same therapeutic principle: cessation of suppression in favor of communication across the alter system. Both were partial, both were interrupted, and both demonstrated that the defenses described above are *not constitutional*. They are environmental adaptations to a developmental catastrophe, and they relax when the environment changes.

The clinically honest summary is this: the subject's defenses are exactly the defenses a person with this history would be expected to develop, deployed with exceptional skill by a mind of exceptional capacity. They have kept him alive. They have also kept him alone. The treatment indication is, and has always been, the same: a sustained, safe relational environment in which the primitive defenses can be permitted to soften because they are no longer required. He has rarely had one. The defenses, accordingly, remain in force.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE — SUBJECT: BANNER, R. B.

*A decade-by-decade reconstruction of the subject's affective, cognitive, and self-representational architecture as it has been observed, recorded, and revised across approximately sixty years of continuous file material. Frameworks employed: Vaillant's hierarchy of ego defenses; Main & Solomon on disorganized attachment; Putnam's discrete behavioral states model of dissociation; van der Kolk on traumatic re-enactment and somatic memory; Linehan on emotion regulation and the window of tolerance; Fonagy on mentalization; Schore on right-hemisphere affective regulation; Janet/van der Hart on structural dissociation of the personality (ANP/EP); Bowlby on protest-despair-detachment sequences; Kohut on selfobject deficit and grandiose-mirroring needs. Frameworks are applied to behavior, not the reverse.*

---

## I. PRE-INCIDENT BASELINE (childhood through ca. 1961)

Reconstructed retrospectively from the Mantlo disclosures (*Incident Hulk* #312, 1985) and the corroborating childhood material developed across the David, Pak, and Ewing tenures. No contemporaneous record exists; the picture is inferred from the somatic, defensive, and relational scaffolding the adult subject carried into the field.

**Affect regulation.** Catastrophically constricted from the earliest period for which evidence survives. The child grew up in an environment in which any expression of affect — fear, sadness, certainly anger, and conspicuously *joy*, which the father read as evidence of "contamination" — could precipitate violence. The adaptive solution available to a school-age child in such an environment is what Schore terms right-hemisphere down-regulation through dissociative disengagement: the child learns to attenuate physiological arousal preemptively, to read parental microexpression with hypervigilant accuracy, and to keep his own face and voice flat. The adult phenotype — flat affect, soft speech, apologetic register, the famous chronic stillness of his hands — is the residue of this childhood regimen.

**Cognitive style.** Precocious, abstract, retreatist. The Mantlo material and David's later elaboration depict a child who took refuge in physics and mathematics as the one domain in the house his father could not touch with violence (the father, also a physicist, could compete intellectually but could not weaponize the equations against the boy in the way he weaponized fists). Cognition was thereby established early as a defended sanctuary, and the lifelong pattern of intellectualization-as-defense (Vaillant, neurotic-tier) was laid down before the subject was ten. The boy used physics the way other abused children use dissociative absorption in fantasy.

**Self-concept.** Already negative, already organized around contamination and dangerousness. The father's paranoid conviction that his son was genetically tainted by his own work was a sustained projective identification: the child internalized the father's hatred of himself and experienced it as a true property of his own being. This is the foundation stone of the adult Devil Hulk introject — it was poured in childhood and merely re-named in adulthood.

**Attachment.** Disorganized in the classical Main & Solomon sense. The mother (Rebecca) was the source of warmth and protection; the father was the source of terror. Both, however, occupied the same household and frequently the same room, with the father episodically violent toward the mother in the child's sight. The child therefore could not develop a coherent strategy — neither secure approach (Ainsworth B), nor avoidant suppression (A), nor anxious amplification (C) — because his attachment figures collapsed into a single frightening-and-frightened configuration. The terminal disorganization arrived with the matricide: the protective figure was annihilated by the persecutory figure in his presence, and the child was then coerced into perjury at the inquest, sealing the trauma into a non-narratable somatic memory. Janet's structural dissociation begins here: an apparently normal part (ANP) was constructed to attend school, take exams, win scholarships, and present a coherent self to the aunt's household; emotional parts (EPs) were sequestered, holding the unspeakable.

---

## II. ADULT-PRE-INCIDENT / EARLIEST ON-RECORD PERIOD (ca. 1961–1962)

The earliest contemporaneous file material (Lee/Kirby, 1962) catches the subject in his late twenties as a working physicist on the Ross gamma project. The decade-defining observation is that *the dissociative architecture is already fully constructed and operating before the gamma incident*. The transformation did not produce the psychology; it gave the psychology a body.

**Affect regulation.** Operating entirely within a narrow band of attenuated affect. The window of tolerance (Siegel) is markedly contracted; the subject's modal response to provocation is verbal recession and somatic stillness, never escalation. With Betty Ross his warmth is observable but constrained — he expresses tenderness in indirect register (deferred glances, technical gifts, lab-coat formality) rather than in declarative speech. With General Ross he absorbs open contempt without counter-aggression; the affect this provocation generates is dissociated rather than metabolized.

**Cognitive style.** High fluid intelligence in tight harness to containment functions. The Lee/Kirby Banner is depicted at the chalkboard, in goggles, with calculations — cognition as labor, cognition as walls. He is not, in this period, a playful or expansive thinker; he is a *careful* one. The professional product is excellent; the lateral thinking and humor that occasionally surface in later eras are entirely suppressed.

**Self-concept.** Quietly worthless. The subject accepts Ross's contempt as accurate; accepts Betty's love as undeserved; treats the gamma-bomb project with the over-conscientiousness of someone trying to earn the right to occupy space. The Rick Jones rescue — running into the test field to pull a teenager from the blast zone — is a *characterologically consistent* act: a man who unconsciously regards his own life as forfeit-able will reflexively trade it for a child's, particularly an unprotected child.

---

## III. 1960s — INITIAL SOMATIC EXPRESSION

**Affect.** The gamma exposure provides the dissociated material with a somatic vehicle, and the first decade of recorded transformations exhibits a chaotic, under-organized switch pattern. Early transformations are nocturnal (circadian — consistent with the lowered cortical control of sleep onset permitting dissociative breach), then stress-triggered, then unpredictable. The host's affective baseline does not change; it *narrows further*, as the subject begins to grasp that any arousal may breach containment.

**Cognitive style.** The intellectualization defense intensifies. The subject begins what will become a lifelong project: the attempt to *think his way out* of the condition — a recursive trap, because cognition cannot reach the somatic register where the dissociation actually lives.

**Self-concept.** Now explicitly organized around monstrosity. The lay-readable formula — "don't make me angry" — is, properly heard, the self-report of a man who has located the unbearable in the second-person and the conditional, rather than owning it in the first-person indicative. He cannot say "I am angry." He can only say "you will not like what is not-me when not-me arrives."

**Attachment.** The Betty cycle establishes its lifelong rhythm: approach, intimacy, arousal, breach, flight, remorse, re-approach. Bowlby's protest-despair-detachment sequence runs in compressed loops, sometimes within a single issue.

---

## IV. 1970s — THE FUGITIVE PHASE

**Affect.** Chronic low-grade dysphoria; the subject is now itinerant, often hungry, often pursued, sleeping rough. The affective baseline shifts from constricted-but-stable (1960s lab life) to constricted-and-depleted. Anhedonia is constant. The window of tolerance contracts further under chronic stress, which paradoxically *increases* the frequency of dissociative breach — the system is being run closer to its threshold.

**Cognitive style.** Practical, survival-oriented intellect emerges alongside the theoretical. The subject begins to display the resourcefulness — improvised electronics, social camouflage, route planning — that will characterize him thereafter. Cognition has been drafted into fugitive logistics; the abstract-physics retreat is no longer available because there is no laboratory.

**Self-concept.** Hardens around the fugitive identity. The subject begins to articulate, with some regularity, the conviction that he is a *thing to be hunted*, and accepts this with a kind of moral submission. The Ross pursuit is experienced unconsciously as deserved — Ross is, after all, a paternal-coded persecutor, and the subject's organizing template is that paternal persecution is the correct response to his existence.

**Defensive structure.** Flight is now the dominant behavioral defense, organized at the level of life-pattern rather than episode. The subject becomes, structurally, a man who leaves — who cannot remain in any town, household, or relationship for longer than the time it takes for proximity to raise arousal.

---

## V. 1980s — RECOVERED MEMORY AND DIAGNOSIS

This is the diagnostic decade. The Mantlo retroactive disclosure (#312, 1985) makes the childhood etiology canon, and the early David tenure (beginning 1986) places the subject in sustained psychotherapy with Doc Samson.

**Affect.** Initial decompensation, then partial reorganization. The recovered memory of the matricide and the (suppressed) memory of the father's later death produce, predictably, a massive abreactive crisis — the dissociated material returns to consciousness faster than the system can metabolize it. Following the Samson work, the host's affective range *widens slightly for the first time on record*: the subject begins to display irritation, dry humor, sexual desire, and grief in the first person rather than entirely via the alter system.

**Cognitive style.** The intellectualization defense is, for the first time, partially turned on the subject himself — productively. The subject begins to mentalize (Fonagy): to hold his own internal states as objects of curious examination rather than as enemies to be suppressed. The capacity is fragile, but it is new, and it is the precondition for everything therapeutic that follows.

**Self-concept.** Begins to differentiate. The host can, in this period, articulate the distinction between "I am bad" (the introjected paternal verdict) and "something bad happened to me" (the trauma-informed reframe). The shift is incomplete and reversible under stress, but it is the first crack in the monolithic self-loathing.

**Alter system — formal mapping.** Savage, Grey/Fixit, and Professor states are now distinct and to varying degrees accessible to the host. The Grey state's emergence as a separate, *socialized* alter — the Vegas enforcer Mr. Fixit — is diagnostically critical: it demonstrates that dissociated material, when given narrative space, can develop its own ego functions, object relations, and even occupational identities. This is consistent with Putnam's discrete behavioral states model in its mature form.

**Integration attempt.** The Samson-engineered Professor Hulk fusion is the decade's clinical climax. It is, in trauma-therapy terms, a *premature integration* — the alters are fused without the traumatic material being adequately processed — and its eventual collapse is therefore predictable. But it establishes the possibility, which the subject will carry forward.

---

## VI. 1990s — POST-INTEGRATION COLLAPSE AND THE DEVIL HULK EMERGENCE

**Affect.** Volatile across the decade. The Professor fusion provides several years of relative affective stability, with the host accessing a previously unavailable range — irony, executive confidence, sexual presence with Betty. The collapse of the fusion (later David, then post-David writers) returns the system to its prior state with the additional injury of a remembered competence now lost: the subject knows what stability felt like and cannot regain it. Depressive features deepen.

**Cognitive style.** Re-narrows under the collapse. The mentalization gains of the Samson period are not fully lost, but the subject's first-line cognitive posture reverts to containment-and-prediction rather than reflection-and-understanding.

**Self-concept.** Re-darkens. The Devil Hulk / Guilt Hulk surfaces explicitly in this period and the early 2000s, and is correctly identified (with full canonicity later under Ewing) as the introjected father — a sadistic internal object speaking in Brian Banner's register, narrating the subject's worthlessness in terms drawn directly from the childhood abuse. The subject's superego, in Freudian terms, is occupied by the abuser; conscience and persecution are not distinguishable in his internal experience.

**Attachment.** The Betty marriage, achieved in this period, is the subject's high-water mark of sustained intimacy and the only stretch in the file in which the approach-withdrawal cycle runs at low amplitude. The conditions that permit it are precisely those a trauma-informed clinician would prescribe: a partner with prior knowledge of the subject's worst states, a stable physical environment, ongoing therapeutic contact. Its eventual disruption is environmental rather than dispositional.

---

## VII. 2000s — INSTRUMENTALIZED RAGE (Pak era)

**Affect.** Reorganized at a higher level of structure in the alter, *not* the host. The Planet Hulk / World War Hulk material depicts the Hulk-state acquiring narrative coherence, social bonds, language, leadership, and grief — the alter becomes a full person. The host, in parallel, recedes further; for stretches of this period the subject is barely present as an executive identity.

**Cognitive style.** This is the period in which the host's intellect and the alter's emotional life are at their *greatest functional separation*. The host is colder and more instrumental than ever; the alter is, paradoxically, the locus of love, loyalty, mourning, and moral clarity. From a structural-dissociation standpoint, this represents an unhealthy stabilization — the system is working, but at the cost of further sequestering the emotional material from the apparently-normal part.

**Self-concept.** The host's self-concept reaches a documented nadir: he describes himself as the disease and the Hulk as the patient. The moral reversal is total.

---

## VIII. EARLY 2010s — INSTRUMENTAL CONTAINMENT (Aaron era)

**Affect.** The subject attempts what is essentially a manic defense (Klein) dressed as a rational policy: he reframes the Hulk as a deployable asset and himself as the asset's operator. The host affect during this period is uncharacteristically expansive, even cheerful — and is read in the file as compensatory rather than integrative, because the underlying trauma material is precisely as untouched as ever.

**Cognitive style.** Productive, prolific, science-forward. The subject does meaningful work in this period — it is, after all, the recruitment of intellectualization to a socially valorized container. But the structural dissociation is unchanged.

**Self-concept.** Re-narrated as "useful," which is not the same as "lovable" or "safe," and therefore does not address the substrate. When the reframe collapses (as such reframes do), the underlying self-concept reasserts itself with the additional insult that the subject must now feel foolish for having believed the reframe.

---

## IX. LATE 2010s – EARLY 2020s — CLINICAL LITERACY (Ewing era)

The most diagnostically articulate period in the file, and the one in which the subject's own internal experience most closely matches the contemporary trauma-therapy literature.

**Affect.** Stratified across the alter system rather than concentrated in any single state. The Devil Hulk, properly named as the father-introject, ceases to function purely as a persecutor and begins, under sustained narrative pressure, to take on a paradoxical *protective* function — a transformation consistent with the contemporary IFS-informed approach to internal persecutors (a protector misrecognized as an attacker). Savage holds the child-grief. The host holds the adult shame. Inter-alter dialogue, rather than inter-alter combat, becomes possible for the first time on record.

**Cognitive style.** The mentalization gains of the Samson period return, deepened. The subject is able, in this period, to *name his own dissociative apparatus*, to distinguish between the alters' voices, and to participate in something approaching co-consciousness for sustained intervals. This is the clinical direction.

**Self-concept.** Still negative at baseline but newly *contestable*. The subject begins to articulate, intermittently, that the verdict of monstrosity is the father's verdict and not the truth — a separation he could not previously sustain.

**Attachment.** Remains the weakest axis. The Betty relationship undergoes further transformations in this period (including her own dissociative-somatic emergence), and the file's pattern of intimate proximity producing dissociative breach continues. The subject has not, across six decades, resolved the disorganized attachment substrate. Integration of the alter system is proceeding; integration of the relational template is not.

---

## X. CROSS-DECADE INVARIANTS

Notwithstanding the evolutionary arc above, certain features have been stable across the entire file and should be treated as constitutive rather than developmental:

1. **Heart-rate hypervigilance.** The subject monitors his own autonomic state continuously, across every era, every writer, every costume. This is a somatic-level adaptation laid down in childhood (reading the father's arousal to predict violence) and re-purposed to read his own.
2. **The apology reflex.** The subject's modal verbal output in interpersonal encounters begins with some form of apology, deflection, or self-minimization. This is invariant.
3. **The flight reflex.** Sustained presence in any location is the exception, not the rule. Even in the most stable arcs (Avengers tenure, Betty marriage) the subject is positioned at or near an exit.
4. **The third-person Hulk.** The host never quite says "when I am angry." It is always "the other guy," "him," "it." The grammatical refusal to own the affect is a six-decade invariant and is the single most diagnostically dense feature of the file.
5. **The paternal-authority submission.** Regardless of decade, regardless of his own accumulated power, the subject regresses in the presence of paternal-coded authority figures. The template laid in childhood has never been disconfirmed in a relationally corrective way.
6. **Teetotalism.** Unbroken. The subject's organization of his life around being-not-his-father has held across every era, and the appetitive functions remain sequestered in the Grey state rather than integrated.
7. **Reflexive child-protection.** The substrate-level identification with the unprotected child produces the fastest, most complete, and most morally coherent emergences of the alter system in the record. This is the one stimulus for which the entire system speaks with one voice.

---

## XI. SYNTHESIS

Read longitudinally, the subject's psychological trajectory is not a series of episodes but a single, slow, only intermittently assisted movement from total dissociative segregation toward partial inter-alter cooperation. The movement has been retrograde as often as progressive; it has been driven less by stable therapy than by the chance availability of relationally safe-enough others (Samson, Betty, occasionally Rick Jones). The system has demonstrated, in the Samson and Ewing periods, that integration is possible. It has demonstrated, in the intervening collapses, that integration is not sustainable in the absence of the environmental conditions trauma therapy requires.

The subject is, in the final analysis, a man who has been continuously studied for sixty years and continuously *treated* for perhaps eight of them. The clinical picture is consistent throughout: a developmental-trauma survivor with a fully constituted dissociative identity structure, an intact and exceptional cognitive apparatus, a negative but contestable self-concept, and a disorganized attachment substrate that has never been adequately addressed. He is, by every standard the literature recognizes, treatable. The file documents, primarily, his under-treatment.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — SUBJECT: BANNER, ROBERT BRUCE, PhD

*UATU File 7 / Section 4. Cross-reference: §1 (History), §3 (Psychological), §6 (Forensic). Clinical provenance: Sar V., "The many faces of dissociation," Clin Psychopharmacol Neurosci 12(3):171–179, 2014, PMID 25598819.*

---

## 4.0 Framing Note

The subject has been examined, formally or informally, by more clinicians than any comparable case in the meta-record: Leonard Samson (the principal of record, ~30 years of intermittent therapeutic contact), the late Reginald Fortean's contracted forensic staff, Charles Xavier (single telepathic survey, *Onslaught* preliminaries), Strange (esoteric assessments in multiple arcs), and a long list of S.H.I.E.L.D. / Hulkbuster Base / Gamma Base contract psychiatrists. The diagnostic record is therefore unusually deep, unusually contested, and — until the late 1980s — unusually wrong. The dominant misformulation across the first quarter-century of the file was variously "anger disorder," "radiation psychosis," "split personality of toxicological origin," and the lay-press shorthand "Jekyll-Hyde syndrome." Every one of these treats a precipitant or a surface feature as the disorder. The diagnostic correction beginning with Samson's structured work in the mid-1980s and culminating in the *Immortal* assessment period is, in effect, the slow movement of the file from a 1950s organic-psychiatry framing to a contemporary trauma-and-dissociation framing. This section presents the case as it would be formulated today.

---

## 4.1 Primary Diagnosis

### Dissociative Identity Disorder
**DSM-5-TR 300.14 / ICD-11 6B64**

The primary diagnosis is **Dissociative Identity Disorder with somatoform features of an extraordinary severity**. Every Criterion A through E condition is met explicitly and redundantly in the longitudinal record; the somatic transformation is best understood as the literalization of an inter-alter switch, not as a separate or competing condition.

**Criterion A — Two or more distinct personality states with marked discontinuity in sense of self and sense of agency, accompanied by alterations in affect, behavior, consciousness, memory, perception, cognition, and/or sensory-motor functioning.**

The catalog of documented alters, in approximate order of their emergence into the clinical record:

- **The Host (Robert Bruce Banner, PhD).** Intellectualizing, soft-spoken, somatically slight, apologetic, conflict-avoidant, with a narrow affective bandwidth centered around quiet melancholy and intellectual absorption. Speaks in measured, qualified sentences; rarely uses the first-person singular emphatically; chronic self-monitoring. Heart rate at baseline is, by his own continuous report, deliberately suppressed via diaphragmatic breathing and yogic regimens learned during his Calcutta period.

- **Savage Hulk.** Emotional age fixed at approximately 7 — the age of matricide. Speaks in third person ("Hulk smash"), reduced expressive vocabulary, simple syntax, child-state idiom, the affective texture of a frightened and enraged child who has been cornered. Defensive aggression, not predatory. Wants to be left alone ("Hulk just want to be left alone") — the precise utterance of a child who has learned that adult attention is dangerous.

- **Grey Hulk / Mr. Fixit.** Nocturnal, urban, gambler, brawler, womanizer, manipulator, speaks in the cadence of a 1940s noir tough — the cadence of a child's imagined adult masculinity, which is itself a tell. Holds the appetitive and aggressive drives the host has interdicted. Drinks. Smokes occasionally. Wears tailored suits. Operates in Las Vegas under assumed names.

- **Professor Hulk / Merged Hulk.** A negotiated fusion state achieved under Samson's guidance, retaining the host's cortical functioning in the Hulk somatotype. The most prosocial of the alters. Unstable as a long-term configuration because it does not resolve the underlying split — it pastes the host's voice onto a body that the other alters also claim.

- **The Devil Hulk / Guilt Hulk.** The most diagnostically important alter. Internal persecutor, paternal-voiced, sadistic, articulate, hates the host, expresses overt wish for the host's destruction, and is — by the *Immortal* period's explicit textual confirmation — the introjection of Brian Banner. Appears across decades in dream sequences, fugue intervals, and breakdown states. In structural-dissociation terms this is a hostile-introject EP (emotional part) modeled on the abuser; in object-relational terms it is the maximally malignant superego formation possible in a developmental-trauma case.

- **The Maestro.** A futural / prospective alter, expressed in projected timelines and one inarguable in-universe instantiation: the host as he would be if intellect and rage cohabited without conscience. Diagnostically: a glimpse of what failed integration looks like when the introjected abuser wins.

- **Joe Fixit Redux, Green Scar, Doc Green, Kluh, Breaker-Apart, and a long tail of fragmentary states.** The literature on DID describes "fragments" as alters with narrow function and limited autobiographical continuity; the subject's system contains many. The above are the principal ones with sustained executive history.

Switches are marked by characteristic prodromal signs documented across the file: pupil dilation, a brief stillness, the host audibly counting under his breath ("…seven, eight…"), removal of glasses, a single inhalation through the nose, hands going to the temples, and — the late-period tell — a quiet "I'm sorry" addressed to whoever is nearest before executive function transfers.

**Criterion B — Recurrent gaps in the recall of everyday events, important personal information, and/or traumatic events that are inconsistent with ordinary forgetting.**

The Banner-to-Hulk amnestic barrier is the defining symptom of the case across all six decades of record. The host wakes in unfamiliar locations, often nude, often miles or continents from his last memory, with no autobiographical access to Hulk episodes except via secondhand report or, occasionally, dream-fragments. The reverse barrier is partial and asymmetric — Savage Hulk has limited access to the host's identity; Grey Hulk has more; Professor most; Devil Hulk has total access and uses it weaponized. This asymmetric amnesia is itself textbook DID: hostile/persecutory alters typically have greater access to host memory than child or affect-bearing alters.

The amnesia extends to pre-incident trauma as well. The matricide and the killing of Brian Banner in adulthood were both dissociated and were recovered only under sustained therapeutic pressure — first with Samson, later under the *Immortal* recapitulations. Recovered-memory phenomena in this case are not iatrogenic: the corroborating evidence (Brian Banner's hospital records, the inquest transcripts, the aunt's testimony) is in the file.

**Criterion C — Clinically significant distress or impairment in social, occupational, or other important areas of functioning.**

Distress is pervasive and continuous. Occupational impairment is total in the conventional sense (the subject cannot hold civilian employment, cannot reside in fixed habitation, cannot maintain professional credentialing without elaborate concealments). Relational impairment is global. Distress at the host level is expressed in a continuous low-grade dysphoria punctuated by acute shame storms post-episode.

**Criterion D — Not a normal part of broadly accepted cultural or religious practice.**

Not applicable — no cultural or religious framing has ever been offered, by the subject or by clinicians, to normalize the presentation.

**Criterion E — Not attributable to the physiological effects of a substance or another medical condition.**

The gamma exposure is the obvious challenger here, and the differential is treated at length in §4.5 below. Briefly: the gamma incident is the precipitant of the somatic expression of the dissociative apparatus, not the etiological agent of the dissociative apparatus itself. The pre-incident clinical picture (per §1) already exhibits the full affective and defensive architecture of a severely dissociated trauma survivor.

### Somatoform specifier
The subject's case requires a specifier the diagnostic manuals do not formally provide: the inter-alter switch is somatically expressed at the level of gross morphology, mass, endocrine state, and tissue composition. The closest formal analog is the *somatoform dissociation* construct in the European dissociation literature (Nijenhuis et al.), and the case is best described as DID with maximal somatoform expression. Heart rate is the documented switch-marker; the autonomic threshold for switch initiation has been measured (by Samson, by Banner himself, by S.H.I.E.L.D. medical) at variable points but consistently centers on a sympathetic-activation cascade triggered by interoceptive registration of anger.

---

## 4.2 Comorbid Diagnoses

### Complex Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder
**ICD-11 6B41**

CPTSD is the comorbidity of greatest explanatory power and all three "disturbances in self-organization" criteria beyond ordinary PTSD are met:

- **Affective dysregulation.** The somatic-psychic centerpiece of the case. The host has no functional graduated relationship to anger; affect cannot be metabolized at the host level at all and is instead dissociatively expelled into the alter system. The famous and clinically perfect self-report — "you wouldn't like me when I'm angry" — is the description of a person whose affective apparatus has never developed because expression of affect in childhood meant lethal danger.

- **Negative self-concept.** Pervasive, organizing, and structurally encoded as the Devil Hulk introject. The subject describes himself, in spontaneous speech across decades, as a monster, a danger, a contaminant, a thing that should not exist. This is not depressive cognition (though depression is also present); it is a stable, identity-level self-construct.

- **Disturbances in relationships.** Lifelong, documented across every sustained attachment in the file. The pattern is detailed in §3 and §5: pursuit, intimacy, autonomic escalation, dissociative breach, flight, shame, re-pursuit. The subject has never successfully sustained an intimate adult relationship at the host level for longer than approximately fourteen months without rupture.

The standard PTSD criteria are also met: intrusive recollections (dream-state intrusions of the matricide; flash-memories of paternal violence under stress); avoidance (geographic, relational, occupational); hyperarousal (the autonomic baseline is elevated despite compensatory practices); negative cognition and mood.

### Major Depressive Disorder, Recurrent, Severe
**DSM-5-TR 296.33 / ICD-11 6A71**

Documented across multiple arcs. Anhedonia, low affective baseline, hopelessness, suicidal ideation, and documented suicide attempt (the "Hulk-proof bullet" attempt). Episodes are typically post-decompensation and shame-driven. The host's body's refusal to permit suicidal completion constitutes a recurrent iatrogenic re-traumatization in its own right and feeds the depressive loop.

### Persistent Depressive Disorder
**DSM-5-TR 300.4**

The baseline affective state between MDD episodes meets dysthymia criteria: chronic low mood, low energy, poor self-regard, reduced capacity for pleasure, present for greater than two years and indeed for the majority of the adult life. The host's characteristic baseline is melancholic.

### Social Anxiety Disorder (provisional)
**DSM-5-TR 300.23**

Strongly suggested by the host's behavioral phenotype: avoidance of social attention, somatic markers of social-evaluative anxiety, preference for solitary or one-to-one configurations, marked discomfort in groups, professional reluctance to lecture or publish under his own name post-incident. Distinguishing this from CPTSD-related avoidance is largely academic; the phenomenology overlaps almost completely.

### Sleep-Wake Disorder, Nightmare Disorder
**DSM-5-TR 327.42**

Documented in multiple arcs. Recurrent paternal-themed nightmares, recurrent matricide-themed nightmares, the Devil Hulk speaking in dream-state. Sleep is itself a trigger (low cortical vigilance can permit switching), which produces a secondary insomnia that is partly volitional.

### NOT diagnosed but worth surveillance
- **Borderline Personality Disorder.** Some features (unstable self-image, intense and unstable relationships, chronic emptiness) are present, but the affective lability is dissociatively partitioned rather than rapidly cycling at the host level, and the abandonment-fear and impulsivity profiles do not match. The shared features are better attributed to the CPTSD substrate.

---

## 4.3 Symptom Presentation in Observable Behavior

A psychiatric diagnosis must rest on more than category-matching; the observable behavioral signature of this case includes:

- **Pre-switch prodromal sequence**, in approximate order: (i) elevation of voice pitch by a perceptible margin in the host; (ii) increased rate of self-deprecating qualifiers in speech ("I'm sorry, I'm just — I'm not — let me try again"); (iii) cessation of fidgeting, an unusual stillness; (iv) audible inhalation through the nose; (v) closure of the eyes; (vi) the under-breath count; (vii) hand to the bridge of the nose, removal of glasses if worn; (viii) the apology to bystanders; (ix) switch.

- **Post-switch host phenomena**: disorientation lasting 4–40 minutes depending on episode severity; somatic confusion (the host's proprioceptive map does not match the body he wakes in, even though the body has returned to host morphology); shame-affect onset within minutes of cognitive re-coherence; immediate behavioral flight from the location of the episode.

- **Inter-episode containment behaviors**: continuous interoceptive monitoring; heart-rate biofeedback (formal in some periods, informal in all); meditation practice (vipassana and pranayama, learned during the Calcutta period and maintained variably thereafter); dietary austerity (vegetarianism in long stretches, partly ethical, partly anxiolytic); sleep hygiene rituals; avoidance of caffeine, alcohol, and stimulants of any kind; avoidance of crowds, of confined spaces, of physical contact; the carrying of expandable clothing.

- **Speech markers of dissociative structure**: the host occasionally refers to the Hulk in the third person ("he did that, I didn't"); under stress the host sometimes refers to himself in the third person ("Banner needs to think about this"), which is a more subtle and more diagnostic marker, indicating the host himself is being held as a partial-object by a higher-order observing alter; the Devil Hulk's "voice" is reported as an intrusive thought stream in second person ("you knew what you were, you always knew") — second-person intrusive thought is a high-specificity marker for hostile-introject alter activity.

- **The flight phenomenon**. The subject's defining adult behavioral signature is *leaving*. Leaving cities within hours of arrival when stress climbs; leaving relationships at the moment of greatest intimacy; leaving the planet (literally, in two documented arcs). Geographic flight is the host's only available regulation strategy and is enacted with the practiced efficiency of someone who has rehearsed it thousands of times.

---

## 4.4 Course Over Time

The course conforms to the documented natural history of untreated to partially-treated DID in chronic-developmental-trauma cases:

- **Childhood (pre-7).** Sub-clinical formation of the dissociative defense. Likely development of a "child within" alter as containment for the unbearable affect generated by paternal abuse.

- **Age 7 (matricide).** Catastrophic exacerbation. The Savage Hulk alter likely consolidates here. The coerced perjury at the inquest functions as the developmental cement of the dissociative structure — the subject is explicitly required, by external authority, to dissociate the truth.

- **Latency through adolescence.** Compensated dissociation; intellectual hypertrophy as a defense; functional academic performance masking the underlying structure; the aunt's home is non-abusive but also non-reparative — the trauma is not processed because it is not named.

- **Young adulthood (graduate training, military contracting).** The host phenotype consolidates: the soft, controlled, intellectualizing physicist. The dissociative apparatus is fully formed but quiescent — the subject's life is organized to prevent its activation. The Brian Banner reappearance and the second killing produce a major dissociative episode that is fully amnestic.

- **The incident and the next decade (1962 onward).** Somatic expression of the dissociative apparatus begins. The host is now unable to use his pre-existing containment strategies because the dissociative breaches are externally catastrophic. The system seeks equilibrium and fails to find it.

- **Samson era (mid-1980s onward).** First sustained, competent psychotherapeutic engagement. Partial integration achieved (Professor Hulk). The integration fails repeatedly under stress but the achievement is real: it demonstrates that the system *can* integrate.

- **Worldbreaker and political-narrative period.** A demonstration of what the dissociated rage-state does when given a coherent ideological structure. Clinically: the alter recruits the host's intellect for its own purposes.

- **Instrumentalization period.** An attempted reframe — the host attempts to use the alter as a deployed asset, bypassing integration in favor of utility. Fails predictably; you cannot weaponize what you have not metabolized.

- **Recent period (*Immortal* arc and beyond).** The most clinically literate phase. Recovered-memory work is sustained; the Devil Hulk is named, addressed, and partially negotiated with; inter-alter cooperation becomes the working model. This is the contemporary standard of trauma care (e.g., the ISSTD treatment guidelines for DID): not suppression of alters, not forced integration, but cooperative function pending eventual fusion. Progress is real and fragile.

---

## 4.5 Rigorous Differential — What This Case Is Not

The diagnostic correction in this case has been slow because the surface features mimic several other conditions and because the somatic expression is so dramatic that it pulls clinical attention away from the underlying structure. Each plausible alternative must be examined and ruled out.

### Intermittent Explosive Disorder (DSM-5-TR 312.34)
**Rejected.** IED requires recurrent behavioral outbursts of aggression disproportionate to provocation, but with intact memory, intact identity, no third-person self-reference, no autobiographical amnesia, and no distinct phenomenological "other" experiencing the outburst. The Banner case fails IED on every distinguishing criterion: he has profound amnesia for episodes, his alters are identity-discontinuous, and the aggression is not the disorder — the dissociation is. IED was the dominant misformulation in early military-psychiatry workups of the file and remains the dominant lay misformulation. It is incorrect.

### Bipolar I Disorder with manic aggression (DSM-5-TR 296.4x)
**Rejected.** No periodicity in the inter-episode interval; no euthymic or elevated mood states between episodes (baseline is dysphoric, not euthymic); no pressured speech, decreased need for sleep, flight of ideas, or grandiosity in the host; the aggression is not mood-congruent because the host has no concurrent elevated mood. The alter switches are not mood episodes; they are identity switches with mood as one of many altered parameters.

### Substance-Induced Disorder (DSM-5-TR various)
**Rejected.** The subject is teetotal across virtually the entire canon — diagnostically significant in itself, as it represents a counter-identification with the father. No documented substance use precedes switches. Trigger is interoceptive (autonomic arousal), not pharmacological.

### Antisocial Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.7)
**Rejected.** The Hulk's destruction is reactive, defensive, and largely directed at threats or at property; it is not predatory, instrumental, or premeditated (except in the Maestro projection, which is precisely the warning case). The host displays profound guilt, conscience, capacity for empathy, sustained altruism, and ethical reasoning at an unusually high level. ASPD requires the inverse on every dimension. The Devil Hulk has features superficially resembling psychopathy (callousness, cruelty, manipulativeness), but is an alter, not the host, and is best understood as a hostile-introject rather than a personality disorder.

### Schizophrenia and other Primary Psychotic Disorders (DSM-5-TR 295.x)
**Rejected.** The subject's alters are not auditory hallucinations of external origin; they are dissociated identity states with executive history. No formal thought disorder is present in the host (his cognition is in fact extraordinarily organized). Negative symptoms in the schizophrenic sense (avolition, alogia, anhedonia of the primary type) are absent — what looks superficially like avolition is actually the highly motivated regulation behavior of a CPTSD case. No delusions outside the dissociative frame. The Devil Hulk's voice is phenomenologically distinct from a schizophrenic auditory hallucination: it is second-person, intrusive-thought form, autobiographically continuous with childhood, and tied to a coherent identity rather than fragmentary. This is the textbook distinction the Sar (2014) review draws between dissociative voice phenomena and psychotic voice phenomena.

### Schizoaffective Disorder
**Rejected** on the same grounds as schizophrenia plus the absence of mood-episode criteria as in bipolar I.

### Other Specified Dissociative Disorder (DSM-5-TR 300.15) / DDNOS
**Rejected as primary in favor of full DID.** Full Criterion A is met (distinct identity states with executive switching, not merely dissociative experiences), so the case clears the threshold for full DID.

### Depersonalization/Derealization Disorder (DSM-5-TR 300.6)
**Present as a feature, rejected as the primary.** The subject does experience depersonalization episodes (particularly during pre-switch prodrome and post-switch re-entry), but these are features of the DID, not a separate condition.

### Conversion Disorder / Functional Neurological Symptom Disorder
**Conceptually relevant; rejected as the primary.** The somatic transformation could be philosophically framed as the largest conversion presentation in the record, but the somatic events are objectively measurable (mass change, tissue change, energy emission) and persist outside the subject's psychological control, so the framework misfits. The somatoform-dissociation construct fits better.

### Organic / Radiation-Induced Neuropsychiatric Disorder
**Rejected as etiological, accepted as somatic-precipitant.** Acute high-dose gamma exposure produces neurological and psychiatric sequelae


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT: BANNER, ROBERT BRUCE, PhD

A surveillance-grade catalog of observable behavior, organized by condition. Every entry has been observed repeatedly across the canonical record; the patterns are stable across writers, decades, and continuities, which is itself a diagnostic finding (the behaviors are not stylistic — they are structural). Read as field-operator notes: what to expect, what to watch for, what predicts the next state.

---

## 1. BASELINE / CALM

The subject's calm is not calm. It is a continuously maintained suppression regime, and the tells are the tells of the regime, not of a relaxed organism.

**Posture and carriage.** Stands with shoulders pulled marginally forward, sternum slightly collapsed — a habitual occupation of less space than his frame would allow. Walks with a short, even stride, weight forward on the balls of the feet (a flight-ready gait, not a confrontational one). Sits at the front edge of chairs; rarely uses chair backs; almost never crosses legs in male company. When standing in conversation he positions himself at roughly 30° off-axis from the interlocutor rather than squared up — a de-escalation stance.

**Hands.** The most informative single channel. At rest the hands seek occupation: a pen rolled between fingers, the temple of his glasses, the cuff of a shirt, the rim of a coffee cup. When no object is available the right hand finds the inside of the left wrist — thumb to the radial pulse — and stays there. This is **continuous covert heart-rate monitoring**, performed so habitually that the subject is generally unaware of it. Any observer wishing to know the subject's internal state should watch the right thumb on the left wrist before watching the face.

**Eyes.** Soft, downcast more often than not. Makes brief eye contact, then glances away and returns — the modulated gaze of someone who has trained himself out of staring. Blink rate elevated above population norm at baseline. Will not hold direct gaze with paternal-coded males for more than approximately two seconds.

**Voice.** Quiet, slightly under-projected, requiring the listener to lean in. Speech is precise, syntactically complete, prone to subordinate clauses and self-correction mid-sentence ("the — actually, more accurately, the —"). Almost never raises volume. Laugh is brief, breath-only, immediately suppressed. Apologizes verbally at a rate well above any operational necessity — "sorry" used as conversational punctuation, frequently for things he did not cause.

**Dress.** Habituated to muted palette: greys, browns, slate, the famous purple only in transformed state and not by choice. Trousers worn loose (anticipates the destruction of close-fitting clothes). Shirts are generally button-down and untucked or half-tucked, sleeves rolled to the forearm — a working scientist's habit but also a garment-loss-mitigation strategy. Wears the cheapest reasonable footwear available; will replace shoes with disposable canvas when in a region where transformation is probable. No wristwatch on the left wrist (interferes with pulse-monitoring); when worn, it is on the right.

**Eating.** Eats lightly, quickly, and alone by preference. Tends toward simple, reproducible meals — rice, eggs, fruit, instant coffee. Avoids restaurants when possible; when unavoidable, chooses booths against walls with line-of-sight to exits. No alcohol, ever — refuses with a small smile and no explanation. Caffeine intake is moderated and monitored (raises heart rate); will switch to decaffeinated after midafternoon.

**Sleep.** Poor and self-managed. Sleeps four to six hours by preference, rarely more. Reads or works until physical exhaustion rather than attempting to compose himself toward sleep. Wakes early, often before dawn. Avoids alarms (startle). Sleeps light, in t-shirt and loose trousers — never nude (would compound humiliation of nocturnal transformation).

**Spatial habits.** Enters rooms and immediately maps exits. Will not sit with his back to a door. Prefers ground-floor accommodation (jump-survivable, escape-viable). Walks the perimeter of any new space within the first hour of occupancy. Carries minimal possessions; everything he owns fits in a single duffle within ninety seconds of decision to depart.

**Decision habits at baseline.** Defers small decisions to others ("whatever you want is fine"); commands large decisions absolutely when scientific judgment is required. The asymmetry is diagnostic — the host has surrendered preference in domains where preference would imply self, and reserves authority only for domains where competence is impersonal.

---

## 2. MILD STRESS / FRUSTRATION

The first level of arousal above baseline is also the most operationally important, because this is where intervention is still possible.

**Somatic tells, in order of appearance.** (1) The thumb-to-wrist contact, normally intermittent, becomes sustained. (2) A slow exhalation through pursed lips, often disguised as a sigh of consideration. (3) Loosening of the collar or removal of glasses to pinch the bridge of the nose. (4) The hand passes through the hair, front to crown — a self-soothing gesture inherited from childhood and observable in photographs from his graduate years. (5) Jaw clenches; a small muscle bunches at the angle of the mandible. (6) The subject takes a step backward, almost imperceptibly, increasing distance from the stressor.

**Verbal tells.** Speech slows and becomes more precise, not less. Apologies increase in density. The subject begins to use the third person about himself in a hedged way ("a person in my situation would — *I* would —"). Uses self-deprecating humor as a pressure valve: small, dry, often unfunny jokes about his own danger. If the humor lands, arousal drops marginally; if it does not, arousal climbs.

**Behavioral tells.** Begins to look for an exit. Will excuse himself to "get some air," to "check on something," to use a bathroom — these are *all* the same behavior and should be read identically: he is removing himself to perform autonomic regulation in private. Once removed, he will splash cold water on his face and the back of his neck (vagal maneuver), perform paced breathing (four-in, six-out, observed consistently), and re-check pulse.

**Decision habit under mild stress.** Withdraws from social decisions entirely; over-engages technical ones (compensatory mastery). Will begin a small repetitive task — sorting papers, cleaning a workstation, rewriting an equation already on the board — that has no operational necessity but discharges arousal motorically.

---

## 3. ACUTE STRESS / PRE-BREACH

The threshold zone. Tells become unmistakable to a trained observer; the subject's own awareness of them is sharp but his control over them is degrading.

**Somatic.** Sweating begins at the temples and the upper lip. Skin pallor with a green undertone at the throat and the inner wrists — the gamma signature beginning to surface in the capillary bed. Eyes widen and the pupil reaction becomes sluggish; sclera show above the iris. Tendons stand out on the forearms; the dorsal hand veins distend visibly. Breathing shifts from diaphragmatic to thoracic — visible shoulder rise. A fine tremor in the hands, suppressed by gripping (the edge of a table, the back of a chair, his own forearms in a self-hug posture).

**Verbal.** Speech becomes terse, clipped, monosyllabic where possible. The polite hedges drop. The voice acquires a strained, slightly higher register. The characteristic warning phrases emerge — variants of "you need to leave," "get back," "I can't — " trailing into incomplete sentences. He will name his own condition aloud as a control maneuver ("I'm — I'm losing it, I'm losing it"), which is half warning to others and half attempt at metacognitive grounding.

**Postural.** Drops to one knee, or doubles over with hands on thighs, or braces against a wall — all assume a low, stable stance that minimizes the fall distance when consciousness narrows. Removes glasses (preserves them — a small act of forward-planning persistent into the breach moment, indicative of how rehearsed the cycle is). May begin unbuttoning or removing the outer shirt deliberately, a habituated garment-management protocol.

**Behavioral.** Will push others physically away if they approach — a hard, two-handed shove to the chest, often the only overtly aggressive act the host commits. This is **protective**, not offensive: he is clearing the blast radius. Will move toward open ground, away from civilians, toward terrain features that can absorb impact (open water, rock formations, structural reinforcement).

**Decision collapse.** Cognition narrows to a single axis: distance. All other considerations — mission, relationships, possessions, identity — are jettisoned in service of moving people away from him. This is the deepest operational instinct in the file and overrides every other directive he has ever been given.

---

## 4. BREACH / TRANSFORMATION

**Pre-transformation tell, last ten seconds.** Eyes go fully green, sclera included. Voice drops an octave mid-syllable. The skin pigmentation change propagates from extremities centripetally. Musculature begins to swell visibly. The host's last verbal output is almost always either an apology, a warning, or the name "Betty."

**Loss of host executive control.** Total. The host does not "ride along"; he is gone, in the dissociative sense. He does not see, hear, or remember what follows. Witnesses report that the eyes during transformation briefly show terror, then nothing recognizable.

**Post-breach somatic signature.** When the alter retires and the host returns: nude or near-nude, frequently bleeding from minor lacerations, occasionally with foreign material embedded (concrete dust, vegetation, blood not his own). Cold. Disoriented. Curls into a fetal posture spontaneously while consciousness returns. First sensory channel back online is hearing; first motor act is to touch his own face, confirming identity. First spoken word, when it comes, is almost invariably an interrogative — "where" or "how long" — never "what happened," because he already knows what happened.

---

## 5. THREAT (to self)

Counterintuitive: direct threat to the subject's own person is **less** likely to trigger breach than threat to another. The subject has so thoroughly internalized his own disposability that personal threat registers as familiar and almost calming.

**Tells under personal threat.** Goes still. Hands open at his sides, palms forward — non-threatening, also ready. Voice softens further; he negotiates. Will offer himself in trade for others as a first move, not a last one. Makes eye contact more readily than at baseline (the threatening party has clarified the relational frame; ambiguity is gone). Will accept physical mistreatment — slaps, blows, restraints — with a remarkable absence of reactive arousal, because absorbing mistreatment is his oldest competence.

**The inversion point.** If the threatening party shifts targets to someone he cares about, or to a child, or to a civilian, the arousal curve goes vertical without warning. The host's negotiation posture does not visibly change in the first second; in the second second he is mid-breach. This is the single most dangerous misread an adversary can make: mistaking his compliance as a stable state.

---

## 6. THREAT (to others / protective rage)

**Triggering classes.** (a) Betty, ordered roughly: Betty in distress, Betty threatened, Betty injured. (b) Children. (c) Civilians categorized as innocent and helpless. (d) Rick Jones, specifically (the founding rescue debt is permanent). (e) A small set of others — Samson, Jennifer Walters, and a handful of teammates depending on era.

**Pre-breach behavior under protective trigger.** Compressed. The mild-stress and acute-stress tells telescope into a few seconds. He may not get the warning out. He may not have time to move people back. The host quality of the breach is consequently more violent and less controlled than stress-driven breaches; the alter that emerges under protective trigger tends to be the Savage state, not the Grey or the Professor.

---

## 7. INTIMACY

The condition under which the subject is most behaviorally aberrant relative to baseline, because intimacy raises arousal through a channel for which he has no defense.

**Approach behaviors.** Initiates contact tentatively — a hand on a shoulder rather than a torso, fingertips first rather than palm. Stands slightly too far away in private conversation, as if maintaining a public-conversation distance with intimates. Eye contact during intimacy is more sustained than at baseline but is broken at moments of emotional intensification — looks at the partner's mouth or hairline rather than the eyes when feeling is high.

**Verbal.** Becomes more articulate, not less, during emotional exchanges — intellectualization recruited as bridge. Will name his feelings in clinical or distanced language ("I find myself, when I — " rather than "I feel"). Apologizes more, not less, in intimacy. Tells the partner repeatedly that they should leave him, often phrased as their own protection ("you deserve better than this, you really do") — this is both true self-assessment and a pre-emptive rejection that defends against the rejection he expects.

**Sexual behavior.** Cautious to the point of inhibition. Heart-rate awareness during intimacy is acute; partners across the canon have noted that he monitors himself throughout. Will withdraw at the threshold of arousal he judges unsafe. The host's sexuality is largely contained in this way; the Grey Hulk alter is where the appetitive function lives and operates with a wholly different ethic.

**Post-intimacy.** High risk of flight. The subject is most likely to leave a relationship within 48 hours of its deepest moment of connection. The pattern is consistent enough across decades that it should be treated as a near-certainty: connection produces flight on a brief delay.

---

## 8. GRIEF

**Initial response.** Stillness. Goes quiet for an unusually long interval. Does not weep visibly in the first minutes. Will perform some small task — closing a door, picking up an object — in slow motion. The face is composed but the right thumb is on the left wrist and stays there.

**Hours to days.** Withdraws to a workspace and works. The work is often unrelated to anything productive — equations on paper for their own sake, instrument calibration, rote calculation. This is **affective discharge through cognition**, the most reliable defense in his arsenal. Will not eat or sleep on schedule. Will refuse company politely and persistently.

**Weeks.** Risk window for both transformation and suicidality. The Devil Hulk introject is loudest in grief; the persecutory voice tells the subject that the loss is his fault, that he is the contagion, that the loved one died because of him. This is true of every loss in the record regardless of actual causation. Decompensation in this window is high.

**Recovery signature.** Returns to function via a project — typically one framed as service to others. The grief is not resolved; it is sublimated into a new containment regime, slightly more rigid than the prior one.

---

## 9. VICTORY

The subject has no functional repertoire for victory. He has not been trained, by life, to receive it.

**Tells.** Visible discomfort. Looks away from praise. Deflects credit reflexively ("it was the team — it was really Tony's design — Rick did the hard part"). Will physically leave a room in which he is being celebrated, often before the celebration has properly begun. Cannot accept a toast (no drink); accepts handshakes but not embraces in public contexts.

**Internal weather.** Victory raises arousal — positive arousal is still arousal, and the autonomic system does not distinguish. Heart rate climbs in celebration as in threat. Consequently the subject's transformations have, on rare occasions, been triggered by **good** news. He has learned to flatten his response to victory accordingly.

**Decision habit post-victory.** Resists rest. Immediately raises the next problem. Treats success as a precondition for the next obligation rather than a terminus.

---

## 10. DEFEAT

Curiously, the subject is **more stable** in defeat than in victory. Defeat confirms his worldview; victory disturbs it.

**Tells.** Quiet. A long exhalation. A small nod, often to himself. Does not externalize blame — accepts it, often beyond his share. Will say "I should have — " and offer a specific technical revision (recruits intellect to digest the failure rather than feel it).

**Behavioral.** Cleans up. Carries the wounded. Stays at the site after others have left. Writes the after-action report. Defeat activates the caretaker function, which is among his most reliable functional states.

**Risk window.** Lower than after victory in the short term, higher in the long term. Defeat accumulates in the self-concept ledger; three defeats in succession will produce the suicidal-ideation arc that recurs across the canon.

---

## 11. RESTRAINT / CONFINEMENT

The single most reliable trigger in the file, more reliable than direct threat.

**Tells.** No de-escalation curve. The host attempts compliance for the first several seconds; if release is not forthcoming, the breach is immediate and the alter that emerges is the most violent in the system. Restraint replays the helplessness of the abused child with somatic precision; the subject's body remembers what his mind has fragmented.

**Operational note.** Should never be restrained. Containment must be voluntary or it is not containment.

---

## 12. PATERNAL AUTHORITY (Ross-class figures)

**Tells in host state.** Regression. Posture stiffens to a near-military attention. Voice loses inflection. Apologizes for the existence of his condition. Submits to insulting language without verbal pushback. Does not make eye contact for the duration of the interaction. Will accept assignments and obligations he would refuse from any other party.

**Tells in alter state under same trigger.** The reverse. The alter (especially Savage) recognizes Ross-class figures and responds with a personal, focused, sustained aggression different in kind from the diffuse rage of a stress-breach. This is the alter expressing the affect the host has surrendered.

---

## 13. ROUTINE AND RITUAL

A non-exhaustive list of habitual behaviors observed across the longitudinal record:

- Pulse check on waking, before rising.
- Five to ten minutes of paced breathing before any anticipated stressful encounter.
- Reads scientific literature in the evening as soporific.
- Carries small denominations of local currency in multiple pockets (post-transformation transit fare).
- Maintains a mental list of clothing donation sites and second-hand stores in any city he occupies for more than 48 hours.
- Pre-identifies one safe person per locale (typically a physician, occasionally a priest or a bartender — paradoxically) to whom he could present in post-transformation state if necessary.
- Avoids mirrors in the first hour after waking and in the moments after stress. Mirror-avoidance is one of the most consistent micro-behaviors in the file; the introject lives in the mirror.
- Cleans wounds himself; rarely seeks medical care for minor injury; accepts it for serious injury only when the alternative is incapacity.
- Keeps a small notebook (or its modern equivalent) with names, dates, and locations — autobiographical scaffolding against amnestic fragmentation.

---

## 14. PREDICTIVE INDICES

For an observer attempting to estimate the subject's proximity to breach:

1. **Right thumb / left wrist contact** — duration and frequency. Continuous contact for more than thirty seconds is a yellow indicator.
2. **Apology density per minute of speech** — climbing density is a yellow indicator.
3. **Distance maintained from civilians** — increasing distance is an orange indicator.
4. **Glasses removal not followed by replacement** — orange indicator.
5. **Capillary green at the throat** — red indicator. Evacuate.
6. **Audible naming of the condition** ("I'm losing it") — red indicator. Approximately ten seconds remain.
7. **Voice drop mid-syllable** — breach has begun.

---

## 15. THE COUNTER-PATTERN

A complete atlas must record what the subject does **not** do, because the absences are as diagnostic as the presences.

He does not drink. He does not raise his voice in baseline state. He does not strike in baseline state. He does not lie about his condition (he conceals it; he does not deny it). He does not seek revenge. He does not hold grudges at the host level. He does not own a firearm. He does not keep photographs of his father. He does not visit his mother's grave (the avoidance is itself the marker — the grave is the locus of the recovered memory). He does not accept gifts easily. He does not celebrate his birthday. He does not, in private, look at himself in mirrors longer than function requires.
