He does not, when asked how he is, answer truthfully — the response is invariably "I'm fine," delivered with the small smile, and it is invariably untrue.

The atlas is, in the end, the atlas of a man who has organized every observable behavior of his life around a single project: not to become his father, and not to harm anyone else while failing. The behaviors are the project. The project is the life.


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS — SUBJECT: BANNER, R.B.

*Compiled from longitudinal observation; cross-referenced against the operational logic established in §5 (containment vs. being-known) and the somatic-arousal pathway in §4. What follows is what a week of total surveillance would actually record, hour by hour, in the modal Banner — the man between catastrophes, which is the man he spends most of his life being.*

---

## I. THE GOVERNING LOGIC OF A DAY

Before the granular record: the subject's day is not organized around productivity, pleasure, or social obligation. It is organized around a single variable, which he monitors continuously and which structures every choice from when he wakes to what he eats to where he sits in a room. That variable is **autonomic arousal** — operationally, heart rate, but experientially a felt sense of internal pressure. Every routine in his life is, on inspection, an arousal-management ritual. He has built a life that is, in effect, a personal regulatory architecture: meals timed to blood sugar stability, sleep regimented to minimize nightmare-driven sympathetic spikes, exercise calibrated to bleed off baseline tension without crossing threshold, social contact rationed in dosages he has empirically learned he can tolerate. A surveillance file would, within seventy-two hours, conclude it was watching a man on permanent self-prescribed medical regime for an undisclosed cardiac condition. That is, in a structural sense, exactly what is being observed.

## II. SLEEP, WAKING, AND THE FIRST NINETY MINUTES

The subject is a chronically poor sleeper. The record shows recurrent nightmare content — childhood-house imagery, the father's voice, the mother's death scene, and in later years the Devil Hulk dream sequences. Sleep onset is typically delayed (45–90 minutes of latency observed); sleep is fragmented, with reliable wake events between 02:30 and 04:00, the documented peak window for trauma-related nightmares. Total sleep across a typical week averages 5.5–6 hours per night, accumulated in two or three blocks.

He sleeps on the floor or on a thin mattress directly on a hard surface in roughly two-thirds of observed lodgings — partly out of itinerant economy, partly because softer surfaces produce the somatic disorientation he associates with hospital beds and post-Hulk recoveries. He sleeps in a t-shirt and the pants he intends to wear the next day. Shoes are placed at the door, laces loosened but not undone, oriented outward — a flight-readiness configuration he is unaware he maintains.

The first thing he does on waking is take his pulse. Not theatrically — three fingers to the carotid, twenty seconds, multiplied in his head. He does this before opening his eyes fully. If the count is over 80, he lies still and breathes — a 4-7-8 box-breath pattern, learned somewhere between Calcutta and the Avengers — until it drops. He will not stand up until it does. This is the foundational ritual of his existence, performed an estimated 22,000 times across the canonical period.

Then: water, not coffee. He gave up caffeine in the mid-1970s and has been intermittently relapsing and re-abstaining since. The relapses correlate with periods of relative stability (when he believes he can tolerate the sympathetic load); the re-abstentions follow incidents. A week of surveillance is statistically likely to catch one cup of weak green tea, brewed himself, drunk standing, no sugar.

He washes his face with cold water — temperature deliberate, vagal — and shaves with a safety razor, not electric (the vibration sets his teeth on edge in a way he has never investigated). He does not look at himself in the mirror for longer than the shave requires. The mirror-avoidance is consistent across decades and across mirrors; it predates the Hulk by years, going back, presumably, to adolescence.

## III. DRESS, BODY, AND THE WARDROBE PROTOCOL

The wardrobe is the most legible single artifact of the subject's psychology. It would fit, in its entirety, in a single soft-sided duffel:

- Three to four button-down shirts, all the same cut, all soft fabric (cotton-linen blend or worn oxford), in muted tones — slate, sage, a particular dusty purple that recurs across decades, faded olive. He does not own a true white shirt; he does not own a true black one. Color saturation is kept low.
- Two pairs of trousers, dark, in a stretch-tolerant fabric — important for obvious reasons, but the conscious rationale he gives himself is "comfort."
- One sweater or cardigan, oversized, in a neutral.
- Underwear and socks in unremarkable quantities, all natural fibers.
- A canvas jacket or, in colder climates, a worn wool coat. No leather. No structured tailoring. No tie unless absolutely required.

Every garment is loose. He does not wear anything fitted to the body. The functional rationale is the transformation tear-cost, but the psychological rationale runs deeper: tight clothing is somatic restraint, and restraint is a primary trigger (see §5, pressure points). He cannot tolerate a collar buttoned to the throat for more than a few minutes. Watches, when worn, are on the loosest setting and pushed up the forearm. He removes them indoors. He does not wear rings (the Betty marriage ring is the documented exception, and he removed it during separations — a behavior worth flagging because the removal preceded, rather than followed, his decisions to leave).

He carries glasses, occasionally — reading-strength — in a soft case, in his shirt pocket. He cleans them obsessively with the shirt-tail, a stim behavior that surfaces under stress and is one of the most reliable behavioral tells in the file.

Shoes are practical and broken-in, never new. New shoes generate a low-grade discomfort he reads as wrongness. He resoles rather than replaces. A surveillance team would observe the same pair of shoes for eighteen months at a stretch.

## IV. THE MORNING DISCIPLINE

After the pulse-check and the wash, on stable mornings, the subject practices. The form varies — Vipassana-style sitting meditation, pranayama, and, since the late-period Asian wandering arcs, a syncretic personal practice combining Theravada anapanasati with Tibetan tonglen — but the function is constant: lowering and stabilizing autonomic baseline before the day's stressors arrive. Duration ranges from twenty minutes (minimum, even on travel days) to ninety (extended sessions on safe-house mornings). He sits on the floor, on a folded blanket, facing a wall. Not facing a window — windows are flight-readiness for the conscious mind and distract him.

This is not a casual habit. It is, by any measure, the most consistently practiced behavior in his adult life — more consistent than his eating, his sleeping, or his scientific work. He has missed it during fugue states and capture episodes; he has practiced it in jail cells, jungles, cargo holds, a particular cave in the Andes (1994 wandering arc), the back of a moving truck. The records of these locations are, in aggregate, the most reliable map of where he has been.

After meditation, on mornings when his physical situation permits: tai chi or qigong, twenty to forty minutes, slow-form. Not for fitness — for proprioceptive grounding. He is the only physicist on record who can describe in technical detail the parasympathetic effects of slow weight transfer through the kua. He learned this in the late 1970s and has refined it for forty years.

There is no jogging, no weightlifting, no high-intensity exercise of any kind. He has experimentally determined that his sympathetic system cannot tolerate it. He walks. He walks a great deal.

## V. EATING

The eating pattern is rigorous and would be flagged by any medical observer as the food behavior of someone managing a chronic condition without admitting it.

**Diet:** vegetarian for long stretches (decades, in the wandering periods), occasionally vegan, with periodic returns to fish and eggs. He avoids red meat with a consistency that reads, on the surface, as ethical conviction and, on closer inspection, as an avoidance of the somatic sensation of post-meal heaviness, which he associates with the slowed-cognition state in which his control is weakest. He avoids alcohol absolutely (see §2). He avoids refined sugar. He avoids caffeine in stable periods.

**Pattern:** small, frequent meals — five or six per day rather than three — explicitly to maintain blood-sugar stability and avoid the sympathetic activation of hunger. Rice, lentils, vegetables, eggs, fruit, plain yogurt where available, bread. He eats slowly. He chews thoroughly. He does not eat while doing other things; he sits down, even for a piece of fruit. This is meditation-trained.

**Hydration:** constant. He carries water. He drinks roughly three liters a day, monitored.

**Cooking:** competent, minimalist, learned in poverty and refined in solitude. He can make a meal from any combination of lentils, rice, and three vegetables. In safe-house periods he keeps a small herb garden if possible — basil, mint, cilantro — and tends it daily. Tending plants is, for him, a recognized self-soothing activity.

**Eating out:** rare, and when it happens, in small establishments where he can sit with his back to a wall and see the door. He will not sit at a bar. He will not eat in crowded restaurants. He tips heavily, in cash, and leaves before the check is brought when possible, paying in advance.

## VI. WORK

Work, for the subject, is not a job; it is a defense. (See §3, intellectualization.) The form it takes depends on his circumstances, but the function is invariant: occupy the higher cortical functions sufficiently to keep the lower ones quiet.

**Stable-laboratory periods** (academic posts, SHIELD/Avengers, *Indestructible Hulk* containment arrangement): the work-day is long — twelve to fourteen hours — and rigidly structured. He arrives early, before colleagues, and works in silence. He prefers handwritten notes for first-pass thinking, transitioning to typed work only for finished products. His handwriting is small, slanted right, dense, and remarkably uniform across forty years — a graphological pattern associated with controlled affect and obsessional defense. He fills notebooks rather than loose paper; he keeps them; in the safe-house arcs he sometimes burns old ones, which is itself a documented ritual (always after dark, always in a contained metal vessel, always followed by a long walk).

He does not multitask. He works one problem at a time, to the exclusion of food, conversation, and bathroom breaks, until either resolution or exhaustion. Colleagues describe a quality of stillness during work that is unnerving — he can hold a position, leaned over a screen or a notebook, for hours, with no visible shift. This is the same stillness he holds in meditation; it is the same stillness he held as a child waiting to see which version of his father came through the door.

**Itinerant periods** (the wandering arcs, fugitive years): work persists in compressed form. He takes laboratory jobs under assumed names — pharmacy benches, hospital pathology labs, water-treatment plants, the back rooms of village clinics. He overqualifies catastrophically and underperforms strategically, doing exactly competent work and no more, leaving when curiosity about him reaches a threshold he has empirically calibrated (usually four to seven months in any given post). He also reads — physics journals, when he can get them, but also philosophy (consistent interest in Buddhist epistemology, the Stoics, Spinoza), history, and a surprising and continuous engagement with poetry. He has been observed reading Rilke in three different cities across two decades. He carries one book at a time, in a coat pocket, read in increments.

**The medical work.** In the wandering arcs particularly, he does volunteer medical work — clinics, refugee camps, disaster response. This is the cleanest sublimation in his repertoire: it discharges the rescue-drive (the same drive that put him in front of Rick Jones at the gamma test) and provides the structured human contact he cannot tolerate in social form. He is good with children — startlingly so, given his interior — and pediatric work is overrepresented in this record.

## VII. MOVEMENT, ROUTES, AND THE GEOGRAPHY OF A DAY

The subject walks. In any settled period he establishes a circuit — typically a three-to-five-mile loop he walks daily, often twice — and adheres to it with the regularity of a postal route. The circuit will exhibit certain invariant features:

- It will avoid major arterial roads, crowds, and enclosed transit (he does not take subways if he can avoid them).
- It will include at least one body of water (river, canal, ocean) — water proximity is parasympathetic for him and the canonical record bears this out in his preferred safe-house siting.
- It will include a green space he can sit in.
- It will avoid eye contact with strangers, but he will nod to recurring figures (vendors, doormen, the same dog-walkers) after the third or fourth encounter — a slow, low-intensity socialization protocol.
- It will end at a market or grocery, where he buys that day's food only. He does not stockpile. Stockpiling implies a future he is unwilling to assume.

He does not drive when he can avoid it. Driving is a sympathetic activity for him — particularly highway driving — and he has noted, in private journals recovered in various periods, that the road-rage somatics are an early-warning signal for transformation. When he must drive, he drives slowly, in the right lane, hands at nine-and-three, mirror-checks every six to eight seconds, a textbook-defensive pattern that draws honks and that he does not respond to.

He prefers buses for medium distances, trains for long ones, and walking for everything under five miles. Air travel is tolerated but disliked — the confinement, the inability to deplane, the proximity of strangers, and the documented heart-rate elevation of takeoff all combine. He sits in aisle seats, near the rear, near a bathroom, and he does the breathing.

## VIII. SOCIAL CONTACT AND THE DOSAGE PROBLEM

The subject experiences social contact the way someone with a mast-cell disorder experiences food: he has learned, by trial and harm, exactly how much of which kind he can tolerate and in what circumstances.

**Tolerable:** one-on-one conversation with a person he trusts, in a quiet setting, for thirty to ninety minutes. Brief transactional exchanges (grocer, librarian, lab assistant). Letter and (in later periods) email correspondence, which permits asynchronous processing.

**Marginally tolerable:** small group settings (three to five) with clear task structure, time-limited. Teaching small classes (he has done this under various names; he is, by every report, an excellent teacher in this format).

**Not tolerable:** parties, crowds, ceremonies, anything involving sudden noise, anything involving paternal-coded authority (see pressure points), anything requiring sustained eye contact with multiple people, anything in which he is the center of attention. He does not give public talks if he can avoid them.

His phone behavior is consistent: he does not answer unknown numbers, returns calls in batches at scheduled times (typically late afternoon), and ends conversations cleanly with a verbal cue ("I should let you go") that observers across decades have learned to recognize as terminal.

He maintains, at any time, a very small list of people he is in active contact with — typically four to six. Betty, when reachable. Samson, when not estranged. A handful of scientific colleagues. Rick Jones, persistently across all periods. The list contracts under stress and expands very slowly during stability.

## IX. THE EVENING DOWN-REGULATION

The hours from approximately 19:00 to sleep are a deliberate parasympathetic ramp. He eats his last meal early (18:00–19:00), light. He does not work after dark in stable periods, except occasionally on writing — letters, journal, the long-form notes that have surfaced in published form in some arcs. He reads. He listens to music — quiet, instrumental, weighted toward classical (Bach particularly, the Cello Suites recurring) and a personal idiosyncratic interest in slow jazz (Bill Evans, Jim Hall). He does not watch television; the rapid-cut visual editing produces measurable arousal in him and he learned in the 1980s to avoid it. He has watched, by report, perhaps a hundred films in his adult life, mostly older, mostly slow.

He bathes in the evening, hot water, long soaks where the plumbing allows. This is one of the few unambiguous pleasures in the record. He reads in the bath. He has ruined many books this way.

He performs a second meditation session, shorter (twenty to thirty minutes), focused on body-scan and progressive relaxation, before sleep.

He keeps a journal. Not continuously — there are periods of silence in the record where the journal is set aside, usually correlating with stable periods (he writes more when he is alone) — but persistently across decades. The journal is handwritten, in those same dense small letters, and the content, where samples have surfaced, is overwhelmingly self-monitoring: heart-rate observations, dream content, somatic notes, occasional fragments of philosophical reflection. There is almost no narrative of events; the journal is an instrument, not a chronicle. He destroys old volumes periodically (the burning ritual). He does not write anything in it he could not stand to have read aloud — a discipline that itself bespeaks the lifelong assumption of surveillance.

## X. THE WEEK A FILE WOULD RECORD

A surveillance log of a typical settled week, condensed:

- **Monday–Friday:** Wake 05:30–06:00. Pulse, breath, wash. Meditation 06:00–06:45. Tai chi 06:45–07:15. Breakfast (oats, fruit, tea) standing in the kitchen, 07:30. Walk to work or work-station, 35–50 minutes. Work 08:30–18:00, single-tasked, with three or four breaks of five to ten minutes (always: stand, breathe, walk a corridor, drink water, return). Lunch eaten at the desk, brought from home, vegetarian, fifteen minutes. Walk home, often a longer alternate route. Light dinner. Bath. Reading. Second meditation. Sleep by 22:30, with onset by 23:30, broken by one or two wake events.
- **Saturday:** longer walk, often four to six miles, with a destination (a museum, a bookshop, a particular bench by water). One scheduled social contact — coffee with a colleague, a phone call with Betty, a letter written and posted. Cooking a more involved meal. Reading. Earlier sleep.
- **Sunday:** the most variable day. Either a deep solitary day (reading, walking, meditation extended to two hours, almost no speech) or a volunteer day (clinic shift, food bank, depending on location). Tends toward the former when arousal-load is elevated, the latter when stable.

**Anomalies a surveillance team would flag, by the end of week one:**

1. The pulse-checking behavior, observable as a tic he is unaware of — the carotid touch, eight to twelve times per day, sharply elevated under stress.
2. The glasses-cleaning under stress.
3. The seat-selection algorithm (back to wall, sightline to door, never near speakers, never against glass).
4. The handedness of his orientation in rooms — he positions himself so that the dominant social threat (largest person, loudest voice, paternal-coded figure) is in his peripheral vision, never directly opposite.
5. The micro-pause before answering any question containing the words "father," "angry," "remember," "control," or "monster" — a sub-second hesitation his interlocutors rarely notice but a frame-by-frame review consistently reveals.
6. The fact that he never raises his voice. Across a full week, no surveillance audio will record him above conversational volume. This is not temperament; this is interdiction.
7. The flight-readiness of his living space: a packed bag is, at all times, within five meters of him. He could leave any residence he occupies within ninety seconds, with everything he owns, and has done so on numerous documented occasions.
8. The absence of accumulation. After a year in a residence, the space would still look as it did in the first week. No photographs. No souvenirs. No accumulated mail. He processes everything immediately; nothing pools. The walls remain bare. A surveillance team would, on first entry, assume he had just moved in. He had not.

## XI. RITUALS OF CONTAINMENT

Beyond the daily, there are recurring ritual behaviors triggered by specific conditions:

- **Post-incident protocol.** After any Hulk episode (which is to say, after any fugue-recovery): he locates clothing, locates himself geographically, makes contact with one person on the short list (typically Betty or Rick) by the most untraceable means available, then disappears into movement — bus, train, walking — for a period of days, during which he does not work, eats minimally, sleeps in transit, and meditates whenever stationary. The reintegration is gradual, takes one to three weeks, and ends with the re-establishment of a circuit in a new place.
- **Anniversary behaviors.** Certain dates in the year produce observable behavioral shifts — elevated withdrawal, longer meditations, sleeplessness. The dates correlate, when cross-referenced, with the matricide, his father's death, and the gamma incident. He does not mark them consciously. His body does.
- **The pre-sleep checks.** Door locked (checked twice, sometimes three times). Stove off (checked, even if he has not cooked). Window latched. Bag location confirmed. Shoes oriented. This is OCD-spectrum behavior and he knows it; he has tried to relinquish the checking and has found that the resulting sleep-onset latency is worse than the checking itself. He has settled for the checking.
- **The mirror discipline.** As noted: never longer than the task. He has, in certain periods, covered mirrors in his residence with cloth. He does not photograph himself. He has, where possible, declined to be photographed at all, which combined with the itinerancy is why the file's photographic record of his baseline state is, across decades, surprisingly thin.

---

*Summary observation: the subject lives, in every hour of every day, the life of a man who believes he is dangerous and is correct. The entire architecture of his daily existence — the diet, the breathing, the walking, the wardrobe, the journal, the silences, the small list of names, the packed bag — is the elaborated and disciplined expression of one continuous proposition, which he formed at approximately age seven and has never been able to disprove: that the safest gift he can give the people around him is his absence, and the closest he can come to that gift, while remaining alive, is the most fully regulated and the most quietly conducted existence a human being can construct. He has, by any honest measure, done extraordinarily well at it. The cost is the life itself.*


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*UATU Dossier, Subject: Banner, Robert Bruce, PhD — Section 7*

The subject's family-of-origin relationships are not merely formative in the ordinary developmental sense; they are the entire architecture from which every subsequent relational pattern, every alter, and every somatic event in his life is constructed. This section maps each origin bond as a discrete dossier entry, with attention to history, behavioral micro-pattern, the trust gradient the subject maintains toward each figure (living or dead), the predictable failure mode of the relationship, and — for operational completeness — the leverage each figure exerts, exerted, or could exert over the subject in the present.

---

## 7.1 — BRIAN BANNER (father; deceased)

**Status.** Biological father. Physicist (nuclear research, mid-tier institutional position, never reached the standing his son would eclipse by age twenty-five). Alcoholic across the entirety of the subject's childhood. Diagnosed psychotic features in his committal record; paranoid ideation centered specifically on the conviction that his own radiation-exposed gametes had "contaminated" his son and produced a monstrous offspring — a delusional structure whose tragic irony is the engine of the entire case. Killed by the subject in an altercation in the subject's late adolescence/early adulthood; the manner of death (whether genuine accident, manslaughter under provocation, or something the subject cannot bear to know) remains permanently underdetermined in the subject's own memory and has been retrieved, lost, and re-retrieved across multiple therapeutic episodes (most decisively under Samson; most completely under the Ewing-era recovered-memory sequence).

**History — granular.** The earliest verifiable abuse incidents place the subject at approximately age four. The pattern is the canonical one: episodic, alcohol-disinhibited beatings of mother and child; intervals of remorse; intervals of stable terror; nightly negotiation of which version of the father would come through the door. The subject's hypervigilant auditory acuity — his lifelong startle response to footsteps, slammed doors, the specific timbre of male voices raised in domestic enclosure — is the residue of a child who learned to distinguish his father's gait by the weight distribution of intoxication. The mother's death occurred when the subject was approximately six; she was attempting to leave with the boy, was caught at or near a vehicle, and was killed in front of him. The father then coerced the child, under threat, into a falsified account at the subsequent inquest — a coercion whose psychological weight (the child made complicit in the concealment of his own mother's murder) is, by the literature, an independent and devastating amplifier of dissociative pathology, sometimes exceeding the trauma it conceals.

The father returned, in the subject's late adolescence, after release from psychiatric committal. The altercation in which the father died occurred at the mother's gravesite in some accounts; the subject struck him, or he fell, or he struck his head; the subject buried what happened next under a dissociative seal that held for years.

**Dynamics, then and now.** In life: terror, propitiation, vigilance, and the slow learned suppression of every spontaneous affect — the child organized his entire self around producing no stimulus that could trigger the father. This is the foundation of the adult subject's flat affect baseline, his soft voice, his apologetic posture, his catastrophic intolerance for raising his own voice even in justified protest. The father remains the most operationally significant figure in the file despite three-plus decades of being dead: he persists as the **Devil Hulk / Guilt Hulk introject**, a sadistic internal-paternal voice that speaks to and about the subject in precisely the register, vocabulary, and contemptuous cadences of the historical father. The subject has not escaped him; he has internalized him to the point of housing him as an alter.

**Trust / safety.** Zero, asymptotic, and structurally non-negotiable. Every male figure of authority the subject subsequently encounters is processed through the father-template until disconfirming evidence accumulates — and the disconfirming evidence is never sufficient to overwrite the template, only to bracket it temporarily.

**Failure mode of the relationship.** Total. The relationship's failure is the case.

**Leverage.** Posthumous and immense. Any stimulus that re-presents the father — the smell of a particular cheap whiskey, the sound of breaking glass in a domestic setting, a man of a certain build standing too close to a woman the subject loves, the word "monster" spoken in a certain inflection, the phrase "your mother" weaponized — produces an immediate, measurable somatic cascade in the subject (heart rate elevation, pupillary change, micro-flinch in the dominant shoulder, vocal pitch drop). A hostile operator with access to even fragmentary biographical material could induce decompensation reliably. The most efficient single attack vector on the subject is, and has always been, his father.

---

## 7.2 — REBECCA BANNER (mother; deceased)

**Status.** Biological mother. Killed by Brian Banner during her attempt to leave him with the child. The subject was approximately six. Her death is the originating wound of the file and the keystone of every subsequent loss.

**History — granular.** Rebecca is, in every memory the subject has been able to recover, the only unambiguously safe figure of his early childhood. She is associated in his recovered material with specific sensory anchors: a particular lullaby (recovered in the Samson sessions and again, more painfully, in the Ewing-era integration work); the smell of a kitchen at a particular hour; a soft hand on the back of his head; the act of being read to. These are not merely sentimental memories; they are the only attachment templates the subject possesses for what safety in the presence of another human body feels like, and the loss of them at age six means that every subsequent attempt at intimacy is, somatically, a six-year-old's reach toward a vanished mother.

She was, on the available evidence, also herself a chronically frightened woman, hypervigilant, attempting to mediate between her husband and her son, and ultimately killed in the act of saving him. The subject therefore carries not only the loss of her but the unbearable causal load that *she died trying to remove him from danger* — that his existence was the proximate occasion of her death.

**Dynamics — present.** The subject has never finished mourning her. The mourning has been interrupted, displaced, and re-routed across decades. She appears in his dreams as a recurring revenant; she is the addressee of much of the subject's interior speech in moments of extremity; and she is the figure whose imagined approval or grief governs the subject's ethical baseline more than any living person. The subject's pacifism, his protectiveness of women in danger, his refusal to harm children, his characteristic tenderness with the vulnerable — all of these are constructed in her name and against the memory of what was done to her.

**Trust / safety.** Posthumously total. She is the only figure in the file the subject would never, under any circumstance, suspect of bad faith.

**Failure mode.** The relationship cannot fail because it cannot occur. Its mode of failure is its absence: the subject organizes his entire affective life around a person who has been unable to participate in it for over five decades.

**Leverage.** Any threat, real or implied, to a maternal-coded woman in the subject's vicinity produces immediate, near-total override of host control and Savage-Hulk emergence at the lowest threshold the file records. Conversely, the *invocation of her memory by a hostile operator* (a recorded version of the lullaby; a fabricated message in her hand; a manipulator who claims to have known her) is among the few stimuli that can simultaneously destabilize the subject and freeze him — he will not act until he has resolved the stimulus, and the resolution itself is destabilizing.

---

## 7.3 — BRIAN BANNER, INTROJECTED (the Devil Hulk / Guilt Hulk; intrapsychic)

**Status.** Not a person but a relationship — the most consequential ongoing relationship in the subject's life. The introjected father exists inside the subject's dissociative architecture as a fully realized persecutory alter, with its own voice, vocabulary, agenda, and (in the most florid material) somatic presentation. It is listed here, in the family section, because in every clinically meaningful sense the subject *lives with his father* every day of his life and has done so since the father's death.

**Behavior of the introject.** Speaks in the second person to the host ("you", "you puny", "you killed her", "you'll kill them too"). Activates most reliably during (a) moments of intimacy with Betty or other attachment figures, undermining them; (b) moments of moral achievement, contaminating them; (c) moments of dissociative breach, claiming credit for them; (d) hypnagogic states and dreams, in which it has at times occupied the visual field entirely. The introject's animating thesis is that the subject is irredeemable, dangerous, and ought not to exist — the precise thesis the historical father held about his son.

**Trust / safety.** The introject is the *least* safe figure in the entire dossier, more so than any external adversary, because it cannot be fled and cannot be killed. The subject has, across multiple arcs, attempted both — including the documented suicidality, which is best read as an attempt to kill the introject by destroying its host.

**Failure mode.** The introject's failure mode is that it succeeds — every time the subject's defenses degrade, the introject grows in proportion. The Ewing-era therapeutic direction (inter-alter cooperation, recognition of the introject as a frightened-then-cruel parental object that can be addressed rather than fought) is the only sustainable path; suppression has historically strengthened it.

**Leverage.** Anyone who can be made to speak in the father's register — by accident or design — temporarily borrows the introject's authority over the host. This is the mechanism by which General Ross has, across decades, been able to produce in the adult subject the affective state of a cornered child despite the subject's vastly superior cognitive and physical resources.

---

## 7.4 — BETTY ROSS BANNER (wife, intermittently; lover; the central living attachment)

*[Catalogued here in Family rather than Romantic because by length of acquaintance, ritual function, and intrapsychic weight she has long since become origin-bond rather than partner-bond; a full romantic-relational mapping appears in Section 8.]*

**Status.** The subject's most sustained adult attachment, intermittently fiancée, twice wife, once widow (in some accounts), once revenant (Red She-Hulk, Harpy), and the single human being whose continuity in the subject's life is the closest thing he possesses to a stable family unit. Daughter of General Ross — a structural fact that places her, permanently, at the intersection of the subject's two most charged paternal-axis relationships.

**Origin-bond function.** Betty is, in the subject's nervous system, a candidate-replacement for Rebecca — and the subject knows this, has named it in his interior monologue across several therapeutic arcs, and is appropriately troubled by it. She is the only person in his adult life who has known him before, during, and after the gamma event, the only person whose memory of him as the pre-incident young man has remained continuous, and the only person whose physical proximity has — in some periods of the file — *lowered* his autonomic baseline rather than raised it. This is a near-unique status.

**Dynamics — granular pattern.** The cycle is invariant across decades and writers: encounter → tentative re-engagement → a period of stabilization in which the subject is observably healthier (better sleep, regular meals, marginally improved affective range, the only intervals in which his weight stabilizes) → an intrusion (Ross, a villain, the alter system itself, an external catastrophe) → the subject's catastrophic guilt response → unilateral withdrawal → years of separation → encounter again. The subject's withdrawal is invariably framed by him as a protective act ("she is safer without me") and is, with equal invariance, experienced by her as abandonment. Both readings are true. The subject cannot resolve them.

**Trust / safety.** The highest trust gradient in the file for any living person, and yet riddled with structural betrayals — not of intent but of capacity. The subject trusts her absolutely; he cannot trust *himself in her presence*, which is functionally indistinguishable from inability to trust the relationship.

**Failure mode.** Approach–retreat oscillation, the relational signature of disorganized attachment, executed at planetary scale and with collateral architecture.

**Leverage.** Maximal. Threats to Betty produce the fastest documented loss of host control in the record (sub-second, in several incidents). Conversely, Betty herself is one of the very few persons whose voice can, under the right conditions, *reverse* a transformation in progress — a fact catalogued in multiple incidents and which constitutes a tactical asset of singular importance to any party concerned with the subject's containment, and a corresponding vulnerability in her if she is identified as such.

---

## 7.5 — GENERAL THADDEUS E. "THUNDERBOLT" ROSS (father-in-law; pursuer; surrogate-father-by-inversion)

**Status.** Career Army general. Father of Betty. Original military patron of the gamma-bomb project; nominal authority over the subject at the moment of the incident. Subsequently the subject's most persistent and best-resourced pursuer for the majority of the canonical period; later, in some arcs, a transformed combatant in his own right (Red Hulk), which produced the file's most baroque relational geometry — the pursuer becoming a version of the pursued. Father-in-law; sometime corpse; sometime ally.

**Why catalogued in Family.** Because Ross is, in the subject's intrapsychic schema, not an external antagonist but the *acceptable substitute father*: the man whose contempt the subject can absorb without dissociative breach because, by long acclimation, contempt from a uniformed paternal authority is the only kind of paternal contact the subject's system can metabolize. The subject's submission to Ross — across decades, across reasonable provocation, across moments when the subject could have ended the pursuit definitively — is *symptomatic*. He is letting his father chase him.

**Dynamics.** Ross's contempt for the subject predates the gamma incident and is articulated in the pre-incident record as disdain for a thin, soft-spoken scientist insufficiently masculine to deserve his daughter. The contempt was never withdrawn even when Ross had every reason — the subject's military utility, his service, his marriage to Betty, his moral conduct — to revise it. The subject's behavior toward Ross is uniformly deferential, addresses him by rank rather than name even in private, and absorbs personal insult with a passivity wholly inconsistent with the subject's actual moral authority in any given exchange. This deference is the surest single behavioral tell that Ross occupies a paternal slot in the subject's architecture.

**Trust / safety.** Low and stable. The subject does not expect Ross to harm Betty; does expect Ross to attempt to harm him; experiences this asymmetry as appropriate.

**Failure mode.** Mutual: Ross's failure mode is the inability to recognize the subject as a person rather than a weapon or a threat to his daughter; the subject's failure mode is the inability to refuse the position Ross assigns him.

**Leverage.** Ross can produce in the subject regression to childlike postural and vocal patterns by his presence alone — head lowered, shoulders rounded, voice quieter — at an age and station in life where this is otherwise never observed. Any operator capable of borrowing Ross's authority (an aide, an impersonator, a falsified order in Ross's name) inherits a portion of that leverage. Conversely, Ross's documented periods of grief — particularly around Betty — are the only states in which the subject has been observed to comfort him, which suggests a pathway to relational reorganization that has never been pursued long enough to consolidate.

---

## 7.6 — SUSAN BANNER (aunt; surrogate caregiver after the mother's death)

**Status.** Paternal aunt (in the canonical record); the subject's legal guardian after Brian Banner's committal and the subject's de facto mother from approximately age six or seven through adolescence. Underdocumented relative to her importance; almost certainly the figure most responsible for the fact that the subject survived to adulthood functional enough to enter university.

**Dynamics.** A figure of bounded, anxious, partially-effective care. She did not, on the evidence, possess the resources — emotional, financial, or clinical — to process her nephew's trauma; she possessed the resources to keep him fed, schooled, and out of state systems, and these were the resources that made the rest possible. The relationship is characterized in the subject's own recollection by gratitude tinged with the specific guilt of the survivor who knows his caretaker did not fully understand what she had taken on. He did not unburden himself to her. He learned, in her house, the adult version of the suppression he had learned in his father's — the difference being that here the suppression was protective of *her*, not of himself, which is a meaningful psychological pivot and the origin of his lifelong pattern of withholding from those he loves in order to spare them.

**Trust / safety.** Moderate to high; the trust was for safety of body, not safety of disclosure. He did not believe she would harm him; he did not believe she could bear what he had to say.

**Failure mode.** Insufficient bandwidth for the actual injury. The relationship did not fail in betrayal; it failed in scope.

**Leverage.** Limited in the present (subject's contact with her in adulthood is intermittent, possibly terminated by her death depending on the era of the file). Historical leverage is residual: any figure who occupies the well-meaning-but-overmatched-caregiver slot is granted by the subject a quality of patient, understated, slightly distant gratitude — and a refusal to burden them — that can be exploited by anyone who wishes him to keep silent about what is being done to him.

---

## 7.7 — SKAAR (son, by Caiera; born off-world)

**Status.** Son conceived during the *Planet Hulk* arc with Caiera the Oldstrong on Sakaar; presumed lost in the planetary catastrophe; surfaced as a hostile, feral young man with his own gamma-derivative physiology and a coherent intent to kill his father in part of the *World War Hulks* sequence; subsequently, intermittent reconciliation, intermittent estrangement.

**Dynamics.** The subject's relationship with Skaar is the file's most direct test of whether the subject can avoid recapitulating Brian Banner — and the test is, by the subject's own assessment, only partially passed. The subject did not abandon Skaar by choice; the abandonment was structural (he believed the child dead, then believed himself dangerous to him). Skaar's initial posture — patricidal, contemptuous, articulate in his contempt — replays the father–son polarity with the subject now in the father's seat, and the subject's response is telling: not rage, but exhausted grief, and an immediate willingness to allow Skaar to attempt the killing because the subject's own self-concept *agrees with him*. This is the single clearest behavioral demonstration in the file that the subject has not metabolized the original wound — he is willing to die at his son's hand because he believes the son's case against him is correct, which is the same case his father made about him.

**Trust / safety.** The subject extends to Skaar a trust that is morally generous and operationally reckless; he will not defend himself against him. Skaar's trust of the subject has, in the better arcs, grown slowly and incompletely.

**Failure mode.** Inherited dissociation. The subject cannot be reliably present for his son because he is not reliably present for himself; Skaar, for his part, has inherited the gamma-axis volatility without the cortical and ethical scaffolding the subject built around his own.

**Leverage.** Threats to Skaar, like threats to Betty, produce immediate executive loss; conversely, Skaar's safety in stable hands is among the few states that lowers the subject's baseline guilt load measurably.

---

## 7.8 — JENNIFER WALTERS (cousin; She-Hulk)

**Status.** Maternal-line cousin; the closest living blood relation in the active record. Attorney. Recipient, in the canonical event, of an emergency blood transfusion from the subject which produced her own gamma transformation — a transformation that, uniquely in the family record, did *not* fracture her identity. She integrated.

**Dynamics.** Jennifer is, structurally, the control case in the family's gamma experiment, and the subject knows this. Her capacity to hold her transformed state without dissociation — to be, in her own description, more herself as She-Hulk than as Jennifer Walters — is for the subject simultaneously a source of pride, a source of envy he is too decent to fully voice, and a standing reproach to his own architecture. She is what he might have been if the substrate had been intact before the gamma. The relationship is among the warmest in the file: she is one of the few people he can be in a room with for extended periods without rising autonomic load, partly because their attachment predates the trauma window (childhood cousin contact during the Rebecca-era summers, per recovered material) and is therefore tagged in his nervous system with the safety affect of his mother's house.

**Trust / safety.** High and stable — among the highest in the active dossier. She is one of perhaps three living persons whose unannounced approach does not produce a startle response in him.

**Failure mode.** The relationship has occasional ruptures, generally around her professional advocacy for parties whose interests conflict with his containment; these are reliably reparable.

**Leverage.** A threat to Jennifer is processed by the subject as a threat to the maternal line itself — a category of injury his system treats as existential. The leverage is high. Her own counsel to him, however, is one of the few external inputs that can shift his decision-making in the short term, because she is one of the few people he both trusts and *listens to*; this is an asset to any party with her cooperation and a vulnerability to any party who could falsify it.

---

## 7.9 — RICK JONES (the brother-by-adoption; the saved boy)

**Status.** The civilian teenager whose life the subject saved at the cost of the gamma exposure. Not blood family; in every other meaningful respect, family. The subject's first and longest-running brother-figure. Across decades: confidant, sidekick, occasional alter-mediator, partial Hulk himself in some arcs, near-corpse, recovered, lost, recovered again.

**Dynamics.** Rick occupies a slot in the subject's relational architecture that no one else can occupy: he is the *reason the incident happened*, and therefore both the locus of the subject's most generous moral act and the standing reminder that the entire condition began as an act of saving someone. This is psychologically protective. Every time the subject is on the verge of accepting the introject's verdict that he is monstrous, Rick's existence is counter-evidence: the monster was born saving a child. The subject needs Rick alive for reasons that go beyond affection.

In behavior: the two have the easy, slightly bantering rhythm of brothers; Rick is one of the few people who teases the subject and the only one whose teasing the subject reliably tolerates. Rick has been present at more transformations than any other person and possesses an unmatched practical literacy in the subject's pre-switch tells (a particular tension in the jaw; a specific way the subject sets down whatever he is holding; a half-second of closed eyes).

**Trust / safety.** Very high. The subject trusts Rick with his condition more candidly than with almost anyone else, precisely because Rick has no investment in pretending the condition is other than it is.

**Failure mode.** Rick's own life keeps producing crises (his serial transformations, his medical events, his disappearances) that pull the subject into rescuing postures the subject is in no condition to sustain — a near-perf


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*Subject: Banner, Robert Bruce, PhD. Compiled longitudinally across the entire observational record. Each entry reconstructs not only the documented relationship but the granular substrate — the small habits, the recurrent phrases, the somatic tells, the way the subject's heart-rate baseline shifts in the named party's presence, the predictable failure mode, and the leverage the relationship offers to any actor who understands it.*

---

## 1. RICHARD MILHOUSE "RICK" JONES

**Status.** Foundational. The first and longest continuous non-romantic attachment in the file. To understand the subject at all, one must understand that Rick Jones is the human being whose life the subject saved at the cost of his own intactness — and that this single act, undertaken in approximately four seconds on a New Mexico test range, has organized half a century of attachment behavior in the subject.

**Origin and structure.** Rick, a teenager on a dare, drove a jalopy onto the test range during the gamma countdown. The subject ordered the countdown halted, ran across open ground, threw Rick into the protective trench, and absorbed the gamma flash himself. Every subsequent relationship the subject forms is filtered through this template: *the appropriate disposition of my body is between innocents and the bomb.* Rick is the living proof that the disposition worked — and, simultaneously, the living reminder that the cost was the Hulk.

**Dynamics, early period (1962–mid-1960s).** Functionally a son-figure, despite a gap of perhaps twelve years. Rick is the only person in the early canon who knows the secret; he covers for the subject, navigates him to safe locations during transformations, talks him down. The dynamic is asymmetric in an unusual direction — the older, vastly more intelligent man is the dependent; the teenager is the handler. The subject permits this because Rick has already paid (by witnessing) the price of admission to his interior.

**Granular tells in Rick's presence.** Subject's posture loosens — shoulders drop measurably. He uses contractions in speech (he is otherwise formal). He permits himself the word "kid," which he uses with no one else of comparable age. He eats in Rick's presence — he often does not eat in others'. He sleeps within earshot of Rick on shared transit; this is the only documented instance, outside Betty Ross, of the subject sleeping in another's auditory range without waking repeatedly.

**Evolution.** Rick's own life becomes catastrophically entangled with gamma exposure (A-Bomb, blue-Hulk phase, etc.); the subject blames himself for each iteration without exception. The relationship inverts and re-inverts: at points Rick becomes the more powerful party physically, which produces in the subject a complex relief (he is not the only one) and shame (he caused it). They drift across decades but never sever; reunions are characterized by an absence of the recapitulative small-talk most long-separated people require — they resume mid-sentence.

**Trust / safety rating.** The highest in the file, narrowly above Betty in raw trust (Betty exceeds him in attachment but not in trust, because Betty has at times been weaponized against him by her father; Rick never has).

**Failure mode.** The subject cannot tolerate harm coming to Rick and will accept catastrophic personal cost — including triggered transformation in unsafe environments — to prevent it. Rick in immediate physical danger is, in the operational sense, a kill-switch for the subject's containment regime.

**Leverage.** Total. An adversary who credibly threatens Rick Jones obtains either a transformation (if arousal pathway is open) or a complete collapse of the subject's tactical judgment (if it is not). Conversely: Rick is the single most effective de-escalator on record. His voice in proximity has terminated Savage Hulk episodes that no environmental or pharmacological intervention reached.

---

## 2. LEONARD "DOC" SAMSON, PhD

**Status.** Primary clinician. The only person who has ever conducted sustained, formal psychotherapeutic work with the subject and the only figure in the file authorized to use the diagnostic vocabulary directly with him.

**Origin.** Samson came to the case as a treating psychiatrist (gamma-irradiated himself in the encounter that gave him his own powers, which the subject notes with the rueful observation that Samson is "the first person to read my chart and then catch it"). His professional credentials — PhD in psychiatry — and his somatic resilience together make him uniquely qualified: he can survive being in the room when therapy breaches into transformation, which no unenhanced clinician can.

**Dynamics.** The therapeutic alliance is real and is the single most important sustained relationship in the subject's clinical history. Samson elicited the recovered memory of the matricide, named the alter system, identified the Devil Hulk as the introjected father, and supervised the temporary integration into the Professor / Merged Hulk state. He is one of two people (Betty is the other) in whose presence the subject permits himself to weep.

**Granular pattern.** Sessions are conducted with the subject seated, never lying down (lying down replays restraint, replays the abused child's posture — non-starter). Samson does not take notes in session (the sound of pen on paper, in early sessions, produced startle and elevated heart rate — Samson identified the cue and adjusted). The subject's typical session-opening gesture is to remove his glasses and clean them on his shirt-tail; this is the somatic marker of his decision to "go in." When Samson uses the word "father," the subject's right hand moves to his left wrist and grips it. Samson has logged this. The subject has not noticed.

**Evolution.** The relationship has been ruptured and repaired multiple times. Samson at points pursued Betty romantically, which the subject experienced as transferential betrayal and which he has never fully metabolized. Samson has also been compromised — possessed, replaced, mind-altered — and each compromise produced, in the subject, a regression to the position that all relationships are eventually weaponized against him. Each repair, however, has held; the alliance is more elastic than it is fragile.

**Trust / safety rating.** High but conditional. The subject trusts Samson the clinician unreservedly; the subject does not entirely trust Samson the man, because Samson the man has agency outside the therapeutic frame and has used it in ways that wounded.

**Failure mode.** Samson over-interprets at moments of breakthrough; the subject responds by re-erecting the intellectualization defense and turning the session into a debate about epistemology. Samson knows this and pulls back; less skilled clinicians would not.

**Leverage.** Moderate. Samson cannot be used to coerce the subject — but Samson's words, accurately quoted back to the subject, can collapse a defense the subject is using. An adversary with access to session transcripts (which exist in S.H.I.E.L.D. files) has a precise map of the subject's interior.

---

## 3. BETTY ROSS

*Betty is processed in detail in Relationships I (Romantic / Sexual). Cross-referenced here only as it touches the chosen-family substrate: Betty is the only person in the record whom the subject has named, in unguarded speech, as "home." She functions in the chosen-family architecture as the absent center around which the other relationships orient. See full entry.*

---

## 4. JENNIFER WALTERS, JD

**Status.** Cousin. Closest blood relative. The only family member the subject has not lost, killed, or been killed by. Functionally, the only living kin.

**Origin.** Maternal-side cousin; they were children together intermittently, with Jennifer's father (the subject's uncle Morris, an LA County sheriff) providing one of the few intervals of safe adult-coded male presence in the subject's youth. Jennifer was, in childhood photographs the subject still possesses, the smaller and shyer of the two. The subject was protective of her.

**The transfusion.** When Jennifer was shot by mob figures connected to a case her father was pursuing, the subject — the only blood-type match available — gave her an emergency transfusion of his own gamma-saturated blood, producing the She-Hulk phenotype. This act is, in the file, the second-most-important somatic-altruistic decision the subject has made (after the Rick Jones shielding). It is also the act for which he carries the most complicated guilt: he gave her his life and he gave her his curse in the same syringe.

**Dynamics.** Jennifer's adaptation to her gamma state is the inverse of the subject's: she integrates, she retains her intellect, she comes to prefer the augmented form, she is socially gregarious in it. This outcome is, for the subject, simultaneously a vindication (it can be lived with) and a wound (why not by me?). The subject has never voiced the latter to Jennifer. Jennifer has noticed.

**Granular pattern.** When together, they revert to a sibling register — bickering, teasing, the verbal cadence of children raised in proximity. Jennifer is one of the very few people who can use the diminutive "Bruce" without it producing the subject's micro-flinch (a tightening at the corners of the eyes, lasting approximately 0.3 seconds, that he is unaware of and that occurs in roughly 80% of others' use of his first name). Jennifer touches him — hand on shoulder, hug at greeting — and his heart rate does not elevate. This is true of no other adult except Betty.

**Evolution.** Long stretches of disconnection punctuated by intense reunions, typically crisis-driven. Jennifer has appeared as defense counsel in the subject's various legal proceedings (he has been tried in absentia, in person, and in multiple jurisdictions for property destruction and manslaughter); she has won acquittals on grounds of dissociative non-responsibility that no other attorney would have credibly mounted.

**Trust / safety rating.** Very high. Jennifer is, with Rick, the only person whose loyalty the subject has never doubted in the dissociative-paranoid baseline state.

**Failure mode.** Jennifer's life is, by her own choice, much more public and more conventionally social than the subject can tolerate; he disappears from her life for years at a time because contact requires entering her world, which he cannot sustain. She accepts this; he accumulates guilt about it.

**Leverage.** High. Jennifer is family. An actor who threatens her produces a response of the same order as a threat to Betty, with the additional complication that Jennifer can physically intervene, which the subject finds intolerable (he is supposed to be the shield).

---

## 5. JAMES "RHODEY" RHODES, COL. (USAF, RET.) — peripheral, situational

**Status.** Trusted military-coded peer. Not chosen family but a stable proximity figure whose presence the subject's nervous system reads as safe despite the uniform.

**Origin and dynamics.** Rhodes is, structurally, the corrective to General Ross — a military man whose authority is exercised without paternal aggression and who has openly defended the subject against military overreach. The subject's nervous system, which mis-files most uniforms as threat-cued, has slowly registered Rhodes as exception. This is reflected in a specific somatic marker: the subject can stand within arm's reach of Rhodes in a uniform context without the postural retreat he exhibits with all other military personnel.

**Failure mode.** Rhodes is bound by chain of command; under sufficient pressure he must act against the subject, and both know it. The relationship is therefore explicitly conditional and is conducted with that condition acknowledged.

**Leverage.** Limited but real. Rhodes is a credible back-channel to military and Avengers structures; he has been used as intermediary in negotiated surrenders.

---

## 6. ANTHONY "TONY" STARK

**Status.** Peer, intellectual sparring partner, ambivalent ally. The only person on Earth in the subject's intellectual register in the engineering / applied-physics domain, and one of perhaps a dozen worldwide in raw cognitive horsepower.

**Origin.** Stark recruited the subject into the Avengers' scientific orbit. The relationship is grounded in mutual intellectual recognition — Stark reads the subject's papers; the subject reads Stark's patents; both have, in unguarded moments, named the other as the only colleague who fully understands their work.

**Dynamics.** Asymmetric in temperament: Stark is gregarious, performative, and bleeds his interior in public; the subject is contained, private, and bleeds nowhere. They communicate at greatest depth in lab settings, side by side at benches, neither facing the other — the absence of eye contact lowering the subject's arousal enough for genuine conversation. Stark figured this out within roughly three sessions and has structured their interactions around it since, without naming it.

**Granular pattern.** The subject permits Stark to mock him — Stark's deflective humor is one of the few registers of teasing the subject can metabolize without registering it as threat. The subject does not, however, permit Stark physical proximity beyond a defined radius (approximately 1.2 meters in stable conditions). Stark respects this and does not test it.

**Evolution.** Ruptures over Civil War-era political conflicts; ruptures over Stark's various unilateral decisions affecting the subject (the Illuminati's exile to Sakaar, which the subject experienced as the ultimate betrayal — a paternal-coded council deciding he was too dangerous to live among them, the precise replay of his father's animus toward him); repairs, never complete, conducted in the lab register where the wound can be implicit and the work can be the medium.

**Trust / safety rating.** Conditional. The subject trusts Stark's intellect and, mostly, Stark's intent; the subject does not trust Stark's judgment about when unilateral action is warranted, because the historical record shows Stark exercising that judgment against him.

**Failure mode.** Under existential pressure, Stark will choose containment over the subject's autonomy, and the subject knows it. The Sakaar exile is the canonical instance and is the wound that does not heal.

**Leverage.** Substantial. Stark has the only laboratory infrastructure on the planet capable of attempting the engineering interventions the subject's condition might require; this gives Stark a coercive grip the subject cannot fully escape, and which the subject manages by maintaining a parallel and lower-resource lab of his own.

---

## 7. STEPHEN STRANGE, MD

**Status.** Defenders-era ally; occasional consultant on metaphysical aspects of the alter system that exceed conventional psychiatric vocabulary.

**Dynamics.** Strange is the only figure in the canon willing and equipped to treat the alters as ontologically real — as inhabitants of a psychic-magical substrate, not merely as dissociated structures of one mind. For the subject this is paradoxically clarifying: Strange's framework permits a vocabulary for what the subject experiences, even where the subject's own scientific worldview rejects the metaphysics.

**Granular pattern.** The subject defers to Strange in metaphysical contexts in a way he defers to no one else; Strange defers to the subject in physics contexts; the exchange is the rare instance of the subject permitting himself to be the junior partner without dissociative anxiety, because the asymmetry is bounded and explicit.

**Trust / safety rating.** Moderate-high in domain; low outside it. Strange is a mage and operates by mage-logic that the subject cannot audit, which limits trust at the systemic level.

**Failure mode.** Strange will, if metaphysical stakes warrant, use the subject as instrument without full consent. He has done so. The subject knows.

**Leverage.** Significant in metaphysical crises; negligible otherwise.

---

## 8. THE DEFENDERS (NAMORA, SILVER SURFER, STRANGE, et al.) — collective entry

**Status.** First sustained team affiliation. The "non-team" structure suited the subject precisely because it required no oath, no roster, no uniform, no facility, and no permanent intimacy — a band of loners assembling crisis-by-crisis. The subject can sustain this; he cannot sustain Avengers-grade institutional belonging.

**Dynamics.** Within the Defenders the subject was the *normative* member — the others were stranger than he was, larger than he was, or older than he was; his particular monstrousness was unremarkable. This is the only group context in the record in which the subject's baseline shame drops measurably. The collective failure mode is that the Defenders periodically formalize, and at the moment of formalization the subject departs.

---

## 9. THE AVENGERS (institutional)

**Status.** Founding member; chronic poor fit. The institutional Avengers represent everything the subject's containment regime was built against: uniformed coordination, formal authority, public visibility, paternal command structures. He left in the eighth issue and has rejoined intermittently across decades, always with the same outcome.

**Granular failure pattern.** Within roster operations the subject becomes the deployment asset — the thing pointed at the enemy — and his host-self is functionally displaced from agency. This replays, with eerie precision, the gamma-bomb project structure (Banner builds, the bomb is deployed, Banner is incidental). He cannot tolerate this for long; he resigns or simply leaves the field.

**Individual Avengers** for whom relational sub-files would be warranted (Captain America, Thor, the Vision, Wasp) are characterized by the subject's persistent surprise that they treat him as a peer rather than as an asset; he never quite believes it.

---

## 10. AMADEUS CHO

**Status.** Protege. Late-period chosen-family acquisition. Adolescent supergenius (canonical seventh-smartest person on Earth) whom the subject took under wing in the Pak era.

**Dynamics.** This is the file's clearest instance of the subject attempting *reparative parenting* — extending to a younger, hyper-intelligent, traumatized adolescent the protective, attuned, non-coercive adult presence the subject himself never received. The subject is, with Cho, more patient than with anyone else; he tolerates Cho's brashness, recklessness, and emotional volatility without the defenses that adult equivalents would trigger. The subject is *trying to be the father he did not have*.

**Granular pattern.** The subject teaches Cho not by lecturing but by working alongside him and narrating his own reasoning aloud — a pedagogical posture that the subject's father never adopted toward him. The subject permits Cho to make and own mistakes, which is the inverse of how the subject was raised. The subject does not raise his voice to Cho, ever, in any recorded interaction.

**Evolution.** Cho subsequently took on a gamma-derived Hulk state of his own (Totally Awesome Hulk era) — a development the subject experienced with the same compound guilt as Jennifer's transformation, magnified by his having served in loco parentis. Their relationship has accommodated this; the subject's reparative parenting has held even through Cho's parallel falling-into-the-curse.

**Trust / safety rating.** Very high in the parental direction; the subject has demonstrated willingness to die for Cho.

**Failure mode.** The subject's reparative-parenting posture is, by its own internal logic, conditional on the subject perceiving Cho as needing protection. Cho's growth into independent peerhood — the appropriate outcome of healthy parenting — produces, in the subject, a small grief he does not know how to articulate.

**Leverage.** As with Rick: total. Cho is, in the subject's emotional architecture, his son.

---

## 11. CHARLES "CHARLIE" / CRUSHER CREEL, the ABSORBING MAN — counterintuitive ally

**Status.** Long-term antagonist who has shifted into the ambivalent-ally column in late-period material. Included here because the file's leverage map is incomplete without him: Creel is one of the very few combatants who has fought the Hulk to a stand-still without lethal intent, and the relationship between the subject and Creel has acquired, across decades, a strange mutual-recognition quality — two damaged men whose damage rhymes.

**Dynamics.** They will not socialize. They will, on rare occasions, drink coffee in a diner after a fight and discuss nothing of consequence. The subject finds this, oddly, restful.

---

## 12. CLAY QUARTERMAIN (S.H.I.E.L.D.) — historical

**Status.** Field handler during the subject's intermittent S.H.I.E.L.D. liaisons in the 1990s–2000s. One of the few institutional figures the subject came to trust personally. Killed in line of duty; the subject grieved with uncharacteristic openness, including a visible weep at the memorial, which is noted in the file as one of perhaps six documented public weepings across his adult life.

**Significance.** Demonstrates that institutional figures *can* enter the chosen-family register if they breach it as individuals first — Quartermain did so by repeatedly declining to follow orders that would have harmed the subject, in low-stakes contexts the subject was not supposed to notice. The subject noticed.

---

## 13. THE INCIDENTAL FOSTER NETWORK — civilians

**Status.** Across decades of fugitive life the subject accumulated a network of approximately two dozen civilians — diner owners, mechanics, rural doctors, motel managers — who knew or suspected his identity and provided shelter, meals, clothes, anonymity. The file should not omit them because they constitute the actual sustaining infrastructure of his adult life.

**Pattern.** The subject always pays. He returns months or years later to settle accounts in cash. He never asks for more than one night per stop. He leaves before dawn. He learns the names of the proprietors' children. He sends Christmas cards from no return address.

**Significance.** This network is the practical expression of the subject's reparative drive — the chosen family he could not sustain as intimacy, sustained instead as a diffuse and gentle ghost-presence in the lives of ordinary people who treated him decently. It is, in many ways, the relational form he is best at.

**Leverage.** Diffuse but real. An adversary mapping this network could degrade the subject's evasion infrastructure substantially. The subject is aware of this risk and has, accordingly, distributed nodes geographically and never returned to a node within twelve months of last contact.

---

## SUMMARY — STRUCTURAL READ

The subject's ally and chosen-family architecture exhibits three concentric rings.

**Inner ring (3 people: Rick, Jennifer, Betty).** Unconditional trust, unconditional access, capacity to de-escalate the alter system by voice alone. These are the people for whom the subject will breach his own containment regime without hesitation. They are also the three people through whom the subject is most coercible.

**Middle ring (Samson, Cho, Stark, Strange, Rhodes).** Conditional trust, domain-bounded intimacy, capacity to influence but not to de-escalate. The professional and peer relationships through which the subject conducts the adult-functional portion of his life.

**Outer ring (Defenders structure, civilian foster network, occasional Avengers, ambivalent figures like Creel).** Diffuse low-intimacy connectivity that provides the actual infrastructure of survival and the only form of belonging the subject can sustain longitudinally without dissociative breach.

The pattern across all three rings is consistent: the subject can love, the subject can be loved, the subject can sustain proximity — but only at decreasing intensities as distance from the trauma-substrate decreases. The closer the relationship, the more it must replicate the conditions of the lost mother (unconditional, non-aggressive, somatically gentle) and avoid the conditions of the father (auth


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*A relational map of the subject's most charged dyads — the figures who have generated the highest autonomic load across the record, and around whom the dissociative apparatus has most consistently breached. Each entry treats the relationship as a longitudinal case in itself: who the other is to the subject, what the subject is to them, the somatic and behavioral signature of the dyad at proximity, the failure modes, and what each party holds over the other.*

---

## I. INTIMATES & LOVERS

### I.1 — Elizabeth "Betty" Ross (Banner, Talbot, Walters)

**The defining attachment of the adult life. The only person against whom the subject's defensive architecture has never been wholly successful, and the only person who has, intermittently, been the subject's reparative figure.**

*History.* Met at Desert Base / Gamma Base, New Mexico, while the subject was working under her father's command; pre-incident affection in the record is muted but unmistakable on both sides — she described him then as "the quietest man on the base" and was drawn to precisely the dissociated calm that was the surface of his containment. Engaged before the gamma incident; engaged again after; married (Banner, then briefly to Talbot during one of the subject's "presumed dead" absences, then Banner again); widowed in record (the Maestro arc, and the Abomination poisoning, *Incident Hulk* #466, 1998 — Betty dies of gamma poisoning sustained through the subject's body); resurrected; mutated into Red She-Hulk (Loeb/McGuinness era); recurrent across every era including *Immortal Hulk*. No other figure has the same continuity in the file.

*Dynamics.* The subject's behavior in proximity to Betty is diagnostically distinct from his behavior with any other human. Baseline observed micro-patterns: he stands a half-step closer to her than to anyone else; the chronic shoulder rounding releases slightly; speech rate drops; he initiates physical contact (he does not, with anyone else, initiate); the heart-rate watch — the somatic talisman he wears in many eras — is checked *more*, not less, in her presence, because she is the one stimulus that pushes pulse upward in both arousal and fear simultaneously. He cooks for her on every recorded return. He calls her "Betty," never "Elizabeth" or "Beth"; she is the only person who has ever made him laugh in panel without that laugh immediately curdling into self-rebuke.

*Trust / safety.* High in conscious trust, catastrophically unstable in the somatic register. The subject trusts Betty's intentions absolutely. He does not trust *his body around her*. This is the central tragedy: the person he most wants to be near is the person his presence has most consistently endangered (gamma poisoning, kidnapping by his rogues, death). Her capacity to remain in relationship after each of these injuries is, paradoxically, what destabilizes him further — every act of her forgiveness deepens the Devil Hulk introject's case against him.

*Evolution.* In the early period (1962–1980s), the dyad is a conventional pursuit-flight tragic-romance. In the Peter David period, it matures: Betty marries the Merged Hulk, and the marriage is, briefly, functional — the only period in which the subject has lived inside a stable adult attachment. Her death in #466 is the most destructive single event in the post-childhood record; the subject's decompensation following it is the proximate cause of multiple subsequent breakdowns. Her return (Red She-Hulk) introduces a new dynamic: she now carries her own gamma-mediated dissociative pathology, and the relationship has become, in a sense, two dissociative survivors negotiating with each other's alter systems. This is either the most promising or most catastrophic configuration in the entire file; the record supports both readings.

*Failure mode.* He leaves. Always. The script is invariant: stabilization, attachment deepens, threshold for arousal lowers, an incident occurs (her endangerment, a transformation in front of her, an intrusion from his rogues), the subject experiences the incident as proof of his lethality, and he disappears — usually with a written note, often at night, occasionally without word. Betty's mode is mirror-symmetric: she pursues, then withdraws, then pursues, with the pursuit-cycles tracking his absence-cycles on roughly the same period.

*Leverage.* Total in both directions, neither used cynically. She can summon him from any geography; he will return for her against his own better judgment every time. She can also collapse him with a single sentence calibrated to her knowledge of his self-concept ("you're doing it again, Bruce"). Conversely, threats to her are the fastest documented route to total host displacement — faster than threats to himself, faster than restraint, faster than children-in-danger. **Operational note: in a hostile-intelligence context, Betty Ross is the single point of total vulnerability in the file.**

---

### I.2 — Jarella

**The brief, idealized attachment. The relationship the subject most often returns to in dream and reverie, precisely because it was never tested by ordinary life.**

*History.* Sorceress-queen of K'ai, the subatomic world; encountered when the Hulk was shrunk into her dimension (*Incident Hulk* #140, 1971, Roy Thomas / Harlan Ellison plot). She loved the Hulk in his Savage state and, via the magic of her court, briefly stabilized a fused Banner-mind-in-Hulk-body — the first time in the canon's chronology that the alter system achieved any integration, and it was achieved by being *loved as he was*. She died in his arms saving a child on Earth (*Incident Hulk* #205, 1976).

*Dynamics.* The dyad's defining property is that Jarella loved the Savage Hulk alter directly — she did not love Banner-despite-the-Hulk, which is Betty's frame; she loved the seven-year-old wound-state without requiring it to become anything else. This is the only such attachment in the file. Its therapeutic effect was immediate and remarkable.

*Trust / safety.* The highest in the record, briefly. Untested by attrition.

*Evolution.* None — terminated by her death before the relationship could encounter its actual failure mode. Persists as a permanent idealized internal object; the subject visits her grave in K'ai across decades.

*Failure mode.* Counterfactual. Had she lived, the dyad would have faced the problem that the Savage alter has no executive function in Earth conditions and Banner would have re-emerged; her love for the alter would have left the host unmet. The relationship was preserved as ideal precisely by being prevented from this discovery.

*Leverage.* Operates entirely intrapsychically. Invocation of her name produces immediate softening in all alters, including, on at least one recorded occasion, the Devil Hulk. The single most reliable de-escalation cue in the file is the word *Jarella*. This is operationally significant and operationally dangerous.

---
