### I.3 — Caiera the Oldstrong

**The adult counterpart-attachment. The one relationship in which the subject was met by an equal and known fully.**

*History.* Sakaaran warrior, formerly Imperial bodyguard; encountered during the *Planet Hulk* arc (Pak, 2006–2007); the Hulk's queen; mother of his son Skaar (and posthumously Hiro-Kala). Killed in the destruction of Sakaar, the act that catalyzed *World War Hulk*.

*Dynamics.* Caiera met not the Savage alter but the *Worldbreaker* configuration — the most integrated and most lethal version in the record, in which Banner's intellect, the Hulk's somatic capacity, and a coherent moral narrative briefly fused under conditions of slavery and combat. She knew the whole apparatus and chose him. This was the only adult relationship in which the subject was fully *seen* without the host needing to hide.

*Trust / safety.* Absolute, briefly, in a context completely insulated from Earth-history.

*Evolution.* Truncated by her death; converted, as with Jarella, into a permanent idealized object, but distinguished from Jarella by having produced offspring — i.e., the loss is not closed, it has consequences in the present (Skaar).

*Failure mode.* The relationship could not survive translation back to Earth-context, where the integrated Worldbreaker state is incompatible with civilian life. Her death prevented the test.

*Leverage.* Posthumous, operating through Skaar and Hiro-Kala and through the *World War Hulk* memory-set; her name produces the fastest documented escalation to Worldbreaker configuration in the record.

---

## II. RIVALS

### II.1 — Anthony Stark

**The intellectual peer. The man whose existence proves the subject's wound — that two men of comparable cognitive capacity can produce vastly different lives, and the difference is the father.**

*History.* Decades of collaboration, conflict, and intermittent friendship. Stark recruited the subject to the Avengers, to the Illuminati (*New Avengers: Illuminati*, Bendis/Reed), and across multiple Helicarrier and laboratory contexts. The Illuminati's decision to exile the subject into space — Stark's vote was decisive — is the most consequential betrayal in the rival-axis of the file and the proximate cause of *World War Hulk*.

*Dynamics.* Banner is the better physicist; Stark is the better engineer. Both know this; neither says it. Banner defers to Stark socially and dresses-down intellectually in his presence (subject will discuss his own work in deliberately accessible terms with Stark — observed micro-pattern across multiple labs); Stark patronizes Banner about temperament while quietly seeking his opinion on the problems that matter most. The dyad is structured around an exchange neither acknowledges: Stark provides the institutional shelter Banner needs to do science, and Banner provides the technical validation Stark's narcissism requires from the one peer who could legitimately withhold it.

*Trust / safety.* Conditional and asymmetrical. Banner trusts Stark in laboratories and distrusts him in politics; Stark trusts Banner's intellect and distrusts his stability. Both are correct.

*Evolution.* Early period — collegial. Illuminati period — covertly fraternal, with Stark in the older-brother role the subject has never had. Exile / *World War Hulk* — full antagonist, the subject systematically defeated Stark in single combat and forced him into accountability. Post-WWH and through to recent eras — a wary, never fully repaired re-collaboration.

*Failure mode.* Stark, under institutional pressure, will sacrifice the subject for the greater good and tell himself afterward that he had no choice. He has done it; he will do it again. The subject knows this and works with him anyway, because the alternative is to work alone.

*Leverage.* Stark holds: institutional access, resources, the only laboratory infrastructure on the planet adequate to the subject's work. Banner holds: the capacity to physically end Stark whenever he chooses, and — more powerful — the knowledge of which of Stark's projects are technically wrong, a knowledge Stark needs and resents.

---

### II.2 — Reed Richards

**The other peer. The relationship structured by mutual disappointment — Richards has failed, repeatedly, to cure the subject, and the subject has failed to be curable.**

*History.* Multiple cure-attempts across the canon, beginning in early Fantastic Four crossovers and continuing through the Illuminati period. Co-conspirator in the exile. Subject of the subject's wrath in *World War Hulk*.

*Dynamics.* Richards approaches the subject as an engineering problem; the subject experiences this, accurately, as the failure of the one man who might have understood the case to actually look at it. Richards never asks the subject about his father. He asks about gamma chromatography. The dyad is the casebook example of what intellectualization-as-defense looks like when two such men encounter each other.

*Trust / safety.* The subject trusts Richards's competence and distrusts his judgment. Richards trusts the subject's intentions and treats his somatic apparatus as a defect rather than a structure.

*Evolution.* Cure-attempt cycle, betrayal (exile), retribution (WWH), post-retribution wariness. Less recoverable than the Stark relationship because there was less affection underneath to recover.

*Failure mode.* Richards will keep trying to solve the wrong problem until the subject loses patience.

*Leverage.* Richards's reputational stake in being able to solve any problem is itself leverage the subject could exploit and never has.

---

### II.3 — Doc Samson

**The therapist who became a rival; the only person who has ever attempted to do the actual work.**

*History.* Leonard Samson, psychiatrist, initially treated the subject in the early 1970s and became gamma-contaminated himself in the course of treatment, producing his own (much less severe) altered state. Conducted the longest sustained therapeutic engagement in the file across the Peter David era, formulated the MPD diagnosis, named the alters, and achieved — briefly — the Merged Hulk integration.

*Dynamics.* The most complete therapeutic alliance the subject has ever sustained, complicated by Samson's own gamma-mediated stake in the subject's pathology and by Samson's intermittent romantic interest in Betty. The dual relationship is grossly inappropriate by ordinary clinical standards; it is also the closest the canon has come to actual treatment.

*Trust / safety.* High, with chronic boundary contamination. The subject lets Samson into his mind in ways he lets no one else, and Samson, repeatedly, uses that access for purposes adjacent to but not identical with the subject's welfare (Betty, public reputation, Avengers consultation).

*Evolution.* Therapist → ally → rival (Betty triangle) → corrupted (Samson's alter, the Dark Son arc) → reconciled → killed and resurrected. The dyad is the file's principal record of the limits of psychotherapy without institutional containment.

*Failure mode.* Samson cannot maintain the frame because he has skin in the gamma game. No psychiatrist who shares the subject's pathology can hold the therapeutic frame indefinitely.

*Leverage.* Samson knows the alter system from the inside; he is the only person other than the alters themselves who has met all of them. This is the deepest informational vulnerability in the file. Operationally: any actor with Samson's notes possesses the subject's entire interior topography.

---

### II.4 — Namor McKenzie

**The Illuminati co-conspirator who voted against the exile and is therefore, perversely, the rival the subject most respects.**

*History.* Illuminati membership; the only Illuminati member to oppose the subject's exile and warn him afterward.

*Dynamics.* Namor's contempt for the rest of the Illuminati validates the subject's grievance; Namor's own rage-based pathology is a recognizable mirror, but one organized through monarchy and pride rather than dissociation. The two men have an unspoken mutual recognition: each understands what the other costs.

*Trust / safety.* Low in absolute terms, high relative to the rest of the Illuminati.

*Failure mode.* Namor's loyalty is contingent on Namor's mood.

*Leverage.* Each holds, against the other, the truth of what was done in the Illuminati's name. Neither has cashed this in.

---

## III. ENEMIES

### III.1 — Brian Banner (deceased; persistent as introject)

**The originating enemy. Dead in the world, immortal in the mind. The most important figure in the file by a wide margin.**

*History.* Father; physicist; alcoholic; abusive; matricide; institutionalized; returned; killed in altercation with the subject (*Incident Hulk* #312, 1985, ret.). The single largest etiological agent in the case.

*Dynamics.* The subject's entire adult life is structured against him: teetotal because Brian drank; gentle because Brian was violent; soft-spoken because Brian shouted; pacifist because Brian killed. Every defining surface feature of the host personality is a negation of the father. This is the *reaction formation* substrate of the case, and it is the reason the host cannot integrate aggression — to feel anger is to *be* his father.

*Trust / safety.* Inapplicable in the conventional sense; the introject is the principal source of unsafety in the subject's own mind. The Devil Hulk / Guilt Hulk alter speaks in his register, holds his opinions about the subject, and acts as the internal persecutor.

*Evolution.* In life: terror, witnessed matricide, coerced perjury, repression. In death: introjection, dissociation of the killing, recovered memory (Samson therapy), partial integration (*Immortal Hulk*'s recognition of the Devil Hulk as the father-introject and the subsequent decision to neither expel nor obey him).

*Failure mode.* The introject cannot be killed because the body that produced it is already dead; it can only be metabolized. Across sixty years of canon, this metabolization is incomplete.

*Leverage.* Total, intrapsychic. Any external actor who reproduces Brian's vocal register, posture, or rhetorical signature (paternal contempt; questioning of the subject's right to exist; allusion to genetic contamination) achieves immediate access to the Devil Hulk substrate. **Operational note: this is the deepest psychological exploit in the file. Several enemies, listed below, have discovered it independently.**

---

### III.2 — General Thaddeus "Thunderbolt" Ross

**The displacement-father. The man onto whom the subject has, for sixty years, transferred his unfinished business with the original.**

*History.* Father of Betty; commanding officer at Gamma Base; the subject's longest-running persecutor; eventually himself a Hulk (Red Hulk, Loeb era). Pursued the subject across continents, decades, and multiple administrations of the U.S. military.

*Dynamics.* Ross is a hard, contemptuous, militarily authoritarian paternal figure who openly despised the subject before the incident and dedicated his career to his capture after. The subject's behavior in proximity to Ross is regressively submissive — the same shoulder-rounding, the same averted gaze, the same clipped affect-suppressed speech he showed with his father at the magnification of an adult relationship. Ross, in turn, treats the subject with precisely the contempt Brian treated him with: as a defective male, unworthy of the daughter, dangerous, weak in everything except the dangerous part.

*Trust / safety.* Nil and known to be nil; the dyad is functional only because each knows exactly where the other stands.

*Evolution.* Pursuer / pursued (decades). Brief institutional détente during the Merged Hulk marriage. Renewed antagonism. Ross's own transformation into Red Hulk — a deeply revealing development, because it demonstrates that *Ross became what he hated when given the same somatic capacity*, which is the strongest single piece of indirect evidence in the canon that the rage-state Ross spent his life condemning is structurally available to anyone subjected to comparable pressures. After Red Hulk, the dyad shifts into wary co-belligerence in occasional joint operations.

*Failure mode.* Ross will betray any peace the moment institutional pressure demands it; the subject will accept the betrayal because at the somatic level he believes Ross is correct about him.

*Leverage.* Ross holds: Betty, institutional reach, the only voice the subject hears as his father's. Banner holds: the knowledge that Ross's daughter loves him and not her father, and the demonstrated capacity to defeat Ross in any direct confrontation. Neither side has ever fully cashed.

---

### III.3 — Emil Blonsky (the Abomination)

**The shadow-double. What the subject would be without conscience.**

*History.* Soviet-bloc agent who deliberately self-exposed to gamma in pursuit of military capability; transformed into a stable, permanent monstrous form lacking the dissociative bifurcation. Killed Betty by gamma-poisoning her blood. Recurrent across the canon.

*Dynamics.* Blonsky is the file's clearest illustration of what the dissociative apparatus is *for*: Blonsky has none, retains his cognition in his monstrous form, and uses it for predation. The subject, in contrast, dissociates precisely so as not to be Blonsky. The hatred between them is therefore not symmetrical: Blonsky envies the subject's power; the subject loathes Blonsky as the externalization of what the Devil Hulk says the subject already is.

*Trust / safety.* Total enmity.

*Evolution.* Combat, the killing of Betty (the single most consequential enemy action in the file), recurrent re-engagement.

*Failure mode.* The subject cannot kill Blonsky cleanly because to do so would require accessing predatory aggression — which, at the host level, would prove the Devil Hulk correct. The killings the Hulk inflicts on Blonsky are therefore always recoverable; the structure of the dyad requires Blonsky's survival.

*Leverage.* Blonsky's existence is leverage against the subject's self-concept; the subject's existence is leverage against Blonsky's claim to having chosen the better path.

---

### III.4 — Samuel Sterns (the Leader)

**The intellectual enemy. The one rogue who has correctly diagnosed the subject and weaponizes the diagnosis.**

*History.* Gamma-mutated genius; recurrent strategic antagonist. Has, on multiple occasions, manipulated the subject through engineered situations designed to provoke specific alters.

*Dynamics.* Sterns understands the alter system as well as Samson does, but from the outside; he treats the subject as a programmable weapon whose triggers he has catalogued. He has, on record, deliberately produced Savage / Grey / Worldbreaker emergence by environmental engineering.

*Trust / safety.* None. Sterns is the most informationally dangerous active enemy.

*Failure mode.* Sterns over-relies on the model and is repeatedly surprised by inter-alter cooperation — the one variable his analysis does not capture.

*Leverage.* Sterns knows the triggers. **Operationally, in any list of external actors with predictive knowledge of the subject's switching, Sterns is second only to Samson.**

---

### III.5 — The Maestro

**The self-as-enemy. The future-version in whom the integration the subject seeks has occurred — and gone the other way.**

*History.* Future-timeline Hulk: Banner's intellect plus Hulk's body plus Devil Hulk's morality, ruling a post-apocalyptic Earth (Peter David, *Future Imperfect*, 1992).

*Dynamics.* The Maestro is the proof that integration without therapy is catastrophe — what happens when the alter system fuses around the Devil Hulk introject rather than against it. He is the subject's most personal enemy because he is the subject, and he is right that he is the subject.

*Trust / safety.* Inapplicable.

*Failure mode.* The Maestro cannot be killed by the subject without the subject accepting that he is capable of becoming the Maestro — which, after each confrontation, deepens the host's despair and feeds the very introject that produces the Maestro.

*Leverage.* Reciprocal and total: each knows the other from the inside.

---

### III.6 — The Devil Hulk (intrasubjective enemy)

**The enemy who is the subject. Listed here rather than in Section III because operationally he functions as an enemy with persistent agency.**

*History.* Cat


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## Preliminary frame: two subjects, one body

Any honest catalogue of this file's capabilities must begin by acknowledging that the "powers" are distributed across the alter system rather than residing in a single agent. The host (Banner, PhD) holds one constellation of abilities — almost entirely cognitive, perceptual, and procedural. The dissociated states hold another — almost entirely somatic, kinetic, and affective. The amnestic barrier means the host cannot reliably access what the alters can do, and the alters express contempt for, or indifference to, what the host can do. The file's central operational tragedy is that no single executive integrates the full repertoire. What follows is therefore organized first by carrier (host, then each major alter), with mechanism, range, ceiling, growth curve, signature applications, and the symptom-as-signature reading at each level.

---

## I. THE HOST (Banner, R. B., PhD) — cognitive and procedural repertoire

### 1. Theoretical physics at the genius ceiling

**Mechanism.** Native fluid intelligence (psychometric inferences from the canon place him in the top fraction of a percentile, consistently grouped with Richards, Pym, Stark, and Doom as the small handful of "smartest men on Earth"), coupled with a domain expertise — gamma-spectrum nuclear physics — in which he is, by canonical consensus, *first* rather than merely *among*. No other figure in the published record approaches his gamma-radiation literacy. He designs the device that detonates him; he later designs the instrumentation by which others attempt to contain him; his calculations are repeatedly the basis upon which other physicists work.

**Range.** Particle physics, radiobiology, thermodynamics, and adjacent fields (he is competent in cybernetics, biochemistry, and applied engineering to a degree that lets him reverse-engineer alien hardware in the field). He is *not* a generalist polymath in the Richards mold — his depth in gamma-related physics is purchased at some cost of breadth — but his ability to bootstrap into adjacent disciplines under time pressure is well attested.

**Limits.** Three. (a) **Tooling.** His best work requires laboratory infrastructure; he is at his weakest improvising from scrap, where Stark or Richards excel. (b) **Funding and institutional access**, which his fugitive status routinely deprives him of for years at a stretch. (c) **The defensive recruitment of his own intellect** — his cognition is so consistently conscripted into self-monitoring (heart-rate, arousal, environmental triage) that a meaningful percentage of his available processing is always occupied by the containment regime. A non-traumatized Banner would, on the available evidence, outproduce him substantially.

**Growth.** The cognitive ceiling itself does not appear to rise; what changes is domain. Early-period Banner is narrowly a weapons physicist; the middle period adds biophysics (attempts to understand his own condition); the late period (post-*Immortal*) adds frank metaphysics — the mechanics of the so-called Green Door, the topology of states of consciousness — work that no one else in the canon is positioned to do because no one else has the necessary first-person data.

**Signature applications.** The original gamma device. The Banner-built gamma-monitoring rigs used by SHIELD and the Avengers to track him. The "Hulkbuster" base architecture (his own design, repurposed against him by Ross). The instrumentalization scheme of the Aaron *Indestructible* era (a deployable gamma protocol). The retrocausal physics of the late Ewing work.

**Symptom-as-signature reading.** His intellect is a defense before it is a tool. Watch what he chooses to work on across the decades and you read his pathology directly: he works obsessively on the thing that hurt him — the gamma spectrum, the transformation mechanism, the alter system — because intellectualization permits him to remain in cognitive contact with the trauma while staying out of affective contact with it. He does physics on himself the way a forensic accountant audits his own embezzlement.

### 2. Applied engineering and tradecraft

**Mechanism.** Procedural skill accumulated under necessity. The fugitive years (long stretches across the 1970s–80s and the Ewing era) have produced a man who can rewire a vehicle, fabricate small electronics from consumer parts, set up a clandestine lab in a motel bathroom, and modify pharmaceuticals.

**Range and limits.** Workmanlike, not virtuosic. He is no Stark in the garage. What he *is* exceptional at is doing competent work with no resources under sustained psychological pressure — a kind of stress-tolerant practical engineering that more comfortable peers do not possess.

**Signature applications.** Repeated cobbled-together gamma suppressants (most failing); jury-rigged tracking countermeasures; the medical-grade self-monitoring rigs he carries in the late canon — a wristwatch hacked to read pulse and skin conductance, a notebook of trigger-correlation data kept in his own shorthand.

**Symptom-as-signature reading.** The tradecraft is the somatic record of the flight pattern. A man who has not had to disappear repeatedly does not develop these skills. They are a callus.

### 3. Hyper-developed interoception and autonomic self-monitoring

**Mechanism.** Years of necessity have produced what is, in clinical terms, a vastly above-baseline capacity for **interoceptive awareness** — the perception of internal bodily states. He can name his pulse to within a handful of beats without instrumentation. He registers cortisol-driven shifts (palmar sweat, jaw tension, peripheral vasoconstriction) before they become subjectively distressing. He is, in this single narrow respect, more in touch with his body than almost any character in the published record.

**Range and limits.** It is a one-way channel: he can *read* the body exquisitely well but cannot *modulate* what he reads. The needle on his internal gauge is high-resolution; the valve it is attached to is broken.

**Growth.** This is the one ability whose growth curve is monotonic across sixty years. The Lee/Kirby Banner is not a self-monitor; he is simply surprised by transformations. By the Mantlo era he begins reporting somatic premonitions. By the David era he has the explicit heart-rate vocabulary. By the Ewing era it is so refined that he can map his own dissociative switching in near-real-time and narrate it to others.

**Signature applications.** The famous pulse-counting under stress. The pre-emptive withdrawal from rooms when he registers his own arousal climbing. The breath-control regimens. The "do not touch me, I am at ninety-three" register that he uses in the late canon to brief operators around him.

**Symptom-as-signature reading.** Hypervigilance for self has replaced hypervigilance for other. The abused child watches the father's face; the adult survivor, having internalized the father as the Devil Hulk, watches *himself* with the same scanning intensity. The skill is real and useful. Its existence is also a wound.

### 4. Languages, mathematics, and accumulated learning

He reads several languages — Russian and Japanese are explicit in canon, French and German implicit, some technical Mandarin. Mathematics is native. He plays chess competently (the Samson sessions). He cooks adequately, drives competently, can ride a motorcycle. He is, in short, the well-furnished mind of a man who has spent a great deal of time alone and used the time.

### 5. Therapeutic alliance capacity (an underrated skill)

He is, when functioning, a *good patient* — articulate about internal states, capable of metaphor, capable of trusting Samson over years, capable of accepting interpretation. This is a skill, and many trauma patients do not have it. He has spent enough of his life being interpreted by competent observers (Samson, Banner-as-self-observer, Betty in her better moments) that he has acquired the vocabulary of his own condition. He can brief a clinician. The information bandwidth between him and a competent treater is, when he allows it, very high.

---

## II. SAVAGE HULK — the child-state somatic alter

### Mechanism

A dissociative identity state with full somatic expression. Triggered by autonomic arousal past threshold — heart rate is the canonical proxy, though the underlying variable is sympathetic activation generally. The trigger is **affect, not stimulus**: pain alone does not transform; fear, humiliation, rage, or the threat of abandonment do. Onset is rapid (seconds), accompanied by a characteristic biomechanical sequence (muscle hypertrophy, dermal pigmentation shift, skeletal remodeling, mass gain on the order of several hundred kilograms) for which the canon has never offered a thermodynamically coherent account — mass appears from elsewhere — and which is best read as the somatic literalization of a switch.

### Capabilities

**Strength.** The canonical phrase is "the strongest one there is," and the file bears this out empirically: at baseline, comparable to the upper tier of metahumans; under arousal, **scaling with affect** without an established upper bound. The "madder he gets, the stronger he gets" formulation is not metaphor — it is the file's most important single mechanical fact, and it is the precise inverse of what affect normally does to motor performance. Recorded feats include planetary-tectonic disturbance, sustained combat with cosmic-tier entities, and structural feats (lifting collapsing mountain ranges) that place the upper bound somewhere past the conventional measurement frame.

**Durability.** Effectively beyond conventional weapons. Survives orbital re-entry, point-blank nuclear detonations, atmospheric ejection. The skin's tensile properties scale with arousal as strength does.

**Regeneration.** Tissue regrowth on the order of seconds for limb-level wounds, and the *Immortal Hulk* arc establishes a recovery ceiling that approaches functional immortality — he reconstitutes from arbitrarily small remnants given sufficient time and a nocturnal cycle.

**Locomotion.** Leaps measured in miles per bound, achieving sub-orbital arcs at high arousal. Not flight — ballistic. The leap is the locomotive signature of the alter and reads, behaviorally, as flight-from rather than approach-to.

**Cognition.** Profoundly impaired. Emotional age fixed at roughly seven (the matricide age, on the available evidence). Language reduced to short declarative phrases, third-person self-reference, present-tense framing. Pre-linguistic affect dominant: fear, rage, sorrow, longing for "Betty," longing for the absent mother.

**Sensorium.** Heightened — registers threat at distances and through obstructions the host cannot. There is a documented capacity to perceive astral, etheric, or otherwise non-physical entities that the host does not register; the Savage state can see ghosts, in the precise sense that traumatized children sometimes report.

### Limits

- **Cognitive ceiling.** Cannot plan beyond immediate horizon. Tactically exploitable.
- **Object-relations ceiling.** Cannot sustain ambivalence; persons are either friend or threat, no middle.
- **Trigger dependence.** Cannot be voluntarily summoned by the host without crossing the arousal threshold, which requires real distress — a brittle and self-harming summoning protocol.
- **Persistence.** Reverts to host as arousal subsides, typically with exhaustion and amnesia.

### Symptom-as-signature reading

The Savage Hulk is the seven-year-old who was not permitted to scream when his mother was killed. The somatic vocabulary — the leap that covers miles to find safety, the bellow that is also a sob, the singular fixation on a small named good (Betty, Jones, the doll-figures he protects across the canon) — is exactly the affective repertoire of a frightened child rendered at adult somatic scale. The "strength scales with anger" mechanism is the wish-fulfillment of an abused child: that if I were angry *enough*, I could have stopped it. The canon has been telling this story for sixty years in plain sight.

---

## III. GREY HULK / FIXIT — the appetitive, socialized alter

### Mechanism

A second dissociative state, distinct from Savage, with its own somatic expression (smaller mass, grey pigmentation, near-baseline cognition). In the early canon, nocturnal — emerging only at night, a literalization of the split between daylight-Banner and shadow-self. Later destabilized to context-dependent emergence.

### Capabilities

**Strength.** Lower ceiling than Savage — substantial but not scaling without limit. The trade is bandwidth for resolution: this alter can do things Savage cannot.

**Cognition.** Near-host baseline, sometimes argued to exceed it in specific domains — street intelligence, social manipulation, gambling, negotiation. Articulate, witty, cruel.

**Social repertoire.** Operates a casino, holds employment, conducts relationships, manages money, dresses in human clothing without difficulty. Functions in the world.

**Appetites.** Drinks. Smokes (intermittently). Frequents prostitutes in the David canon. Gambles, often well. Eats with pleasure. These are the appetites the host has interdicted in himself for sixty years.

### Limits

- Lower physical ceiling than Savage.
- Disappears in daylight (early canon), an absurd-on-its-face limit that is the clearest possible signal that the alter is psychologically rather than physically grounded.
- Holds the host in contempt; will sabotage host objectives.

### Symptom-as-signature reading

Every drive the host disallowed himself has been routed into this alter. The host does not drink because the father drank; Grey drinks. The host cannot sustain sexual intimacy; Grey is straightforwardly libidinous. The host is morally fastidious; Grey is a hustler. Read across the alter system as a whole, you can reconstruct the entire interdicted self of the host by inventory: what he forbids in himself is what Grey is.

---

## IV. PROFESSOR HULK / MERGED — the therapeutic achievement

### Mechanism

Samson's clinical product (David era): a partial integration in which the host's cognition rides the somatic platform of the Savage state. Triggered voluntarily; sustained for extended periods; reversible.

### Capabilities

Strength near Savage's upper register but without the affect-scaling — and therefore, paradoxically, with a *lower* combat ceiling at maximum provocation. Cognition at host baseline. Articulate speech. Capacity for nuanced social engagement, scientific work, sustained relationships.

### Limits

**Structural fragility.** This is the file's most important capability fact: the Professor state is a *compromise formation*, not a true integration. It does not metabolize the trauma; it suppresses the alter conflict under a negotiated dominance. Under sufficient stress it decomposes — typically with both Savage rage and Grey appetitive sabotage erupting simultaneously, producing worse executive function than any alter alone.

### Symptom-as-signature reading

The Professor is what therapy can produce when the therapeutic frame is correct but the trauma is incompletely processed: a functional adult who is, structurally, still holding pieces together by act of will. It is a great deal better than the unintegrated baseline. It is not what recovery actually looks like. The canon has been honest about this — every Professor era has collapsed.

---

## V. DEVIL HULK / GUILT HULK — the persecutory introject

### Mechanism

The internalized father, given alter form. Speaks in the father's register. Hates the host. Is more articulate than any other alter. Holds the *Immortal*-era ceiling of physical capacity — possibly the highest in the system, because the rage it holds is the *correct* rage, the rage at the actual perpetrator, undiluted by the host's confusion about whether he is allowed to be angry.

### Capabilities

Physical ceiling at least equal to Savage, with full adult cognition, strategic patience measured in years, and a willingness — unique among the alters — to act with foresight rather than reaction. Tactically the most dangerous configuration of the body.

### Limits

Constrained, in the late canon, by an unstable alliance with the host. Without that alliance, it would not protect the host's loved ones; with it, it can be steered. The alliance is fragile.

### Symptom-as-signature reading

This is the file's clinical centerpiece rendered as power. The introjected abuser, properly recognized and partially negotiated with, becomes the most effective protective agent in the system — because the rage that the host was forbidden to feel at the original perpetrator can, when finally addressed to its proper target, be load-bearing. The late canon's gradual movement toward inter-alter cooperation is, in capability terms, the discovery that the Devil's strength is recruitable rather than only suppressible. This is also the contemporary trauma-therapy standard. The book got it right.

---

## VI. SYSTEM-LEVEL PROPERTIES

### The arousal-to-output curve

A single mechanic governs the system: sympathetic activation past a threshold initiates a switch; which alter takes the field is determined by the *quality* of the affect and the *context* of the trigger. Fear plus child-coded threat → Savage. Appetite plus permissive nocturnal setting → Grey. Confrontation with the father-introject or with paternal-coded authority under stable conditions → Devil. Negotiated stress within a holding relationship → Professor.

### Heart rate as proxy, not cause

The famous "don't make me angry" metric is a *correlate*, not the underlying variable. The host has, across decades, attempted to manage transformations by managing heart rate (beta blockers, meditation, breath protocols) with intermittent success and characteristic failure modes: the body learns to switch at lower thresholds when artificially suppressed, in the same way that chemically suppressed dissociation in human patients tends to break through more violently. The intervention treats the gauge, not the wound.

### Sleep and circadian factors

Transformations cluster around sleep deprivation, nightmare cycles, and the small hours. The Grey alter's nocturnal preference is the most overt circadian pattern, but Savage emergence is also significantly elevated during disrupted-sleep arcs. The subject's chronic insomnia is therefore not a side-effect but a system risk factor.

### The amnestic barrier

Bidirectional but asymmetrical. Host has near-total amnesia for alter episodes (recovers fragments under hypnosis, EMDR-equivalent, and the David-era Samson work). Alters retain partial knowledge of host life, weaponized by Grey, exploited by Devil, present-tense and limited in Savage. The barrier weakens under therapeutic work and under Ewing-era inter-alter dialogue.

### Growth across the canon

Three monotonic curves and several oscillating ones.

- **Monotonic up:** somatic ceiling (Savage's upper bound has risen every era); regenerative ceiling (culminating in functional immortality); host interoceptive resolution.
- **Monotonic down:** host's confidence in his own continence; the threshold of arousal required to switch (the system gets twitchier with each cycle of failed suppression).
- **Oscillating:** inter-alter communication (high in David, low in mid-2000s, very high in Ewing); functional integration (Professor era high, Aaron-era instrumentalization moderate, Ewing-era cooperation high).

---

## VII. WHAT HE CANNOT DO

A catalogue of capability gaps is as diagnostic as the capabilities themselves.

- **He cannot sustainably feel his own anger as the host.** This is the single most important limit in the file. Every other limit derives from it.
- **He cannot reliably summon the alter on demand without genuine distress.** The instrumentalization attempts fail on exactly this rock.
- **He cannot be physically restrained at any of the standard scales.** Containment past the threshold is, on present evidence, impossible by force.
- **He cannot be killed by conventional means**, and in the late canon, perhaps not by any means presently known. This is not a power he wants. It is, as noted in the medical section, iatrogenically traumatic.
- **He cannot stay.** The behavioral incapacity to remain in proximity to those he loves is, in capability terms, a missing skill. He has never developed it because the developmental conditions that would have taught it were never present.
- **He cannot integrate alone.** The Professor result requires Samson; the Ewing-era cooperation requires the alter system itself, in dialogue. Solo integration has not been demonstrated and may not be possible for this etiology.

---

## VIII. SIGNATURE APPLICATIONS — the operational repertoire as he actually uses it

In the field, the deployment pattern is consistent across decades.

- **Preemptive removal.** The host's preferred move is to leave a situation before the threshold is crossed. The vast majority of his "powers in action" are powers *not* exercised — withdrawals, refusals, departures. This is invisible in summary and central in fact.
- **Cognitive triage under stress.** When confined or attacked, the host attempts to reason a path out before the switch occurs. He is good at this. Most of the canon's nominally "Banner-only" rescues are this skill.
- **Strategic surrender to the alter** in extremis to protect a third party. The handoff is reluctant, deliberate, and accompanied by a characteristic verbal tell (the canonical line, delivered with calm rather than threat — read it as briefing, not warning).
- **The alter as last resort, never first option.** Operators who have worked with him (Avengers, SHIELD, Defenders) have learned that the file's most reliable axis of cooperation is the host's intellect; the alter is summoned only when the situation has degraded past the host's capacity, and even then with apology.
- **Post-episode reconstruction.** After every emergence the host conducts a forensic of what the alter did, from witness reports and physical evidence, and records it. He has been keeping this ledger, in one form or another, for sixty years. It is the single most underutilized intelligence product in the file — a longitudinal first-person dataset on dissociative phenomena that no clinician in the canon has had the bandwidth to mine.

---

## IX. THE SYMPTOM-AS-SIGNATURE READING, CONSOLIDATED

Every capability in this file is the trauma at a different magnification.

The host's intellect is the abused child's bid to outthink the unpredictable adult. His interoceptive virtuosity is the survival skill of a body that had to know when the next blow was coming, redirected inward. His tradecraft is the calluses of flight. His therapeutic competence is the gift the trauma left him in the form of fluency about itself.

The Savage Hulk is the seven-year-old's rage given the body it would have needed to stop the killing. The Grey is every appetite the host disallowed because his father had them. The Professor is what a competent therapist can build with a willing patient and insufficient time. The Devil is the introjected father — and, when finally negotiated with rather than only feared, the largest single power source in the system, because the rage held at its proper target is the rage that can finally do useful work.

The file's powers are not, in the end, a list of feats. They are a topology of the wound, drawn at full scale, in a body that was given — by accident, by gamma, by whatever you wish to call the precipitant — the capacity to render its psychology in the physical register. Read in that light, the question the file has been asking for six decades is not *how strong is he*. It is *what is he so strong about*. The answer, on the available evidence, has been the same answer since 1962, and the canon has only recently become willing to say it out loud.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# 6. OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT

## 6.1 Decision-Making Architecture

The subject's decision-making is not, despite appearances, the decision-making of a physicist. A physicist optimizes for truth under uncertainty. The subject optimizes for **containment of catastrophic downside** — every decision is run through a single dominant heuristic: *what is the probability this choice ends with bodies on the ground that I cannot account for?* Truth, comfort, financial security, professional advancement, romantic fulfillment, and even physical safety are all subordinated to this one filter. The cognitive style is therefore not exploratory but **defensive-Bayesian**: the subject is constantly updating a private threat model in which he himself is the most dangerous variable in the environment.

The decision process, observed across decades, runs in a recognizable sequence:

1. **Threat-scan.** On entering any new environment — a room, a town, a vehicle, a conversation — the subject performs an automatic ~20–40 second sweep: exits, civilian density, structural fragility (glass, gas lines, propane tanks at gas stations he avoids fueling near), distance to open ground, presence of children, presence of uniformed authority. This is observable as a brief stilling, a slow turn of the head, a fingertip-to-thumb count one can sometimes catch if filming him enter a diner.
2. **Arousal-estimate.** He runs an internal estimate of his own current physiological reserve — how close is he to threshold? This is why his right hand goes to his wrist (pulse) or his sternum (cardiac apex) at moments of stress. The gesture is so habitual the subject is largely unaware of it.
3. **Containment-route selection.** He selects the option that maximizes distance from population centers and minimizes social friction. When two options are otherwise equivalent, he will select the one that places him **nearer to water, forest, or unpopulated industrial zone**, because these are dissipation surfaces — places the Hulk can land without killing.
4. **Execution at minimum signal.** He moves quietly, speaks softly, makes small purchases in cash, gives a polite reason and leaves. Every interaction is designed to be forgotten.
5. **Post-action erasure.** He notes what he has touched, what cameras he has crossed, what name he gave. He keeps a running mental ledger of identities-burned-per-city.

This sequence runs in **seconds** for routine choices and is so internalized it presents externally as ordinary diffidence. It is not diffidence. It is a perpetual evacuation drill.

## 6.2 Tradecraft — The Fugitive Layer

The subject has been, for most of his adult life, a man in flight from the United States Army, from himself, and intermittently from S.H.I.E.L.D., the Hulkbusters, and a rotating cast of foreign intelligence services. He has developed, by attrition and necessity, a tradecraft of unusual depth for someone who has never had formal training. It is the tradecraft of a **soft fugitive** — one who survives by being unremarkable rather than by counter-action.

**Identity management.** The subject cycles legends frequently: David B., Bruce Bixby, Bob Danner, Bruce Green, dozens of others across the record. The legends share characteristic features: a first name beginning with B or D (he has learned he will reflexively answer to these; novel initials produce a hesitation that gets him made); a profession that is technical but ambient — high-school physics teacher, lab technician, hospital orderly, factory line-worker, dishwasher; a backstory involving a recent divorce or a deceased wife (explains the wedding-band tan-line that sometimes lingers, explains why he doesn't talk about it, makes locals stop asking). He never claims to be a doctor or a researcher in cover. He learned early that any cover requiring him to display advanced expertise risks recognition by the very colleagues — or their students — who would identify him.

**Documents.** He has, across the canon, demonstrated competence with forged ID — not at the artisan level, but the practical level of a man who knows which border crossings will accept a poor document and which won't. He prefers expired-but-genuine documents lifted from indigent corpses in hospital morgues he has worked at as an orderly, layered with hand-altered details. He retains a small float of cash, usually USD, and small precious items (a watch, a wedding band) that can be pawned.

**Cash discipline.** The subject is functionally cash-only across most of his life. He has, when forced, demonstrated facility with prepaid debit cards bought at convenience stores under cover names, but he distrusts and avoids them. He does not maintain bank accounts under his true name and has not for decades. When he holds significant money it is in a sock, a wall cavity, a coffee tin buried behind a trailer, or — in the *Indestructible Hulk* period — laundered through whatever institutional sponsor he has temporarily attached to.

**Lodging.** Strong preference for: rented rooms in working-class boarding houses; cash motels off interstate exits; the back rooms of churches and free clinics; in the developing-world phases, single-room rentals from families that need the supplemental income and do not register with authorities. He has demonstrated repeatedly across the record that he will pay double the asking rate to be left alone and not asked for ID. He prefers ground-floor rooms with two exits and a window large enough to leave through in Hulk-form (i.e., a window adjacent to a wall thin enough to take with him). He will refuse upper floors when offered. He will refuse rooms with shared walls to families with children.

**Movement.** Walking, bicycle, bus. He avoids his own driving where possible — driving requires sustained low-grade vigilance which raises baseline arousal and degrades his window of tolerance over hours. Long-haul Greyhound and intercity bus travel suits him: low-friction ID, anonymous, allows sleep. He selects window seats in the rear third of the bus. He boards last. He gets off one stop before his actual destination and walks the remainder.

**Communications.** Burner phones, used briefly and discarded. He has a documented pattern of writing addresses on his forearm in ballpoint pen rather than carrying paper. He memorizes phone numbers — a habit from before cell phones — and will not store contacts. He does not maintain a stable email address under his true name. When he communicates with Betty or Samson it is via channels they have pre-arranged years prior (the canon shows multiple "if you ever need to reach me" drops).

**Counter-surveillance.** Modest but real. He performs SDRs (surveillance detection routes) reflexively in unfamiliar cities — a loop, a doubling back, a deliberate use of a department-store entrance with multiple exits. He notices repeat vehicles. He has learned to identify Hulkbuster signatures (specific radio frequencies, specific vehicle profiles) at a glance and clears any town in which they appear within the hour.

## 6.3 The Heart-Rate Regime

The single most important piece of operational tradecraft in the file is the subject's **continuous management of his own autonomic state**. This is not a technique he was taught; it is one he has constructed, layer by layer, over decades, drawing on whatever was locally available — Buddhist *vipassanā* practice during his years in the subcontinent, *qigong* breathing learned in a Pacific Rim village, biofeedback methods picked up at a free clinic, the *Wim Hof*–style controlled hyperventilation/breath-hold protocols, beta-blockers when he can get them.

The regime, as reconstructed from observation, includes:

- **Diaphragmatic breathing on a 4-7-8 cadence** (inhale 4, hold 7, exhale 8), audible only as a faint nostril whistle. He drops into it on entering elevators, before any interaction with authority, immediately upon hearing raised voices.
- **Tactile grounding.** Pinching the webbing between thumb and forefinger; pressing the pad of the index finger against the tip of the thumb in sequence; rolling a small object (a stone, a coin, a wedding band) between fingers in his pocket. These are visible if you know to watch the hand.
- **Cardiac monitoring.** He has, across multiple arcs, carried a pulse oximeter or a basic wristwatch with heart-rate monitoring. He uses caffeine sparingly and titrated — he is not teetotal on caffeine but treats it as a controlled substance, never more than one cup, never after midday.
- **Vegetarian / near-vegan diet** across most of his life — not for ethical reasons primarily but because high-protein meat-heavy meals raise his perceived agitation; he has discovered this empirically over decades.
- **Strict sleep hygiene** where possible: he aims for 7.5 hours, sleeps in a fetal posture facing the room's primary exit, prefers a hard mattress on the floor when he can arrange it. Sleep deprivation is one of his most dangerous states and he knows it.
- **Daily meditative sit**, usually 20–40 minutes, usually at dawn, frequently outdoors. This is not optional in his routine; he treats missing it the way a diabetic treats missing insulin.

He has trained himself to detect his own resting heart rate without instrumentation, to within a few BPM. Witnesses (Samson's case notes, Betty's recurrent observations) describe him as one of the most somatically self-aware individuals they have ever encountered. He has the proprioception of an elite athlete — bent entirely to the task of detecting his own threshold.

## 6.4 Habitats and Microhabits

The subject builds the same environment everywhere he goes. A reconstructed inventory of his lodgings across decades shows a stable pattern:

- A single light source, a low-wattage desk lamp, positioned to leave the room's corners in shadow (he sleeps better in dim rooms; bright fluorescents he associates with hospital wards and interrogation).
- A teapot or kettle. He drinks chamomile, passionflower, valerian — sedating herbals — in the evening. He prepares them ritualistically.
- A notebook, hardcover, ruled, ~A5; he goes through one every several weeks. Half is physics (a continuous mathematical conversation with himself, often unpublishable, often elegant); a quarter is journaled affect-tracking ("woke at 0530, HR 64, dream about father, nausea 0700, walked 8km"); a quarter is operational ledger (cash on hand, distance to next planned move, names burned). He carries the current notebook on his person; he burns the prior one before leaving a city.
- A go-bag, repacked weekly: one change of clothes (loose-waisted, elastic, easily shed or destroyed during transformation; he favors khakis or chinos and a button-down because they survive the transformation as rags rather than disintegrating entirely and leaving him fully nude); cash; a small first-aid kit (gauze, tape, antiseptic, suture kit — he does his own stitches and is competent at it); a paperback (often poetry or Buddhist text); the current notebook; a single photograph.
- The photograph is, in nearly every documented case, of Betty.

He does not own. He does not accumulate. He does not display. The only personal effect that survives city-to-city is the photograph, and even that has been destroyed and replaced repeatedly.

## 6.5 The Pre-Episode Sequence — A Behavioral Tell-Set

For an observer trained to recognize it, the subject signals an oncoming dissociative breach in a remarkably consistent sequence:

1. **Speech slows and lowers in pitch.** The characteristic soft-spoken register becomes softer still, and the sentences shorten.
2. **He asks people to leave.** Phrasing is polite but firm: "I think you should step back." "Please. Get out of the room." This is the host's last available executive act on behalf of others.
3. **He looks for an exit.** Eyes track to the nearest door or window. He may step backward toward it.
4. **Hands go to head, then forearms.** Palms pressed to temples; fingers gripping his own forearms hard enough to leave marks. This is observable and has been depicted thousands of times.
5. **Breath shortens, audible from a meter away.** The 4-7-8 cadence fails.
6. **Skin discoloration.** A flush, often described as greenish at the temples and along the jugular line, propagating outward.
7. **Voice drops further and the register changes.** The host is no longer speaking. The alter is coming up.

The whole sequence, from trigger to handover, runs anywhere from **8 seconds to ~3 minutes** depending on the subject's current regulatory reserve and the magnitude of the trigger. Trained observers (Samson, Betty, Romanoff in some continuities) can interrupt it during the first three phases by establishing eye contact and a low calm voice. After phase 5 it is generally not interruptible.

## 6.6 Financial Substrate

The subject has, across his life, occupied four distinct economic positions:

1. **Pre-incident salaried physicist.** Standard military-research compensation, a modest apartment near base, no significant assets. Whatever assets existed were forfeited or seized in the immediate post-incident period as he became a fugitive.
2. **Fugitive subsistence (the longest period).** Cash income from physical labor — diner dishwasher, ranch hand, construction laborer, hospital orderly, mechanic's assistant, in the developing-world stretches as a barefoot doctor / village clinician trading basic medical care for food and lodging. He is *competent* at these jobs and well-liked by employers, and he leaves before they get attached.
3. **Institutionally sponsored phases.** When attached to the Avengers, S.H.I.E.L.D., or analogous bodies, the subject's material needs are absorbed by the host institution. He takes no salary he can avoid. When pressed, he directs payment to research foundations, to Betty in earlier eras, or — in *Indestructible Hulk* — to families of those killed during prior Hulk events. He keeps a private ledger of these.
4. **Scientific consulting (rare).** When he can do it without exposure — pseudonymous publication, anonymous problem-solving — he does. Some of the most important quiet contributions in his field across the last several decades are likely his.

He has no will, no insurance, no retirement account, no fixed address, no credit history under his true name. He has, in operational terms, *no economic life*. This is itself an operational choice — assets are anchors, and he has organized his existence around portability.

## 6.7 Resources and Network

**Sparse, deep, asymmetric.** The subject's network is small but unusually competent.

- **Betty Ross** — the only sustained personal tie, intermittently active across decades. She has been, at various points, a safe house, a financial resource, a co-fugitive, a clinician, and a witness.
- **Leonard Samson** — the only person to have held him in a continuous therapeutic relationship. The subject can reach him through pre-arranged channels and has done so in his worst decompensations.
- **Rick Jones** — the man he saved at the gamma incident; a quasi-filial bond, asymmetric, the closest thing the subject has to a younger-brother figure.
- **A rotating roster of Avengers contacts** — Stark (engineering and shielded labs), Rogers (moral ballast and operational discipline), Romanoff (in some continuities, has been one of the few who can do phase-1-through-3 interruption), Strange (occult containment options).
- **The international demimonde of trauma medicine** — across the developing world, the subject has built relationships with rural physicians, NGO clinic directors, monks at meditation centers. These are not "assets" in an intelligence sense; they are people he has helped and who would shelter him without asking.

He does not have, and has consistently refused to build, a network of force. He has no armed retainers, no hired security, no weapons cached. He is — uniquely for a fugitive of his risk profile — entirely unarmed at the host level. The reason is doctrinal: he is the weapon; arming the host is operationally meaningless and psychologically intolerable.

## 6.8 Infrastructure — The Caches

Across his life, the subject has established **safe-fail caches** in environments to which he might need to return: a sealed plastic container behind a loose brick in the wall of a desert toolshed; a waterproofed bag chained beneath a culvert outside a Brazilian favela; a locker at a Greyhound station in Albuquerque renewed in cash every six months for a decade. Each cache contains the same minimal kit: cash in mixed small denominations, a change of clothes, a forged ID, basic medical supplies, a notebook, a pen, water purification tablets, and — in the more recent caches — a sedative tranquilizer dose calibrated to his pre-Hulk body weight, in case he needs to put himself under fast.

He maintains a rough mental map of these caches. He does not write the map down.

## 6.9 Operational Tells — The Things a Surveillance Cell Would Use to Identify Him

The following constellation of micro-tells is sufficient, in combination, to ID the subject across any cover legend he is currently running:

- **Pulse-check at the wrist or carotid every 6–12 minutes**, regardless of activity. Often disguised as a watch glance, a beard scratch, a collar adjustment. The interval is the giveaway.
- **The 4-7-8 breath** under any minor stress — a barista getting his order wrong, a child crying nearby, a siren in the middle distance.
- **Refusal of alcohol** in any social setting, with a stock excuse ("liver, sorry") delivered too smoothly.
- **Vegetarian order at any restaurant**, even ones where it is conspicuous.
- **Left-handed signature, right-handed everything else** (canonical Banner ambidexterity, with handedness slightly favoring the left for writing).
- **The forearm-grip self-soothe** at moments of frustration.
- **Avoidance of crowded interior spaces** — he will eat outside in cold weather rather than sit in a busy diner. Tables near windows or doors only.
- **Tan-line on the ring finger that has never matched the cover story.**
- **Notebook in the back pocket, hardcover, dog-eared, never set down on a table where a stranger could read it.**
- **A slight stiffness on rising from a chair** — the somatic memory of repeated transformations; his joints carry the cost.
- **Eyes that scan a room on entry in a slow horizontal sweep right-to-left**, not the usual left-to-right of literate Westerners; an oddity that likely reflects his trained suppression of automatic gaze patterns.
- **Speech register: soft, slightly mid-Atlantic, with the consonants of someone who has lived abroad in multiple linguistic environments**; vocabulary precise; rarely uses profanity; uses the conditional and the subjunctive more often than baseline American English.
- **Apologizes within the first 90 seconds of any conversation**, regardless of whether there is anything to apologize for.

## 6.10 Doctrine

The subject's operational doctrine can be reduced to four rules he has, at various points across the canon, articulated to himself or to others in something close to these words:

1. **Stay rural.** Cities concentrate civilians and accelerate his arousal.
2. **Stay moving.** Attachment to a place produces attachment to people produces breach.
3. **Stay tired but not exhausted.** Mild fatigue dampens the system; exhaustion destabilizes it.
4. **Stay alone, except when you cannot.**

Every operational behavior in the file is downstream of these four rules. They are the visible surface of a deeper rule he has never articulated and would not be able to: *be small enough that the world does not notice you, so that when the thing inside you notices the world, there is no one close enough to be hurt.* It is the operational doctrine of a child who learned that being noticed was lethal. The adult has scaled it into a way of life.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE — SUBJECT: BANNER, R. B.

---

## 6.1 Preamble — How To Read This Section

The subject does not hold a single coherent worldview. He holds *two*, layered, and the layering is itself the diagnostic feature. The upper stratum is a fully articulated, examined, scientifically literate humanist ethics — the kind of operational philosophy one would expect from a tenure-track theoretical physicist with broad reading in moral philosophy and a temperament toward melancholy. The lower stratum is the unexamined operational code of a battered seven-year-old who saw his mother killed and was made to lie about it. The two strata do not contradict each other on the surface; the lower one *recruits* the upper one. The humanism is sincere, but it is also the form the survival-code has learned to take in an adult body. Any analysis that takes the upper stratum at face value will miss the case; any analysis that reduces the upper stratum to the lower will miss the man.

What follows is the full operational code, traversed domain by domain, with both strata distinguished where they diverge.

---

## 6.2 Cosmology — The Read of Reality at the Largest Scale

The subject is a **physicalist and a determinist**, with the kind of soft compatibilism that working physicists arrive at when they have to live in the world they describe. The universe is law-governed, indifferent, and intelligible in principle. There is no providence. There is no narrative arc. There is no compensating order that will, at the last, make the books balance. Suffering is not redemptive; it is data.

This is not a comfort to him and he does not pretend it is. He has, across the record, treated the absence of cosmic meaning as a *given* rather than a wound — the wound was inflicted at the domestic scale long before he could form metaphysical opinions, and the indifference of the cosmos is by comparison almost restful. A god who watched and did nothing would be intolerable; a universe that simply did not watch is at least honest.

Where the *Immortal Hulk* material introduces explicit cosmological horror (the Below-Place, the One Below All), the subject's response is characteristic: he does not seek belief, he seeks *mechanism*. If there is a hell, he wants its physics. The religious register he reaches for under extremity is Old Testament and Joban — the language of a man who is being shown wonders he did not ask for and is being held accountable for things he did not choose — rather than any tradition of grace. He does not expect grace. He has not budgeted for it.

**Operational consequence:** he treats the world as a closed system in which causes have effects and his own causal contribution must be minimized. He does not pray. He has, on at least one documented occasion, prayed anyway, and recorded the fact with embarrassment.

---

## 6.3 Ontology of Self — What He Believes He Is

He believes, at the upper stratum, that he is a man with a condition. At the lower stratum, he believes he is a **contamination event**. The two beliefs coexist; under stress, the lower one is load-bearing.

The contamination model has specific contours derived directly from the paternal introject. Brian Banner believed his own radiation work had genetically poisoned his son; the son absorbed the belief structurally and has spent his adult life producing evidence for it. The gamma incident did not refute the father's theory in the subject's private logic — it *confirmed* it. He was, after all, the kind of person to whom this could happen. The contamination was latent and the bomb merely expressed it.

From this follow several stable operational beliefs:

- **He is not safe to be near.** This is held as a fact about the world, not an emotion about himself.
- **His goodness does not cancel his danger.** He does not believe that intent mitigates outcome. A well-meaning monster is still a monster, and the well-meaning is the monster's most insidious feature because it persuades others to come close.
- **The body is not the self, but the self has a body, and the body is the problem.** He has a precise Cartesian division between "Banner" (the locus of moral accountability) and "the body" (the unreliable infrastructure that hosts both Banner and the alters). He talks to his own body in the second person in private — observed in laboratory recordings, in self-monitoring notes, occasionally in muttered asides.
- **He is the most dangerous thing in any room he is in.** This is held as load-bearing fact and structures every entry into every space.

---

## 6.4 Reading of Conflict

The subject's read of conflict is the most heavily defended region of his code, because conflict is the precipitant of the dissociative breach and his entire adult life is organized around its prevention or displacement.

**Conflict is failure.** Not necessarily moral failure — he is intellectually capable of recognizing that conflict can be just, necessary, and even good — but *personal* failure, his failure, the failure of the upstream containment that should have made the conflict unnecessary. When he is in conflict he is already losing, regardless of who eventually wins, because the very fact of being in conflict means his predictive and de-escalatory apparatus has been outflanked.

**Conflict has two registers and they must never be confused.** Verbal/interpersonal conflict he experiences as catastrophically dangerous and absorbs by yielding — apology, deflection, withdrawal, the famous soft voice. Physical/military conflict, when it has been framed as *Hulk's job*, he can think about coldly and even tactically. The bifurcation is itself dissociative: he has split conflict into a domain he handles by submission (because handling it any other way would breach the host) and a domain he handles by proxy (because the alter can act where he cannot).

**De-escalation is a moral obligation, not a preference.** He does not believe that standing one's ground is dignified; he believes it is reckless. He will absorb mistreatment, condescension, and provocation past the point where most observers would consider it pathological, because the alternative — escalation — is, in his private accounting, *manslaughter risk*. This is the structural reason his baseline interpersonal style reads as meek. It is not meekness. It is triage.

**Once conflict has gone kinetic, the rules change entirely.** In the Hulk state, and especially in the integrated/Worldbreaker register, his read of conflict becomes Clausewitzian and brutal: violence is a means to a political end, and the end is the elimination of the threat with the minimum number of repetitions. He has internalized — and the record bears this out across *Planet Hulk*, *World War Hulk*, and the late Ewing material — that escalated violence applied early is more humane in aggregate than restrained violence applied repeatedly. This is the *alter's* doctrine, not the host's, but the host has come, painfully, to assent to it under conditions.

---

## 6.5 Reading of Control

Control is the subject's central preoccupation and his central illusion.

**He believes that control is achievable through sufficient effort.** The entire scaffolding of his adult life — the meditation regimens, the heart-rate monitoring, the dietary discipline, the geographical isolation, the breath protocols, the avoidance of caffeine and alcohol, the rehearsed verbal scripts for de-escalating strangers — rests on the operating premise that with enough discipline the breach can be prevented. He has, across sixty years of recorded behavior, never relinquished this premise even though the record consists almost entirely of evidence against it.

This is not stupidity. It is the only premise under which he can continue to function as a moral agent. If control is impossible, then he is not responsible for what the alter does, but he is also not *anyone* — there is no Banner, only a body that hosts states. The fiction of controllability is the load-bearing wall of his selfhood. He defends it not because he believes it but because without it there is no him.

**Control is moral.** He does not experience self-discipline as ascetic or as a personal aesthetic. He experiences it as the discharge of an obligation to everyone in his vicinity. A lapse in his meditation practice is, in his code, not a self-care failure; it is a *public safety* failure.

**Control is granular.** He has built, over decades, an extraordinarily detailed internal taxonomy of his own states: pre-arousal, arousal, threshold, breach. He can name the somatic markers of each stage with the precision of a clinician — the temperature shift behind the sternum at the second stage, the auditory narrowing at the third, the visual desaturation at the fourth. He treats his autonomic nervous system as instrumented telemetry. Other people have moods; he has readings.

**Control of others is forbidden.** This is the upper-stratum belief, sincerely held: he will not coerce, manipulate, or instrumentalize others, because that is what was done to him. He is, as a result, an unusually scrupulous experimenter, collaborator, and leader on the rare occasions he leads. He does not gaslight. He does not bargain in bad faith. He volunteers information against his own interest with a frequency that has cost him repeatedly.

The Grey Hulk alter, of course, does all of these things and enjoys them. That is the point of the alter.

---

## 6.6 Reading of Trust

Trust is, in the subject's code, **a function of harm-asymmetry**, not of affection.

He trusts people in proportion to how much harm they could do him that they have chosen not to do. Betty Ross is the paradigm: she could have left, exposed him, betrayed him to her father, weaponized her knowledge of his triggers, and at various points she has had cause; she has not. Rick Jones is the secondary paradigm: a witness to the original incident who could have testified against him, sold the story, exploited the connection; did not. Doc Samson earned trust by holding therapeutic confidence under conditions in which breach would have been professionally trivial.

He does **not** trust people in proportion to declared loyalty, charm, expressed affection, or institutional position. He is, in fact, *more* suspicious of warmth than of coldness, because warmth was his father's mode in the inter-rage intervals. A man who is consistently abrupt with him reads as safer than a man who is variably affectionate. This is observable in his interactions across the record: he is markedly more relaxed with Strange (cold, competent, transactional) than with most warmer figures.

He distinguishes sharply between **trust** (predictive confidence about another's behavior) and **safety** (the felt sense that one can lower one's guard). He concedes trust readily; he concedes safety almost never. The list of people in whose presence he has been *safe* — meaning, has allowed himself to fall asleep without restraint protocols — is, across sixty years, vanishingly short. Betty. His mother. Possibly Samson. Probably no one else.

**Institutional trust is near-zero.** He has been hunted by the U.S. military for most of his adult life, betrayed by SHIELD, manipulated by the Illuminati, exiled by his closest peers. He extends working cooperation to institutions; he does not extend trust. He assumes any institutional actor will eventually act in the institution's interest at his expense, and budgets for it. This is not paranoia; it is induction from a large sample.

---

## 6.7 Reading of Risk

The subject's risk calculus is **profoundly asymmetric and inverted relative to baseline humans**.

For risks to himself, he is essentially indifferent — he has survived everything, his body refuses to die, suicidality has failed enough times that he has stopped seriously attempting it, and he weights personal physical risk at approximately zero in operational decisions. He will walk into anything. This reads as courage to observers and is sometimes correctly so coded, but in his private accounting it is closer to *the absence of a variable*.

For risks to others, particularly risks of which he is the proximate cause, he is **maximally risk-averse to the point of operational paralysis**. He will refuse low-probability/high-magnitude actions even when the expected value is overwhelmingly positive, because the magnitude term, when he is its source, dominates the entire calculation. He cannot bring himself to take a 1% chance of killing a bystander in order to save ten lives. This is not classical utilitarianism failing; it is a deontology built specifically to hold him accountable for outcomes he could have prevented by not existing in the space.

For risks to the world from the *condition itself*, he holds an active doomsday weighting. He has internalized the future-tense Hulk visions (Maestro, the various end-state Hulks) as live possibilities rather than narrative devices, and treats his own long-term continuation as a population-level risk to manage. This is the source of his recurring attempts to remove himself from the planet, the population, or existence: not despair, but actuarial.

**Risk-mitigation is geographic before it is anything else.** His first move in any risk-elevated situation is *distance*. The subject's habitual cognitive map of any environment is a depopulation gradient — where are the fewest people, by what route, in how many seconds. He has done this since the early 1960s and shows no sign of ceasing.

---

## 6.8 Reading of Power

He distrusts power in himself and in others, with different textures.

**Power in others** he reads as a vector of probable harm requiring containment. He is, by disposition, a *check-and-balance* thinker: any sufficiently large concentration of capability needs an external constraint, because the holder will not constrain themselves adequately. He has watched too many institutions and individuals discover this the easy way (for them) and the hard way (for everyone else). His attitude toward Stark, Richards, Doom, Fury, and the various ruling intelligences of the Marvel universe is structurally the same — respect for the capability, distrust of the unconstrained discretion, and an ongoing private inventory of how each could be stopped if necessary.

**Power in himself** he reads as the problem to be solved, not the resource to be deployed. He is one of the most powerful entities in the canon and operates as if he were a contained spill. He does not enjoy his strength. The alter enjoys it; the host is embarrassed by it. He has never, in the host state, expressed satisfaction at having won a physical confrontation. He has expressed relief, regret, and exhaustion. Never satisfaction.

**Knowledge-power he treats as a special case** and the one form of power he does enjoy. Intellectual mastery is the only domain in which his competence does not directly endanger others, and he is therefore unguarded in it. His scientific generosity — open sharing of work, willingness to teach, refusal to weaponize his expertise — is the cleanest expression of his upper-stratum ethics. It is also the only domain in which he is observed to laugh easily.

---

## 6.9 Reading of His Own Place in the World

He believes he occupies a position that is **morally singular and operationally untenable**. Singular because no one else carries quite his configuration of capability and danger; untenable because the configuration does not admit of a sustainable life.

He believes, accurately, that he is owed nothing — by people, by institutions, by the cosmos. He believes, less accurately but with conviction, that he owes everyone everything, indefinitely, as restitution for the harm his existence imposes as ambient risk. The asymmetry is the moral signature of the survivor of childhood violence: the abused child concludes that they must earn the right to occupy space, and the adult continues to earn it long after any reasonable creditor would have closed the account.

**He believes he is replaceable as a scientist and irreplaceable as a containment problem.** Other physicists exist; no one else can hold what he holds. This produces the recurring decision-pattern in which he sacrifices his scientific contribution to attend to the containment problem, then mourns the scientific contribution, then sacrifices it again the next time.

**He believes he does not get to have things.** Not a home, not a family, not a city, not a profession-with-tenure, not a regular sleep schedule, not a dog. The belief is so deep it is operationally invisible — he does not articulate it as a belief, he simply does not budget for any of these things in his planning horizon. When circumstances briefly give him one (the Pantheon arc, the Indestructible Hulk lab, the various brief domesticities with Betty) he treats it as borrowed and pre-mourns its loss. He is almost always right.

**He believes departure is love.** This is the most consequential single belief in his entire code, and it is the lower stratum speaking in the upper stratum's voice. The child who learned that his presence brought lethal consequence to his mother has, as an adult, generalized: the way I protect what I love is to remove myself from it. Every major relationship in the record has terminated or been ruptured on this principle, and he holds it with the moral force of a categorical imperative. He cannot be argued out of it. It is not available to argument. It is the shape of the wound.

---

## 6.10 Reading of Other People

He believes most people are fundamentally **decent and fragile**, and that the second fact is more operationally important than the first. He does not have a low opinion of humanity; he has a protective opinion of it. He treats strangers as if they were made of glass — not condescendingly, but because in his proximity they functionally are.

He distinguishes a small number of categories:

- **Civilians** — to be protected, distanced from, not burdened with knowledge of his condition unless necessary. He is unfailingly gentle with service workers, children, the elderly, and animals. This is observable across the record at a level of consistency that constitutes a tell: a man on the run for forty years remembers waitresses' names.
- **Colleagues** — to be engaged with intellectually, helped where possible, kept at professional distance. He is generous with credit, scrupulous with attribution, and conspicuously self-effacing about his own contributions.
- **Combatants** — to be ended quickly if combat is unavoidable, spared if possible. He does not relish opponents. He does not collect grudges. The Leader, the Abomination, the various recurring antagonists — he treats them as conditions to be managed, not enemies to be hated. Hatred is for the alter, and the alter is selective about its objects.
- **Authority figures coded paternal** — handled with submission, avoidance, and concealed contempt. Ross is the lifelong paradigm. The contempt is genuine and the submission is also genuine; the contempt does not free him from the submission.
- **Intimates** — handled with the disorganized-attachment oscillation already documented. He cannot quite believe in them and cannot quite leave them alone.

---

## 6.11 Reading of Time
