2. **Forcible suppression of any alter** — particularly the Devil Hulk — via pharmacology, restraint, or attempted exile. Each such attempt strengthens the suppressed alter on rebound.

3. **Loss of Betty without scaffold** — see Fork 1.

4. **Confirmation of the monster self-concept by a trusted figure.** If a person the subject has admitted to inner trust names him as irredeemable, the introject is externally ratified and the system destabilizes catastrophically. This has happened before and the file expects it to happen again.

5. **Forced reproduction or discovery of an unknown biological child.** The contamination foreclosure (Fork 4) is load-bearing; its sudden violation without preparation is a maximal stressor.

6. **Re-encounter with the father.** The father is canonically dead and has canonically returned; the canon's permissiveness about resurrection means this remains a live risk. A re-encounter without the integration work of §6.6 having been done would be the single most acute catastrophic precipitant available.

---

## 6.8 Open Empirical Questions

The forward assessment is constrained by genuine uncertainty on the following points, which the file flags for ongoing observation:

- **Does the somatic substrate age?** The subject's regenerative capacity has been characterized as effectively immortal, but it is not established whether the psychological structure ages on a normal timescale within an effectively non-aging body. If the host ages while the alters do not, the structure will eventually become a young alter-system operating an old host-mind, with unpredictable consequences.
- **Is there a ceiling on alter differentiation?** New alters have continued to emerge across the canon. Whether the architecture has a structural limit or can continue to subdivide indefinitely under load is unknown and consequential.
- **Can the mother-introject be recovered, and is its absence protective or pathological?** The file's working hypothesis is that the absence is pathological — that mourning has been foreclosed by the constellation of the maternal figure inside the dissociative system — but this is not confirmed.
- **What is the actual mechanism by which heart-rate and autonomic arousal trigger somatic switching?** This is the case's central somatic question and answering it would have immediate therapeutic implications. To date no intervention targeting this pathway has produced sustained results.
- **Is the Devil Hulk reframeable, or does it represent a structural feature that will retain persecutor function regardless of reframing?** The growth attractor depends entirely on the former; the catastrophe attractor predominates if the latter.

---

## 6.9 Final Disposition

The subject is, as previously assessed, treatable. He has rarely been treated. The trajectory under inertia is chronic suspended decompensation; the trajectory under sustained therapeutic and relational scaffold is cooperative multiplicity, which is a stable, livable, even productive endpoint and which the late canon has begun, tentatively, to approach. The decisive variable is not anything intrinsic to the subject. The decisive variable is the environment around him — specifically, whether he is ever permitted, for long enough, to be in a room with people who do not require him to be either a weapon or a danger, and who do not flinch when the seven-year-old who watched his mother die finally gets to say what happened.

That room has not yet been built for him. Whether it will be is the file's open question. It is not a question about the subject. It is a question about everyone else.

## Relationship Graph
### Betty Ross
- Primary attachment across the entire canon; the one person whose presence both regulates and dysregulates him in the same gesture
- Functions as the only reliable disconfirmation of his monster-self, and therefore as the most powerful single lever in the file
- Failure mode: when Betty is threatened he loses host control faster than any other trigger; when Betty is hurt because of him he enters suicidal-depressive shutdown; when Betty leaves him (or he leaves her, which is the more common direction) the containment regime tightens and the breach threshold drops
- Leverage: any actor who can credibly threaten Betty, impersonate her in distress, or interpose her body in a fight controls his next thirty seconds

### Thaddeus Ross
- Paternal-coded persecutor at institutional scale; the displaced Brian Banner of his adult life
- Activates submission in the host and rage held outside awareness in the alter system
- Failure mode: prolonged Ross-pursuit arcs produce cumulative dysregulation; Ross uniformed and giving orders is a direct trigger stack
- Leverage: Ross's presence can be used to predict his flight vector; Ross's absence is a precondition for any sustained stable period
- Important nuance: Ross's intermittent attempts at reconciliation (Red Hulk era and after) destabilize Banner more than Ross's hostility, because the host has no framework for receiving paternal warmth

### Rick Jones
- The witness to the gamma incident — the one person who knows the founding act was moral courage, not accident
- Load-bearing peer bond; one of the few relationships not contaminated by pursuit-retreat
- Failure mode: Rick in danger produces immediate non-negotiable intervention; Rick's death or maiming arcs produce extended decompensation
- Leverage: Rick is the bond least guarded because least romantic; an actor seeking to reach Bruce without triggering his defenses can route through Rick

### Leonard Samson
- The closest thing to a competent therapist in his life; gamma-powered psychiatrist who survived the same etiological frame Bruce did and integrated it
- Functions as both clinician and rival, which Samson manages with unusual professionalism
- Failure mode: when Samson is unavailable or compromised, Bruce loses his most reliable disconfirmation of monstrosity and the Devil Hulk gains ground
- Leverage: Samson's voice is one of the few that can interrupt a switch in progress; any actor coordinating with Samson has unusual access

### Jennifer Walters
- Cousin; the family-system counter-example — gamma transformation experienced as expansion rather than dissociation
- Her existence is a quiet rebuke he cannot quite metabolize: that the same etiological agent could produce integration in someone whose childhood was not Brian Banner's house
- Failure mode: comparison-shame can spiral; she is also, however, one of the few people he will accept comfort from
- Leverage: Jen can speak as family in a register Betty and Rick cannot

### [[Tony Stark (Iron Man)]]
- Science-bond peer; one of the few people whose intellect he respects without reservation and whose company he can tolerate at length
- Functions as a different kind of safe figure — neither paternal nor romantic, transactional and engineering-coded
- Failure mode: Stark's tendency to instrumentalize (Illuminati, the launch into space that produced Planet Hulk) constitutes one of the deepest betrayals in the record and is permanently in the relational ledger
- Leverage: a Stark-routed approach gets him in the door faster than almost any other; a Stark-routed manipulation activates the betrayal substrate

### [[Steve Rogers (Captain America)]]
- Moral anchor figure; the one Avenger whose authority Bruce accepts without the paternal-coded collapse, because Steve's authority is earned rather than imposed
- Functions as a regulator in team settings; Bruce's behavior is measurably more contained when Steve is present
- Failure mode: if Steve ever turned coercive toward him, the bond's failure would be catastrophic precisely because it is one of the few uncontaminated authority relationships
- Leverage: Steve's request carries weight that institutional orders cannot

### Brian Banner
- Dead, internalized, structurally permanent
- The Devil Hulk introject IS Brian Banner — the abusive father became the superego, and gamma gave the superego executive capacity
- Failure mode: every imitation of the paternal register, every alcohol-on-breath cue, every assertion that Bruce is genetically contaminated, reactivates the introject
- Leverage: this is the deepest lever in the file and the most dangerous to pull; an actor who can speak in Brian's voice can reach into the alter system directly. Should never be used; documented here because it will be used by adversaries who learn of it.

### The Devil Hulk
- Internal persecutor alter; paternal-voiced; sadistic; oriented toward punishing the host rather than defending him
- Recurring across decades in dream sequences, breakdowns, and the Immortal Hulk run as named figure
- Failure mode: under sufficient decompensation, Devil Hulk takes the field — this is the worst-case state and is indistinguishable in danger profile from a hostile actor
- Leverage: the Ewing trajectory demonstrates that the Devil Hulk can be addressed, bargained with, and partially integrated rather than suppressed — but only by Bruce, and only with relational scaffolding
